| * [v](/wiki/Template:TopicTOC-World_War_II "Template:TopicTOC-World War II") _[t](/wiki/Template_talk:TopicTOC-World_War_II "Template talk:TopicTOC-World War II")_ [e](/wiki/Special:EditPage/Template:TopicTOC-World_War_II "Special:EditPage/Template:TopicTOC-World War II") |

**World War II**\[[b]\](#cite_note-2 "#cite_note-2") or the **Second World War** (1 September 1939 – 2 September 1945) was a [global conflict](/wiki/World_war "World war") between two coalitions: the [Allies](/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II "Allies of World War II") and the [Axis powers](/wiki/Axis_powers "Axis powers"). [Nearly all of the world's countries](/wiki/World_War_II_by_country "World War II by country") participated, with many nations mobilising all resources in pursuit of [total war](/wiki/Total_war "Total war"). [Tanks](/wiki/Tanks_in_World_War_II "Tanks in World War II") and [aircraft played major roles](/wiki/Air_warfare_of_World_War_II "Air warfare of World War II"), enabling the [strategic bombing](/wiki/Strategic_bombing "Strategic bombing") of cities and delivery of the [first and only nuclear weapons](/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki "Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki") ever used in war. World War II is the [deadliest conflict](/wiki/List_of_wars_by_death_toll "List of wars by death toll") in history, causing [the death of 70 to 85 million people](/wiki/World_War_II_casualties "World War II casualties"), more than half of whom were civilians. Millions died in [genocides](/wiki/Genocide "Genocide"), including [the Holocaust](/wiki/The_Holocaust "The Holocaust"), and by massacres, starvation, and disease. After the Allied victory, [Germany](/wiki/Allied-occupied_Germany "Allied-occupied Germany"), [Austria](/wiki/Allied-occupied_Austria "Allied-occupied Austria"), [Japan](/wiki/Occupation_of_Japan "Occupation of Japan"), and [Korea](/wiki/Division_of_Korea#Post%E2%80%93World_War_II "Division of Korea") were occupied, and German and Japanese leaders were tried for [war crimes](/wiki/War_crime "War crime").

The [causes of World War II](/wiki/Causes_of_World_War_II "Causes of World War II") included unresolved tensions in the [aftermath of World War I](/wiki/Aftermath_of_World_War_I "Aftermath of World War I") and the rise of [fascism in Europe](/wiki/Fascism_in_Europe "Fascism in Europe") and [militarism in Japan](/wiki/Japanese_militarism "Japanese militarism"). Key events preceding the war included [Japan's invasion of Manchuria](/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_Manchuria "Japanese invasion of Manchuria") in 1931, the [Spanish Civil War](/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War "Spanish Civil War"), the outbreak of the [Second Sino-Japanese War](/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War "Second Sino-Japanese War") in 1937, and Germany's [annexations of Austria](/wiki/Anschluss "Anschluss") and [the Sudetenland](/wiki/Munich_Agreement "Munich Agreement"). World War II is generally considered to have begun on 1 September 1939, when [Nazi Germany](/wiki/Nazi_Germany "Nazi Germany"), under [Adolf Hitler](/wiki/Adolf_Hitler "Adolf Hitler"), [invaded Poland](/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland "Invasion of Poland"), after which the [United Kingdom](</wiki/United_Kingdom_declaration_of_war_on_Germany_(1939)> "United Kingdom declaration of war on Germany (1939)") and [France declared war](</wiki/French_declaration_of_war_on_Germany_(1939)> "French declaration of war on Germany (1939)") on Germany. Poland was divided between Germany and the [Soviet Union](/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union") under the [Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact](/wiki/Molotov%E2%80%93Ribbentrop_Pact "Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact"). In 1940, the Soviet Union [annexed the Baltic states](/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Baltic_states "Occupation of the Baltic states") and [parts of Finland](/wiki/Winter_War "Winter War") and [Romania](/wiki/Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina "Soviet occupation of Bessarabia and Northern Bukovina"). After the [fall of France](/wiki/Battle_of_France "Battle of France") in June 1940, the war continued mainly between Germany and the [British Empire](/wiki/British_Empire "British Empire"), with [fighting in the Balkans](</wiki/Balkans_campaign_(World_War_II)> "Balkans campaign (World War II)"), [Mediterranean, and Middle East](/wiki/Mediterranean_and_Middle_East_theatre_of_World_War_II "Mediterranean and Middle East theatre of World War II"), the aerial [Battle of Britain](/wiki/Battle_of_Britain "Battle of Britain") and [the Blitz](/wiki/The_Blitz "The Blitz"), and the naval [Battle of the Atlantic](/wiki/Battle_of_the_Atlantic "Battle of the Atlantic"). Through campaigns and treaties, Germany gained control of much of [continental Europe](/wiki/Continental_Europe "Continental Europe") and [formed the Axis alliance](/wiki/Tripartite_Pact "Tripartite Pact") with [Italy](/wiki/Fascist_Italy "Fascist Italy"), [Japan](/wiki/Empire_of_Japan "Empire of Japan"), and other countries. In June 1941, Germany [invaded the Soviet Union](/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa "Operation Barbarossa"), opening the [Eastern Front](</wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)> "Eastern Front (World War II)") and initially making large territorial gains.

In December 1941, Japan attacked American and British territories [in Asia and the Pacific](/wiki/Pacific_War#Japanese_offensives,_1941%E2%80%931942 "Pacific War"), including at [Pearl Harbor in Hawaii](/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor "Attack on Pearl Harbor"), leading the United States to enter the war against Japan and Germany. Japan conquered much of coastal China and Southeast Asia, but its advances in the Pacific were halted in June 1942 at the [Battle of Midway](/wiki/Battle_of_Midway "Battle of Midway"). In early 1943, Axis forces were defeated [in North Africa](/wiki/North_African_campaign "North African campaign") and [at Stalingrad](/wiki/Battle_of_Stalingrad "Battle of Stalingrad") in the Soviet Union, and that year their continued defeats on the Eastern Front, an [Allied invasion of Italy](/wiki/Allied_invasion_of_Italy "Allied invasion of Italy"), and Allied offensives in the Pacific forced them into retreat on all fronts. In 1944, the Western Allies [invaded France at Normandy](/wiki/Normandy_landings "Normandy landings") as the Soviet Union [recaptured its pre-war territory](/wiki/Stalin%27s_ten_blows "Stalin's ten blows") and the US crippled Japan's navy and [captured key Pacific islands](</wiki/Leapfrogging_(strategy)> "Leapfrogging (strategy)"). The war in Europe concluded with the liberation of [German-occupied territories](/wiki/German-occupied_Europe "German-occupied Europe"); [invasions of Germany by the Western Allies](/wiki/Western_Allied_invasion_of_Germany "Western Allied invasion of Germany") and the Soviet Union, which culminated in the [fall of Berlin](/wiki/Battle_of_Berlin "Battle of Berlin") to Soviet troops; and [Germany's unconditional surrender](/wiki/German_Instrument_of_Surrender "German Instrument of Surrender") on [8 May 1945](/wiki/Victory_in_Europe_Day "Victory in Europe Day"). On 6 and 9 August, the US [dropped atomic bombs](/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki "Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki") on [Hiroshima](/wiki/Hiroshima "Hiroshima") and [Nagasaki](/wiki/Nagasaki "Nagasaki") in Japan. Faced with an [imminent Allied invasion](/wiki/Operation_Downfall "Operation Downfall"), the prospect of further atomic bombings, and a [Soviet declaration of war](/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Japanese_War "Soviet–Japanese War") and [invasion of Manchuria](/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Manchuria "Soviet invasion of Manchuria"), Japan announced [its unconditional surrender](/wiki/Surrender_of_Japan "Surrender of Japan") on 15 August, and signed [a surrender document](/wiki/Japanese_Instrument_of_Surrender "Japanese Instrument of Surrender") on [2 September 1945](/wiki/Victory_over_Japan_Day "Victory over Japan Day").

World War II transformed the political, economic, and social structures of the world, and established the foundation of international relations for the rest of the 20th century and into the 21st century. The [United Nations](/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations") was created to foster international cooperation and prevent future conflicts, with the victorious great powers—China, France, the Soviet Union, the UK, and the US—becoming [the permanent members](/wiki/Permanent_members_of_the_United_Nations_Security_Council "Permanent members of the United Nations Security Council") of [its security council](/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council "United Nations Security Council"). The Soviet Union and the US emerged as rival [superpowers](/wiki/Superpower "Superpower"), setting the stage for the half-century [Cold War](/wiki/Cold_War "Cold War"). In the wake of Europe's devastation, the influence of its great powers waned, triggering the [decolonisation of Africa](/wiki/Decolonisation_of_Africa "Decolonisation of Africa") and [of Asia](/wiki/Decolonisation_of_Asia "Decolonisation of Asia"). Many countries whose industries had been damaged moved towards [economic recovery and expansion](/wiki/Post%E2%80%93World_War_II_economic_expansion "Post–World War II economic expansion").

## Start and end dates

| * [v](/wiki/Template:WWII_timelines "Template:WWII timelines") _[t](/wiki/Template_talk:WWII_timelines "Template talk:WWII timelines")_ [e](/wiki/Special:EditPage/Template:WWII_timelines "Special:EditPage/Template:WWII timelines") |

Most historians date the beginning of World War II to the [German invasion of Poland](/wiki/German_invasion_of_Poland "German invasion of Poland") on 1 September 1939\[[1]\](#cite\*note-FOOTNOTEWeinberg20056-3 "#cite\*note-FOOTNOTEWeinberg20056-3")\[[2]\](#cite_note-4 "#cite_note-4") and the [United Kingdom](</wiki/United_Kingdom_declaration_of_war_on_Germany*(1939)> "United Kingdom declaration of war on Germany (1939)") and [France](</wiki/French_declaration_of_war_on_Germany*(1939)> "French declaration of war on Germany (1939)")'s declaration of war on Germany two days later. Dates for the beginning of the [Pacific War](/wiki/Pacific_War "Pacific War") include the start of the [Second Sino-Japanese War](/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War "Second Sino-Japanese War") on 7 July 1937,\[[3]\](#cite_note-5 "#cite_note-5")\[[4]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFörsterGessler200564-6 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFörsterGessler200564-6") or the earlier [Japanese invasion of Manchuria](/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_Manchuria "Japanese invasion of Manchuria"), on 19 September 1931.\[[5]\](#cite_note-7 "#cite_note-7")\[[6]\](#cite_note-8 "#cite_note-8") Others follow the British historian [A. J. P. Taylor](/wiki/A._J._P._Taylor "A. J. P. Taylor"), who stated that the Sino-Japanese War and war in Europe and its colonies occurred simultaneously, and the two wars became World War II in 1941.\[[7]\](#cite_note-9 "#cite_note-9") Other proposed starting dates for World War II include the [Italian invasion of Abyssinia](/wiki/Second_Italo-Ethiopian_War "Second Italo-Ethiopian War") on 3 October 1935.\[[8]\](#cite_note-10 "#cite_note-10") The British historian [Antony Beevor](/wiki/Antony_Beevor "Antony Beevor") views the beginning of World War II as the [Battles of Khalkhin Gol](/wiki/Battles_of_Khalkhin_Gol "Battles of Khalkhin Gol") fought between [Japan](/wiki/Empire_of_Japan "Empire of Japan") and the forces of [Mongolia](/wiki/Mongolian_People%27s_Republic "Mongolian People's Republic") and the [Soviet Union](/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union") from May to September 1939.\[[9]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor201210-11 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor201210-11") Others view the [Spanish Civil War](/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War "Spanish Civil War") as the start or prelude to World War II.\[[10]\](#cite_note-12 "#cite_note-12")\[[11]\](#cite_note-13 "#cite_note-13")

The exact date of the war's end also is not universally agreed upon. It was generally accepted at the time that the war ended with the armistice of 15 August 1945 ([V-J Day](/wiki/Victory_over_Japan_Day "Victory over Japan Day")), rather than with the formal [surrender of Japan](/wiki/Surrender_of_Japan "Surrender of Japan") on 2 September 1945, which officially [ended the war in Asia](/wiki/End_of_World_War_II_in_Asia "End of World War II in Asia"). A [peace treaty between Japan and the Allies](/wiki/Treaty_of_San_Francisco "Treaty of San Francisco") was signed in 1951.\[[12]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasaya19904-14 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasaya19904-14") A 1990 [treaty regarding Germany's future](/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Final_Settlement_with_Respect_to_Germany "Treaty on the Final Settlement with Respect to Germany") allowed the [reunification of East and West Germany](/wiki/German_reunification "German reunification") to take place.\[[13]\](#cite_note-15 "#cite_note-15") No formal peace treaty between Japan and the Soviet Union was ever signed,\[[14]\](#cite_note-16 "#cite_note-16") although the state of war between the two countries was terminated by the [Soviet–Japanese Joint Declaration of 1956](/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Japanese_Joint_Declaration_of_1956 "Soviet–Japanese Joint Declaration of 1956"), which also restored full diplomatic relations between them.\[[15]\](#cite_note-nyt-17 "#cite_note-nyt-17")

## Background

Main article: [Causes of World War II](/wiki/Causes_of_World_War_II "Causes of World War II")

### Aftermath of World War I

[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-09042%2C_Genf%2C_V%C3%B6lkerbund%2C_Sitzungssaal.jpg/250px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-09042%2C_Genf%2C_V%C3%B6lkerbund%2C_Sitzungssaal.jpg' alt='' title='' width='250' height='166' />](/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-09042,_Genf,_V%C3%B6lkerbund,_Sitzungssaal.jpg "/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-09042,_Genf,_V%C3%B6lkerbund,_Sitzungssaal.jpg")

The [League of Nations](/wiki/League_of_Nations "League of Nations") assembly, held in [Geneva](/wiki/Geneva "Geneva"), Switzerland (1930)

[World War I](/wiki/World_War_I "World War I") had radically altered the political European map with the defeat of the [Central Powers](/wiki/Central_Powers "Central Powers")—including [Austria-Hungary](/wiki/Austria-Hungary "Austria-Hungary"), [Germany](/wiki/German_Empire "German Empire"), [Bulgaria](/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bulgaria "Kingdom of Bulgaria"), and the [Ottoman Empire](/wiki/Ottoman_Empire "Ottoman Empire")—and the 1917 [Bolshevik seizure of power](/wiki/October_Revolution "October Revolution") in [Russia](/wiki/Russian_Republic "Russian Republic"), which led to the founding of the Soviet Union. Meanwhile, the victorious [Allies of World War I](/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I "Allies of World War I"), such as France, Belgium, Italy, Romania, and Greece, gained territory, and new [nation-states](/wiki/Nation_state "Nation state") were created out of the dissolution of the Austro-Hungarian, Ottoman, and Russian Empires.\[[16]\](#cite_note-18 "#cite_note-18")

To prevent a future world war, the [League of Nations](/wiki/League_of_Nations "League of Nations") was established in 1920 by the [Paris Peace Conference](</wiki/Paris_Peace_Conference_(1919%E2%80%931920)> "Paris Peace Conference (1919–1920)"). The organisation's primary goals were to prevent armed conflict through collective security, military, and [naval disarmament](/wiki/Washington_Naval_Treaty "Washington Naval Treaty"), as well as settling international disputes through peaceful negotiations and arbitration.\[[17]\](#cite_note-19 "#cite_note-19")

Despite strong pacifist sentiment [after World War I](/wiki/Aftermath_of_World_War_I "Aftermath of World War I"),\[[18]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIngram2006[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidbREQibN9i-sCpgPA76_76–78]-20 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIngram2006[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidbREQibN9i-sCpgPA76_76–78]-20") [irredentist](/wiki/Irredentism "Irredentism") and [revanchist](/wiki/Revanchism "Revanchism") [nationalism](/wiki/Nationalism "Nationalism") had emerged in several European states. These sentiments were especially marked in Germany because of the significant territorial, colonial, and financial losses imposed by the [Treaty of Versailles](/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles "Treaty of Versailles"). Under the treaty, Germany lost around 13 percent of its home territory and all [its overseas possessions](/wiki/German_colonial_empire "German colonial empire"), while German annexation of other states was prohibited, [reparations](/wiki/World_War_I_reparations "World War I reparations") were imposed, and limits were placed on the size and capability of the country's [armed forces](/wiki/Reichswehr "Reichswehr").\[[19]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKantowicz1999149-21 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKantowicz1999149-21")

### Germany and Italy

The German Empire was dissolved in the [German revolution of 1918–1919](/wiki/German_revolution_of_1918%E2%80%931919 "German revolution of 1918–1919"), and a democratic government, later known as the [Weimar Republic](/wiki/Weimar_Republic "Weimar Republic"), was created. The interwar period saw strife between supporters of the new republic and hardline opponents on both the political right and left. Italy, as an Entente ally, had made some post-war territorial gains; however, Italian nationalists were angered that the [promises made](</wiki/Treaty_of_London_(1915)> "Treaty of London (1915)") by the United Kingdom and France to secure Italian entrance into the war were not fulfilled in the peace settlement. From 1922 to 1925, the [Fascist](/wiki/Italian_fascism "Italian fascism") movement led by [Benito Mussolini](/wiki/Benito_Mussolini "Benito Mussolini") seized power in Italy with a nationalist, [totalitarian](/wiki/Totalitarianism "Totalitarianism"), and [class collaborationist](/wiki/Class_collaboration "Class collaboration") agenda that abolished representative democracy, repressed socialist, left-wing, and liberal forces, and pursued an aggressive expansionist foreign policy aimed at making Italy a world power, promising the creation of a "New Roman Empire".\[[20]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShaw200035-22 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShaw200035-22")

[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/N%C3%BCrnberg_Reichsparteitag_Hitler_retouched.jpg/250px-N%C3%BCrnberg_Reichsparteitag_Hitler_retouched.jpg' alt='' title='' width='190' height='317' />](/wiki/File:N%C3%BCrnberg_Reichsparteitag_Hitler_retouched.jpg "/wiki/File:N%C3%BCrnberg_Reichsparteitag_Hitler_retouched.jpg")

[Adolf Hitler](/wiki/Adolf_Hitler "Adolf Hitler") at a German [Nazi](/wiki/Nazism "Nazism") political rally in [Nuremberg](/wiki/Nuremberg "Nuremberg"), August 1933

[Adolf Hitler](/wiki/Adolf_Hitler "Adolf Hitler"), after an [unsuccessful attempt to overthrow the German government](/wiki/Beer_Hall_Putsch "Beer Hall Putsch") in 1923, eventually [became the chancellor of Germany](/wiki/Adolf_Hitler%27s_rise_to_power "Adolf Hitler's rise to power") in 1933 when President [Paul von Hindenburg](/wiki/Paul_von_Hindenburg "Paul von Hindenburg") and the Reichstag appointed him. Following Hindenburg's death in 1934, Hitler proclaimed himself _Führer_ of Germany and abolished democracy, espousing a [radical, racially motivated revision of the world order](</wiki/New_Order_(Nazism)> "New Order (Nazism)"), and soon began a massive [rearmament campaign](/wiki/German_rearmament "German rearmament").\[[21]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrody19994-23 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrody19994-23") France, seeking to secure its alliance with Italy, [allowed Italy a free hand in Ethiopia](/wiki/Franco-Italian_Agreement_of_1935 "Franco-Italian Agreement of 1935"), which Italy desired as a colonial possession. The situation was aggravated in early 1935 when the [Territory of the Saar Basin](/wiki/Territory_of_the_Saar_Basin "Territory of the Saar Basin") was legally reunited with Germany, and Hitler repudiated the Treaty of Versailles, accelerated his rearmament programme, and introduced conscription.\[[22]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZalampas198962-24 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZalampas198962-24")

### European treaties

The United Kingdom, France and Italy formed the [Stresa Front](/wiki/Stresa_Front "Stresa Front") in April 1935 in order to contain Germany, a key step towards [military globalisation](/wiki/Military_globalization "Military globalization"); however, that June, the United Kingdom made an [independent naval agreement](/wiki/Anglo-German_Naval_Agreement "Anglo-German Naval Agreement") with Germany, easing prior restrictions. The Soviet Union, concerned by Germany's [goals of capturing vast areas of Eastern Europe](/wiki/Drang_nach_Osten "Drang nach Osten"), drafted a treaty of mutual assistance with France. Before taking effect, though, the [Franco-Soviet pact](/wiki/Franco-Soviet_Treaty_of_Mutual_Assistance "Franco-Soviet Treaty of Mutual Assistance") was required to go through the bureaucracy of the League of Nations, which rendered it essentially toothless.\[[23]\](#cite_note-25 "#cite_note-25") The United States, concerned with events in Europe and Asia, passed the [Neutrality Act](/wiki/Neutrality_Acts_of_the_1930s "Neutrality Acts of the 1930s") in August of the same year.\[[24]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchmitz2000124-26 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchmitz2000124-26")

Hitler defied the Versailles and [Locarno Treaties](/wiki/Locarno_Treaties "Locarno Treaties") by [remilitarising the Rhineland](/wiki/Remilitarisation_of_the_Rhineland "Remilitarisation of the Rhineland") in March 1936, encountering little opposition due to the policy of [appeasement](/wiki/Appeasement "Appeasement").\[[25]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdamthwaite199252-27 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdamthwaite199252-27") In October 1936, Germany and Italy formed the [Rome–Berlin Axis](/wiki/Axis_powers "Axis powers"). A month later, Germany and Japan signed the [Anti-Comintern Pact](/wiki/Anti-Comintern_Pact "Anti-Comintern Pact"), which Italy joined the following year.\[[26]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer1990298–299-28 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer1990298–299-28")

### Asia

The [Kuomintang](/wiki/Kuomintang "Kuomintang") party in China launched a [unification campaign](/wiki/Northern_Expedition "Northern Expedition") against [regional warlords](/wiki/Warlord_Era "Warlord Era") and nominally unified China in the mid-1920s, but was soon embroiled in [a civil war](/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War "Chinese Civil War") against its former [Chinese Communist Party](/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Party "Chinese Communist Party") (CCP) allies\[[27]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPreston1998104-29 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPreston1998104-29") and [new regional warlords](/wiki/Central_Plains_War "Central Plains War"). In 1931, an [increasingly militaristic](/wiki/Statism_in_Sh%C5%8Dwa_Japan "Statism in Shōwa Japan") [Empire of Japan](/wiki/Empire_of_Japan "Empire of Japan"), which had long sought influence in China\[[28]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMyersPeattie1987458-30 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMyersPeattie1987458-30") as the first step of what its government saw as the country's [right to rule Asia](/wiki/Hakk%C5%8D_ichiu "Hakkō ichiu"), staged the [Mukden incident](/wiki/Mukden_incident "Mukden incident") as a pretext to [invade Manchuria](/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_Manchuria "Japanese invasion of Manchuria") and establish the [puppet state](/wiki/Puppet_state "Puppet state") of [Manchukuo](/wiki/Manchukuo "Manchukuo").\[[29]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmithSteadman200428-31 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmithSteadman200428-31")

China appealed to the [League of Nations](/wiki/League_of_Nations "League of Nations") to stop the Japanese invasion of Manchuria. Japan withdrew from the League of Nations after being [condemned](/wiki/Lytton_Report "Lytton Report") for its incursion into Manchuria. The two nations then fought several battles, in [Shanghai](/wiki/January_28_incident "January 28 incident"), [Rehe](/wiki/Battle_of_Rehe "Battle of Rehe"), and [Hebei](/wiki/Defense_of_the_Great_Wall "Defense of the Great Wall"), until the [Tanggu Truce](/wiki/Tanggu_Truce "Tanggu Truce") was signed in 1933. Thereafter, Chinese volunteer forces continued the resistance to Japanese aggression in [Manchuria](/wiki/Pacification_of_Manchukuo "Pacification of Manchukuo"), and [Chahar and Suiyuan](</wiki/Actions_in_Inner_Mongolia_(1933%E2%80%931936)> "Actions in Inner Mongolia (1933–1936)").\[[30]\](#cite_note-32 "#cite_note-32") After the 1936 [Xi'an Incident](/wiki/Xi%27an_Incident "Xi'an Incident"), the Kuomintang and CCP forces agreed on a ceasefire to present [a united front](/wiki/Second_United_Front "Second United Front") to oppose Japan.\[[31]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBusky200210-33 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBusky200210-33")

## Pre-war events

### Italian invasion of Ethiopia (1935)

Main article: [Second Italo-Ethiopian War](/wiki/Second_Italo-Ethiopian_War "Second Italo-Ethiopian War")
[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Mussolini_truppe_Etiopia.jpg/250px-Mussolini_truppe_Etiopia.jpg' alt='' title='' width='250' height='188' />](/wiki/File:Mussolini_truppe_Etiopia.jpg "/wiki/File:Mussolini_truppe_Etiopia.jpg")

[Benito Mussolini](/wiki/Benito_Mussolini "Benito Mussolini") inspecting troops during the [Italo-Ethiopian War](/wiki/Second_Italo-Ethiopian_War "Second Italo-Ethiopian War"), 1935

The [Second Italo-Ethiopian War](/wiki/Second_Italo-Ethiopian_War "Second Italo-Ethiopian War") was a brief [colonial war](/wiki/Colonial_war "Colonial war") that began in October 1935 and ended in May 1936. The war began with the invasion of the [Ethiopian Empire](/wiki/Ethiopian_Empire "Ethiopian Empire") (also known as [Abyssinia](/wiki/Etymology_of_Ethiopia "Etymology of Ethiopia")) by the armed forces of the [Kingdom of Italy](/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy "Kingdom of Italy") (_Regno d'Italia_), which was launched from [Italian Somaliland](/wiki/Italian_Somaliland "Italian Somaliland") and [Eritrea](/wiki/Italian_Eritrea "Italian Eritrea").\[[32]\](#cite*note-34 "#cite_note-34") The war resulted in the [military occupation](/wiki/Military_occupation "Military occupation") of Ethiopia and its [annexation](/wiki/Annexation "Annexation") into the newly created colony of [Italian East Africa](/wiki/Italian_East_Africa "Italian East Africa") (\_Africa Orientale Italiana*); in addition it exposed the weakness of the [League of Nations](/wiki/League_of_Nations "League of Nations") as a force to preserve peace. Both Italy and Ethiopia were member nations, [but the League did little](/wiki/Appeasement "Appeasement") when the former clearly violated Article X of the League's [Covenant](/wiki/Covenant_of_the_League_of_Nations "Covenant of the League of Nations").\[[33]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarker1971131–132-35 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarker1971131–132-35") The United Kingdom and France supported imposing sanctions on Italy for the invasion, but the sanctions were not fully enforced and failed to end the Italian invasion.\[[34]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer1990289-36 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer1990289-36") Italy subsequently dropped its objections to Germany's goal of absorbing [Austria](/wiki/Federal_State_of_Austria "Federal State of Austria").\[[35]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKitson2001231-37 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKitson2001231-37")

### Spanish Civil War (1936–1939)

Main article: [Spanish Civil War](/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War "Spanish Civil War")
When civil war broke out in Spain, Hitler and Mussolini lent military support to the [Nationalist rebels](</wiki/Nationalist_faction_(Spanish_Civil_War)> "Nationalist faction (Spanish Civil War)"), led by General [Francisco Franco](/wiki/Francisco_Franco "Francisco Franco"). Italy supported the Nationalists to a greater extent than the Nazis: Mussolini sent more than 70,000 ground troops, 6,000 aviation personnel, and 720 aircraft to Spain.\[[36]\](#cite\*note-FOOTNOTENeulen200025-38 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeulen200025-38") The Soviet Union supported the existing government of the [Spanish Republic](/wiki/Second_Spanish_Republic "Second Spanish Republic"). More than 30,000 foreign volunteers, known as the [International Brigades](/wiki/International_Brigades "International Brigades"), also fought against the Nationalists. Both Germany and the Soviet Union used this [proxy war](/wiki/Proxy_war "Proxy war") as an opportunity to test in combat their most advanced weapons and tactics. The Nationalists won the civil war in April 1939; Franco, now dictator, remained officially neutral during World War II but [generally favoured the Axis](/wiki/Spain_during_World_War_II "Spain during World War II").\[[37]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPayne2008271-39 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPayne2008271-39") His greatest collaboration with Germany was the sending of [volunteers](/wiki/Blue_Division "Blue Division") to fight on the [Eastern Front](</wiki/Eastern_Front*(World_War_II)> "Eastern Front (World War II)").\[[38]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPayne2008146-40 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPayne2008146-40")

### Japanese invasion of China (1937)

Main article: [Second Sino-Japanese War](/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War "Second Sino-Japanese War")
[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Shanghai1937IJA_ruins.jpg/250px-Shanghai1937IJA_ruins.jpg' alt='' title='' width='250' height='158' />](/wiki/File:Shanghai1937IJA_ruins.jpg "/wiki/File:Shanghai1937IJA_ruins.jpg")

[Imperial Japanese Army](/wiki/Imperial_Japanese_Army "Imperial Japanese Army") soldiers during the [Battle of Shanghai](/wiki/Battle_of_Shanghai "Battle of Shanghai"), 1937

# \<<\<<\<<< HEAD In July 1937, Japan captured the former Chinese imperial capital of [Peking](/wiki/Beijing "Beijing") after instigating the [Marco Polo Bridge incident](/wiki/Marco_Polo_Bridge_incident "Marco Polo Bridge incident"), which culminated in the Japanese campaign to invade all of China.\[[39]\](#cite\*note-FOOTNOTEEastman1986547–551-41 "#cite\*note-FOOTNOTEEastman1986547–551-41") The Soviets quickly signed a [non-aggression pact with China](/wiki/Sino-Soviet_Non-Aggression_Pact "Sino-Soviet Non-Aggression Pact") to lend [materiel](/wiki/Materiel "Materiel") support, effectively ending China's prior [cooperation with Germany](</wiki/China%E2%80%93Germany_relations*(1912%E2%80%931949)> "China–Germany relations (1912–1949)"). From September to November, the Japanese attacked [Taiyuan](/wiki/Battle_of_Taiyuan "Battle of Taiyuan"), engaged the [Kuomintang Army](/wiki/National_Revolutionary_Army "National Revolutionary Army") [around Xinkou](/wiki/Battle_of_Xinkou "Battle of Xinkou"),\[[40]\](#cite_note-Hsu\_&\_Chang_1971_221-42 "#cite_note-Hsu\*&\_Chang_1971_221-42") and fought [Communist forces](/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Party "Chinese Communist Party") [in Pingxingguan](/wiki/Battle_of_Pingxingguan "Battle of Pingxingguan").\[[41]\](#cite_note-Tucker2009-43 "#cite_note-Tucker2009-43")\[[42]\](#cite_note-yang-44 "#cite_note-yang-44") [Generalissimo](/wiki/Generalissimo "Generalissimo") [Chiang Kai-shek](/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek "Chiang Kai-shek") deployed his [best army](/wiki/List_of_German-trained_divisions_of_the_National_Revolutionary_Army "List of German-trained divisions of the National Revolutionary Army") to [defend Shanghai](/wiki/Battle_of_Shanghai "Battle of Shanghai"), but after three months of fighting, Shanghai fell. The Japanese continued to push Chinese forces back, [capturing the capital Nanking](/wiki/Battle_of_Nanking "Battle of Nanking") in December 1937. After the fall of Nanking, tens or hundreds of thousands of Chinese civilians and disarmed combatants were [murdered by the Japanese](/wiki/Nanjing_Massacre "Nanjing Massacre").\[[43]\](#cite_note-45 "#cite_note-45")\[[44]\](#cite_note-tot-46 "#cite_note-tot-46")

In July 1937, Japan captured the former Chinese imperial capital of [Peking](/wiki/Beijing "Beijing") after instigating the [Marco Polo Bridge incident](/wiki/Marco_Polo_Bridge_incident "Marco Polo Bridge incident"), which culminated in the Japanese campaign to invade all of China.\[[39]\](#cite\*note-FOOTNOTEEastman1986547–551-41 "#cite\*note-FOOTNOTEEastman1986547–551-41") The Soviets quickly signed a [non-aggression pact with China](/wiki/Sino-Soviet_Non-Aggression_Pact "Sino-Soviet Non-Aggression Pact") to lend [materiel](/wiki/Materiel "Materiel") support, effectively ending China's prior [cooperation with Germany](</wiki/China%E2%80%93Germany_relations*(1912%E2%80%931949)> "China–Germany relations (1912–1949)"). From September to November, the Japanese attacked [Taiyuan](/wiki/Battle_of_Taiyuan "Battle of Taiyuan"), engaged the [Kuomintang Army](/wiki/National_Revolutionary_Army "National Revolutionary Army") [around Xinkou](/wiki/Battle_of_Xinkou "Battle of Xinkou"),\[[40]\](#cite_note-Hsu\_&\_Chang_1971_221-42 "#cite_note-Hsu\*&\_Chang_1971_221-42") and fought [Communist forces](/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Party "Chinese Communist Party") [in Pingxingguan](/wiki/Battle_of_Pingxingguan "Battle of Pingxingguan").\[[41]\](#cite_note-Tucker2009-43 "#cite_note-Tucker2009-43")\[[42]\](#cite_note-yang-44 "#cite_note-yang-44") [Generalissimo](/wiki/Generalissimo "Generalissimo") [Chiang Kai-shek](/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek "Chiang Kai-shek") deployed his [best army](/wiki/List_of_German-trained_divisions_of_the_National_Revolutionary_Army "List of German-trained divisions of the National Revolutionary Army") to [defend Shanghai](/wiki/Battle_of_Shanghai "Battle of Shanghai"), but after three months of fighting, Shanghai fell. The Japanese continued to push Chinese forces back, [capturing the capital Nanking](/wiki/Battle_of_Nanking "Battle of Nanking") in December 1937. After the fall of Nanking, tens or hundreds of thousands of Chinese civilians and disarmed combatants were [murdered by the Japanese](/wiki/Nanjing_Massacre "Nanjing Massacre").\[[43]\](#cite_note-45 "#cite_note-45")\[[44]\](#cite_note-tot-46 "#cite_note-tot-46")

> > > > > > > origin/main

In March 1938, Nationalist Chinese forces won their [first major victory at Taierzhuang](/wiki/Battle_of_Taierzhuang "Battle of Taierzhuang"), but then the city of [Xuzhou](/wiki/Xuzhou "Xuzhou") [was taken by the Japanese](/wiki/Battle_of_Xuzhou "Battle of Xuzhou") in May.\[[45]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHsuChang1971221–230-47 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHsuChang1971221–230-47") In June 1938, Chinese forces stalled the Japanese advance by [flooding the Yellow River](/wiki/1938_Yellow_River_flood "1938 Yellow River flood"); this manoeuvre bought time for the Chinese to prepare their defences at [Wuhan](/wiki/Wuhan "Wuhan"), but the [city was taken](/wiki/Battle_of_Wuhan "Battle of Wuhan") by October.\[[46]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEastman1986566-48 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEastman1986566-48") Japanese military victories did not bring about the collapse of Chinese resistance that Japan had hoped to achieve; instead, the Chinese government relocated inland to [Chongqing](/wiki/Chongqing "Chongqing") and continued the war.\[[47]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaylor2009150–152-49 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaylor2009150–152-49")\[[48]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTESella1983651–687-50 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTESella1983651–687-50")

### Soviet–Japanese border conflicts

Main article: [Soviet–Japanese border conflicts](/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Japanese_border_conflicts "Soviet–Japanese border conflicts")
In the mid-to-late 1930s, Japanese forces in [Manchukuo](/wiki/Manchukuo "Manchukuo") had sporadic border clashes with the Soviet Union and [Mongolia](/wiki/Mongolian_People%27s_Republic "Mongolian People's Republic"). The Japanese doctrine of [Hokushin-ron](/wiki/Hokushin-ron "Hokushin-ron"), which emphasised Japan's expansion northward, was favoured by the Imperial Army during this time. This policy would prove difficult to maintain in light of the Japanese defeat at [Khalkin Gol](/wiki/Battles_of_Khalkhin_Gol "Battles of Khalkhin Gol") in 1939, the ongoing Second Sino-Japanese War\[[49]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor2012342-51 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor2012342-51") and ally Nazi Germany pursuing neutrality with the Soviets. Japan and the Soviet Union eventually signed a [Neutrality Pact](/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Japanese_Neutrality_Pact "Soviet–Japanese Neutrality Pact") in April 1941, and Japan adopted the doctrine of [Nanshin-ron](/wiki/Nanshin-ron "Nanshin-ron"), promoted by the Navy, which took its focus southward and eventually led to war with the United States and the Western Allies.\[[50]\](#cite_note-52 "#cite_note-52")\[[51]\](#cite_note-53 "#cite_note-53")

### European occupations and agreements

[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R69173%2C_M%C3%BCnchener_Abkommen%2C_Staatschefs.jpg/250px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R69173%2C_M%C3%BCnchener_Abkommen%2C_Staatschefs.jpg' alt='' title='' width='250' height='171' />](/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R69173,_M%C3%BCnchener_Abkommen,_Staatschefs.jpg "/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R69173,_M%C3%BCnchener_Abkommen,_Staatschefs.jpg")

[Chamberlain](/wiki/Neville_Chamberlain "Neville Chamberlain"), [Daladier](/wiki/%C3%89douard_Daladier "Édouard Daladier"), [Hitler](/wiki/Adolf_Hitler "Adolf Hitler"), [Mussolini](/wiki/Benito_Mussolini "Benito Mussolini"), and [Ciano](/wiki/Galeazzo_Ciano "Galeazzo Ciano") pictured just before signing the [Munich Agreement](/wiki/Munich_Agreement "Munich Agreement"), 29 September 1938

In Europe, Germany and Italy were becoming more aggressive. In March 1938, Germany [annexed Austria](/wiki/Anschluss "Anschluss"), again provoking [little response](/wiki/Appeasement "Appeasement") from other European powers.\[[52]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollierPedley2000144-54 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollierPedley2000144-54") Encouraged, Hitler began pressing German claims on the [Sudetenland](/wiki/Sudetenland "Sudetenland"), an area of [Czechoslovakia](/wiki/Czechoslovakia "Czechoslovakia") with a predominantly [ethnic German](/wiki/Germans "Germans") population. Soon the United Kingdom and France followed the appeasement policy of British Prime Minister [Neville Chamberlain](/wiki/Neville_Chamberlain "Neville Chamberlain") and conceded this territory to Germany in the [Munich Agreement](/wiki/Munich_Agreement "Munich Agreement"), which was made against the wishes of the Czechoslovak government, in exchange for a promise of no further territorial demands.\[[53]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2001121–122-55 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2001121–122-55") Soon afterwards, Germany and Italy forced Czechoslovakia to [cede additional territory](/wiki/First_Vienna_Award "First Vienna Award") to Hungary, and Poland annexed the [Trans-Olza](/wiki/Trans-Olza "Trans-Olza") region of Czechoslovakia.\[[54]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2001157-56 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2001157-56")

Although all of Germany's stated demands had been satisfied by the agreement, privately Hitler was furious that British interference had prevented him from seizing all of Czechoslovakia in one operation. In subsequent speeches Hitler attacked British and Jewish "war-mongers" and in January 1939 [secretly ordered a major build-up of the German navy](/wiki/Plan_Z "Plan Z") to challenge British naval supremacy. In March 1939, [Germany invaded the remainder of Czechoslovakia](</wiki/Occupation_of_Czechoslovakia_(1938%E2%80%931945)> "Occupation of Czechoslovakia (1938–1945)") and subsequently split it into the German [Protectorate of Bohemia and Moravia](/wiki/Protectorate_of_Bohemia_and_Moravia "Protectorate of Bohemia and Moravia") and a pro-German [client state](/wiki/Client_state "Client state"), the [Slovak Republic](</wiki/Slovak_Republic_(1939%E2%80%931945)> "Slovak Republic (1939–1945)").\[[55]\](#cite*note-FOOTNOTEDavies2006pp.\_143–144*(2008*ed.)-57 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies2006pp.\_143–144*(2008*ed.)-57") Hitler also delivered an [ultimatum to Lithuania](/wiki/1939_German_ultimatum_to_Lithuania "1939 German ultimatum to Lithuania") on 20 March 1939, forcing the concession of the [Klaipėda Region](/wiki/Klaip%C4%97da_Region "Klaipėda Region"), formerly the German \_Memelland*.\[[56]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer1990461–462-58 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer1990461–462-58")

[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H27337%2C_Moskau%2C_Stalin_und_Ribbentrop_im_Kreml.jpg/250px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H27337%2C_Moskau%2C_Stalin_und_Ribbentrop_im_Kreml.jpg' alt='' title='' width='190' height='250' />](/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H27337,_Moskau,_Stalin_und_Ribbentrop_im_Kreml.jpg "/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H27337,_Moskau,_Stalin_und_Ribbentrop_im_Kreml.jpg")

German Foreign Minister [Joachim von Ribbentrop](/wiki/Joachim_von_Ribbentrop "Joachim von Ribbentrop") (right) and the Soviet leader [Joseph Stalin](/wiki/Joseph_Stalin "Joseph Stalin"), after signing the [Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact](/wiki/Molotov%E2%80%93Ribbentrop_Pact "Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact"), 23 August 1939

Greatly alarmed and with Hitler making further demands on the [Free City of Danzig](/wiki/Free_City_of_Danzig "Free City of Danzig"), the United Kingdom and France [guaranteed their support for Polish independence](/wiki/Anglo-Polish_alliance#British_assurance_to_Poland "Anglo-Polish alliance"); when [Italy conquered Albania](/wiki/Italian_invasion_of_Albania "Italian invasion of Albania") in April 1939, the same guarantee was extended to the [Kingdoms of Romania](/wiki/Kingdom_of_Romania "Kingdom of Romania") and [Greece](/wiki/Kingdom_of_Greece "Kingdom of Greece").\[[57]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTELoweMarzari2002330-59 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTELoweMarzari2002330-59") Shortly after the [Franco](/wiki/Franco-Polish_alliance "Franco-Polish alliance")-[British](/wiki/Anglo-Polish_alliance "Anglo-Polish alliance") pledge to Poland, Germany and Italy formalised their own alliance with the [Pact of Steel](/wiki/Pact_of_Steel "Pact of Steel").\[[58]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDearFoot2001234-60 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDearFoot2001234-60") Hitler accused the United Kingdom and Poland of trying to "encircle" Germany and renounced the [Anglo-German Naval Agreement](/wiki/Anglo-German_Naval_Agreement "Anglo-German Naval Agreement") and the [German–Polish declaration of non-aggression](/wiki/German%E2%80%93Polish_declaration_of_non-aggression "German–Polish declaration of non-aggression").\[[59]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer1990471-61 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer1990471-61")

The situation became a crisis in late August as German troops continued to mobilise against the Polish border. On 23 August the Soviet Union signed [a non-aggression pact](/wiki/Molotov%E2%80%93Ribbentrop_Pact "Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact") with Germany,\[[60]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShore2003108-62 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShore2003108-62") after tripartite negotiations for a military alliance between France, the United Kingdom, and Soviet Union had stalled.\[[61]\](#cite_note-63 "#cite_note-63") This pact had a secret protocol that defined German and Soviet "spheres of influence" (western [Poland](/wiki/Second_Polish_Republic "Second Polish Republic") and Lithuania for Germany; [eastern Poland](/wiki/Territories_of_Poland_annexed_by_the_Soviet_Union "Territories of Poland annexed by the Soviet Union"), Finland, [Estonia](/wiki/Estonia "Estonia"), [Latvia](/wiki/Latvia "Latvia") and [Bessarabia](/wiki/Bessarabia "Bessarabia") for the Soviet Union), and raised the question of continuing Polish independence.\[[62]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDearFoot2001608-64 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDearFoot2001608-64") The pact neutralised the possibility of Soviet opposition to a campaign against Poland and assured that Germany would not have to face the prospect of a two-front war, as it had in World War I. Immediately afterwards, Hitler ordered the attack to proceed on 26 August, but upon hearing that the United Kingdom had concluded a formal mutual assistance pact with Poland and that Italy would maintain neutrality, he decided to delay it.\[[63]\](#cite_note-65 "#cite_note-65")

In response to British requests for direct negotiations to avoid war, Germany made demands on Poland, which served as a pretext to worsen relations.\[[64]\](#cite_note-ww2db_com-66 "#cite_note-ww2db_com-66") On 29 August, Hitler demanded that a Polish [plenipotentiary](/wiki/Plenipotentiary "Plenipotentiary") immediately travel to Berlin to negotiate the handover of [Danzig](/wiki/Gda%C5%84sk "Gdańsk"), and to allow a [plebiscite](/wiki/Referendum "Referendum") in the [Polish Corridor](/wiki/Polish_Corridor "Polish Corridor") in which the German minority would vote on secession.\[[64]\](#cite_note-ww2db_com-66 "#cite_note-ww2db_com-66") The Poles refused to comply with the German demands, and on the night of 30–31 August in a confrontational meeting with the British ambassador [Nevile Henderson](/wiki/Nevile_Henderson "Nevile Henderson"), Ribbentrop declared that Germany considered its claims rejected.\[[65]\](#cite_note-ibiblio1939-67 "#cite_note-ibiblio1939-67")

## Course of the war

For a chronological guide, see [List of timelines of World War II](/wiki/List_of_timelines_of_World_War_II "List of timelines of World War II").
See also: [Diplomatic history of World War II](/wiki/Diplomatic_history_of_World_War_II "Diplomatic history of World War II") and [World War II by country](/wiki/World_War_II_by_country "World War II by country")

### War breaks out in Europe (1939–1940)

Main article: [European theatre of World War II](/wiki/European_theatre_of_World_War_II "European theatre of World War II")
[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Danzig_Police_at_Polish_Border_%281939-09-01%29.jpg/250px-Danzig_Police_at_Polish_Border_%281939-09-01%29.jpg' alt='' title='' width='250' height='172' />](</wiki/File:Danzig_Police_at_Polish_Border_(1939-09-01).jpg> "/wiki/File:Danzig_Police_at_Polish_Border_(1939-09-01).jpg")

A German propaganda photo reenacting the removal of the Polish border crossing in [Sopot](/wiki/Sopot "Sopot")\[[66]\](#cite_note-68 "#cite_note-68")

On 1 September 1939, Germany [invaded Poland](/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland "Invasion of Poland") after [having staged](/wiki/Operation_Himmler "Operation Himmler") several [false flag border incidents](/wiki/Gleiwitz_incident "Gleiwitz incident") as a pretext to initiate the invasion.\[[67]\](#cite*note-FOOTNOTEEvans20081–2-69 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans20081–2-69") The first German attack of the war came against the [Polish defences at Westerplatte](/wiki/Battle_of_Westerplatte "Battle of Westerplatte").\[[68]\](#cite_note-Zabecki2015-70 "#cite_note-Zabecki2015-70") The United Kingdom responded with an ultimatum for Germany to cease military operations, and on 3 September, after the ultimatum was ignored, Britain and France declared war on Germany.\[[c]\](#cite_note-71 "#cite_note-71") During the [Phoney War](/wiki/Phoney_War "Phoney War") period, the alliance provided no direct military support to Poland, outside of a [cautious French probe into the Saarland](/wiki/Saar_Offensive "Saar Offensive").\[[69]\](#cite_note-Keegan_1997_35-72 "#cite_note-Keegan_1997_35-72") The Western Allies also began a [naval blockade of Germany](</wiki/Blockade_of_Germany*(1939%E2%80%931945)> "Blockade of Germany (1939–1945)"), which aimed to damage the country's economy and war effort.\[[70]\](#cite*note-73 "#cite\*note-73") Germany responded by ordering [U-boat warfare](/wiki/Submarine_warfare#World_War_II "Submarine warfare") against Allied merchant and warships, which would later escalate into the [Battle of the Atlantic](/wiki/Battle_of_the_Atlantic "Battle of the Atlantic").\[[71]\](#cite_note-74 "#cite_note-74")
On 8 September, German troops reached the suburbs of [Warsaw](/wiki/Warsaw "Warsaw"). The Polish [counter-offensive](/wiki/Battle_of_the_Bzura "Battle of the Bzura") to the west halted the German advance for several days, but it was outflanked and encircled by the \*[Wehrmacht](/wiki/Wehrmacht "Wehrmacht")\_. Remnants of the Polish army broke through to [besieged Warsaw](</wiki/Siege_of_Warsaw*(1939)> "Siege of Warsaw (1939)"). On 17 September 1939, two days after signing a [cease-fire with Japan](/wiki/Battles_of_Khalkhin_Gol "Battles of Khalkhin Gol"), the [Soviet Union invaded Poland](/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Poland "Soviet invasion of Poland")\[[72]\](#cite\*note-FOOTNOTEZaloga200280,\_83-75 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZaloga200280,\_83-75") under the supposed pretext that the Polish state had ceased to exist.\[[73]\](#cite_note-76 "#cite_note-76") On 27 September, the Warsaw garrison surrendered to the Germans, and [the last large operational unit of the Polish Army](/wiki/Independent_Operational_Group_Polesie "Independent Operational Group Polesie") [surrendered on 6 October](</wiki/Battle_of_Kock*(1939)> "Battle of Kock (1939)"). Despite the military defeat, Poland never surrendered; instead, it formed the [Polish government-in-exile](/wiki/Polish_government-in-exile "Polish government-in-exile") and a [clandestine state apparatus remained](/wiki/Polish_Underground_State "Polish Underground State") in occupied Poland.\[[74]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHempel200524-77 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHempel200524-77") A significant part of Polish military personnel [evacuated to Romania](/wiki/Romanian_Bridgehead "Romanian Bridgehead") and Latvia; many of them later [fought against the Axis](/wiki/Military_history_of_Poland_during_World_War_II "Military history of Poland during World War II") in other theatres of the war.\[[75]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZaloga200288–89-78 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZaloga200288–89-78")

Germany [annexed western](/wiki/Polish_areas_annexed_by_Nazi_Germany "Polish areas annexed by Nazi Germany") Poland and [occupied central Poland](/wiki/General_Government "General Government"); the Soviet Union [annexed eastern Poland](/wiki/Territories_of_Poland_annexed_by_the_Soviet_Union "Territories of Poland annexed by the Soviet Union"); small shares of Polish territory were transferred to [Lithuania](/wiki/Territorial_evolution_of_Poland#World_War_II "Territorial evolution of Poland") and [Slovakia](/wiki/Slovak_invasion_of_Poland "Slovak invasion of Poland"). On 6 October, Hitler made a public peace overture to the United Kingdom and France but said that the future of Poland was to be determined exclusively by Germany and the Soviet Union. The proposal was rejected\[[65]\](#cite*note-ibiblio1939-67 "#cite_note-ibiblio1939-67") and Hitler ordered an immediate offensive against France,\[[76]\](#cite_note-79 "#cite_note-79") which was postponed until the spring of 1940 due to bad weather.\[[77]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTELiddell_Hart197739–40-80 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTELiddell_Hart197739–40-80")\[[78]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock1990pp.\_563–564,\_566,\_568–569,\_574–575*(1983*ed.)-81 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock1990pp.\_563–564,\_566,\_568–569,\_574–575*(1983_ed.)-81")\[[79]\](#cite_note-82 "#cite_note-82")

[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Karelian_Isthmus_13_March_1940.png/250px-Karelian_Isthmus_13_March_1940.png' alt='' title='' width='250' height='225' />](/wiki/File:Karelian_Isthmus_13_March_1940.png "/wiki/File:Karelian_Isthmus_13_March_1940.png")

[Mannerheim Line](/wiki/Mannerheim_Line "Mannerheim Line") and [Karelian Isthmus](/wiki/Karelian_Isthmus "Karelian Isthmus") on the last day of the [Winter War](/wiki/Winter_War "Winter War"), 13 March 1940

After the outbreak of war in Poland, Stalin threatened [Estonia](/wiki/Estonia "Estonia"), [Latvia](/wiki/Latvia "Latvia"), and [Lithuania](/wiki/Lithuania "Lithuania") with military invasion, forcing the three [Baltic countries](/wiki/Baltic_states "Baltic states") to sign [pacts](/wiki/Background_of_the_occupation_of_the_Baltic_states#Soviet_ultimatums_and_occupation "Background of the occupation of the Baltic states") allowing the creation of Soviet military bases in these countries; in October 1939, significant Soviet military contingents were moved there.\[[80]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmithPabriksPursLane200224-83 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmithPabriksPursLane200224-83")\[[81]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBilinsky19999-84 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBilinsky19999-84")\[[82]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMurrayMillett200155–56-85 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMurrayMillett200155–56-85") [Finland](/wiki/Finland "Finland") refused to sign a similar pact and rejected ceding part of its territory to the Soviet Union. [The Soviet Union invaded Finland](/wiki/Winter_War#Soviet_invasion "Winter War") in November 1939,\[[83]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpring1986207–226-86 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpring1986207–226-86") and was subsequently expelled from the [League of Nations](/wiki/League_of_Nations "League of Nations") for this crime of aggression.\[[84]\](#cite_note-87 "#cite_note-87") Despite overwhelming numerical superiority, Soviet military success during the [Winter War](/wiki/Winter_War "Winter War") was modest, and the Finno-Soviet war ended in March 1940 with [some Finnish concessions of territory](/wiki/Moscow_Peace_Treaty "Moscow Peace Treaty").\[[85]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHanhimäki199712-88 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHanhimäki199712-88")

In June 1940, the Soviet Union [occupied](</wiki/Soviet_occupation_of_the_Baltic_states_(1940)> "Soviet occupation of the Baltic states (1940)") the entire territories of Estonia, Latvia and Lithuania,\[[81]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBilinsky19999-84 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBilinsky19999-84") as well as the Romanian regions of [Bessarabia, Northern Bukovina, and the Hertsa region](/wiki/Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina "Soviet occupation of Bessarabia and Northern Bukovina"). In August 1940, Hitler imposed the [Second Vienna Award](/wiki/Second_Vienna_Award "Second Vienna Award") on Romania which led to the transfer of [Northern Transylvania](/wiki/Northern_Transylvania "Northern Transylvania") to Hungary.\[[86]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDearFoot2001745,\_975-89 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDearFoot2001745,\_975-89") In September 1940, Bulgaria demanded [Southern Dobruja](/wiki/Southern_Dobruja "Southern Dobruja") from Romania with German and Italian support, leading to the [Treaty of Craiova](/wiki/Treaty_of_Craiova "Treaty of Craiova").\[[87]\](#cite_note-Haynes-2000-90 "#cite_note-Haynes-2000-90") The loss of one-third of Romania's 1939 territory caused a coup against King Carol II, turning Romania into a fascist dictatorship under Marshal [Ion Antonescu](/wiki/Ion_Antonescu "Ion Antonescu"), with a course set towards the Axis in the hopes of a German guarantee.\[[88]\](#cite_note-91 "#cite_note-91") Meanwhile, German-Soviet political relations and economic co-operation\[[89]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2006367,\_376,\_379,\_417-92 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2006367,\_376,\_379,\_417-92")\[[90]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTESnyder2010118ff-93 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTESnyder2010118ff-93") gradually stalled,\[[91]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKoch1983912–914,\_917–920-94 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKoch1983912–914,\_917–920-94")\[[92]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoberts200656-95 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoberts200656-95") and both states began preparations for war.\[[93]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoberts200659-96 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoberts200659-96")

### Western Europe (1940–1941)

Main article: [Western Front (World War II)](</wiki/Western_Front_(World_War_II)> "Western Front (World War II)")
[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/WWIIEuropeMay40.gif/500px-WWIIEuropeMay40.gif' alt='' title='' width='350' height='271' />](/wiki/File:WWIIEuropeMay40.gif "/wiki/File:WWIIEuropeMay40.gif")

German advance into Belgium and Northern France, 10 May – 4 June 1940, sweeping past the [Maginot Line](/wiki/Maginot_Line "Maginot Line") (shown in dark red)

In April 1940, [Germany invaded Denmark and Norway](/wiki/Operation_Weser%C3%BCbung "Operation Weserübung") to protect shipments of [iron ore from Sweden](/wiki/Swedish_iron-ore_industry_during_World_War_II "Swedish iron-ore industry during World War II"), which the Allies were [attempting to cut off](/wiki/Operation_Wilfred "Operation Wilfred").\[[94]\](#cite\*note-97 "#cite_note-97") [Denmark capitulated after six hours](</wiki/German_invasion_of_Denmark*(1940)> "German invasion of Denmark (1940)"), and [despite Allied support](/wiki/Norwegian_campaign "Norwegian campaign"), Norway was conquered within two months.\[[95]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTECommager20049-98 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTECommager20049-98") [British discontent over the Norwegian campaign](/wiki/Norway_Debate "Norway Debate") led to the resignation of Prime Minister [Neville Chamberlain](/wiki/Neville_Chamberlain "Neville Chamberlain"), who was replaced by [Winston Churchill](/wiki/Winston_Churchill "Winston Churchill") on 10 May 1940.\[[96]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReynolds200676-99 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReynolds200676-99")

On the same day, Germany [launched an offensive against France](/wiki/Battle_of_France "Battle of France"). To circumvent the strong [Maginot Line](/wiki/Maginot_Line "Maginot Line") fortifications on the Franco-German border, Germany directed its attack at the neutral nations of [Belgium](</wiki/German_invasion_of_Belgium_(1940)> "German invasion of Belgium (1940)"), [the Netherlands](/wiki/German_invasion_of_the_Netherlands "German invasion of the Netherlands"), and [Luxembourg](/wiki/German_invasion_of_Luxembourg "German invasion of Luxembourg").\[[97]\](#cite\*note-FOOTNOTEEvans2008122–123-100 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2008122–123-100") The Germans carried out a flanking manoeuvre through the [Ardennes](/wiki/Ardennes "Ardennes") region,\[[98]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeegan199759–60-101 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeegan199759–60-101") which was mistakenly perceived by the Allies as an impenetrable natural barrier against armoured vehicles.\[[99]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTERegan2004152-102 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTERegan2004152-102")\[[100]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTELiddell_Hart197748-103 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTELiddell_Hart197748-103") By successfully implementing new \*[Blitzkrieg](/wiki/Blitzkrieg "Blitzkrieg")\_ tactics, the \_Wehrmacht\_ rapidly advanced to the Channel and cut off the Allied forces in Belgium, trapping the bulk of the Allied armies in a cauldron on the Franco-Belgian border near Lille. The United Kingdom was able [to evacuate a significant number of Allied troops](/wiki/Dunkirk_evacuation "Dunkirk evacuation") from the continent by early June, although they had to abandon almost all their equipment.\[[101]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeegan199766–67-104 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeegan199766–67-104")

On 10 June, [Italy invaded France](/wiki/Italian_invasion_of_France "Italian invasion of France"), declaring war on both France and the United Kingdom.\[[102]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOveryWheatcroft1999207-105 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOveryWheatcroft1999207-105") The Germans turned south against the weakened French army, and [Paris](/wiki/Paris_in_World_War_II "Paris in World War II") fell to them on 14 June. Eight days later [France signed an armistice with Germany](/wiki/Armistice_of_22_June_1940 "Armistice of 22 June 1940"); it was divided into [German](/wiki/German_military_administration_in_occupied_France_during_World_War_II "German military administration in occupied France during World War II") and [Italian occupation zones](/wiki/Italian_occupation_of_France "Italian occupation of France"),\[[103]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUmbreit1991311-106 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUmbreit1991311-106") and an unoccupied [rump state](/wiki/Rump_state "Rump state") under the [Vichy Regime](/wiki/Vichy_France "Vichy France"), which, though officially neutral, was generally aligned with Germany. France kept its fleet, which [the United Kingdom attacked](/wiki/Attack_on_Mers-el-K%C3%A9bir "Attack on Mers-el-Kébir") on 3 July in an attempt to prevent its seizure by Germany.\[[104]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrown2004198-107 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrown2004198-107")

The air [Battle of Britain](/wiki/Battle_of_Britain "Battle of Britain")\[[105]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeegan1997[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidTF8kcx9hTssCpgPA72_72]-108 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeegan1997[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidTF8kcx9hTssCpgPA72_72]-108") began in early July with [Luftwaffe attacks on shipping and harbours](/wiki/Kanalkampf "Kanalkampf").\[[106]\](#cite_note-Murray_BoB-109 "#cite_note-Murray_BoB-109") The [German campaign for air superiority](/wiki/Adlertag "Adlertag") started in August but its failure to defeat [RAF Fighter Command](/wiki/RAF_Fighter_Command "RAF Fighter Command") forced the indefinite postponement of the [proposed German invasion of Britain](/wiki/Operation_Sea_Lion "Operation Sea Lion"). The German [strategic bombing](/wiki/Strategic_bombing "Strategic bombing") offensive intensified with night attacks on London and other cities in [the Blitz](/wiki/The_Blitz "The Blitz"), but largely ended in May 1941\[[107]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDearFoot2001108–109-110 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDearFoot2001108–109-110") after failing to significantly disrupt the British war effort.\[[106]\](#cite_note-Murray_BoB-109 "#cite_note-Murray_BoB-109")

Using newly captured French ports, the German Navy [enjoyed success](</wiki/Battle_of_the_Atlantic#'The_Happy_Time'_(June_1940_%E2%80%93_February_1941)> "Battle of the Atlantic") against an over-extended [Royal Navy](/wiki/Royal_Navy "Royal Navy"), using [U-boats](/wiki/U-boat "U-boat") against British shipping [in the Atlantic](/wiki/Battle_of_the_Atlantic "Battle of the Atlantic").\[[108]\](#cite\*note-111 "#cite_note-111") The British [Home Fleet](/wiki/Home_Fleet "Home Fleet") scored a significant victory on 27 May 1941 by [sinking the German battleship \_Bismarck\*](/wiki/Last_battle_of_Bismarck "Last battle of Bismarck").\[[109]\](#cite_note-112 "#cite_note-112")

In November 1939, the United States was assisting China and the Western Allies, and had amended the [Neutrality Act](/wiki/Neutrality_Acts_of_the_1930s "Neutrality Acts of the 1930s") to allow "[cash and carry](</wiki/Cash_and_carry_(World_War_II)> "Cash and carry (World War II)")" purchases by the Allies.\[[110]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOveryWheatcroft1999328–330-113 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOveryWheatcroft1999328–330-113") In 1940, following the German capture of Paris, the size of the [United States Navy](/wiki/United_States_Navy "United States Navy") was [significantly increased](/wiki/Two-Ocean_Navy_Act "Two-Ocean Navy Act"). In September the United States further agreed to a [trade of American destroyers for British bases](/wiki/Destroyers-for-bases_deal "Destroyers-for-bases deal").\[[111]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaingot199452-114 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaingot199452-114") Still, a large majority of the American public continued to oppose any direct military intervention in the conflict well into 1941.\[[112]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTECantril1940390-115 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTECantril1940390-115") In December 1940, Roosevelt accused Hitler of planning world conquest and ruled out any negotiations as useless, calling for the United States to become an "[arsenal of democracy](/wiki/Arsenal_of_Democracy "Arsenal of Democracy")" and promoting [Lend-Lease](/wiki/Lend-Lease "Lend-Lease") programmes of military and humanitarian aid to support the British war effort; Lend-Lease was later extended to the other Allies, including the Soviet Union after it was [invaded](/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa "Operation Barbarossa") by Germany.\[[113]\](#cite_note-ibiblio_1940-116 "#cite_note-ibiblio_1940-116") The United States started strategic planning to prepare for a full-scale offensive against Germany.\[[114]\](#cite_note-117 "#cite_note-117")

At the end of September 1940, the [Tripartite Pact](/wiki/Tripartite_Pact "Tripartite Pact") formally united Japan, Italy, and Germany as the [Axis powers](/wiki/Axis_powers "Axis powers"). The Tripartite Pact stipulated that any country—with the exception of the Soviet Union—that attacked any Axis Power would be forced to go to war against all three.\[[115]\](#cite\*note-FOOTNOTEBilhartzElliott2007179-118 "#cite\*note-FOOTNOTEBilhartzElliott2007179-118") The Axis expanded in November 1940 when [Hungary](</wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary*(1920%E2%80%931946)> "Kingdom of Hungary (1920–1946)"), [Slovakia](</wiki/Slovak_Republic*(1939%E2%80%931945)> "Slovak Republic (1939–1945)"), and [Romania](/wiki/Kingdom_of_Romania "Kingdom of Romania") joined.\[[116]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDearFoot2001877-119 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDearFoot2001877-119") [Romania](/wiki/Romania_in_World_War_II "Romania in World War II") and [Hungary](/wiki/Hungary_in_World_War_II "Hungary in World War II") later made major contributions to the Axis war against the Soviet Union, in Romania's case partially to recapture [territory ceded to the Soviet Union](/wiki/Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina "Soviet occupation of Bessarabia and Northern Bukovina").\[[117]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDearFoot2001745–746-120 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDearFoot2001745–746-120")

### Mediterranean (1940–1941)

Main article: [Mediterranean and Middle East theatre of World War II](/wiki/Mediterranean_and_Middle_East_theatre_of_World_War_II "Mediterranean and Middle East theatre of World War II")
In early June 1940, the Italian _[Regia Aeronautica](/wiki/Regia_Aeronautica "Regia Aeronautica")_ [attacked and besieged Malta](</wiki/Siege_of_Malta_(World_War_II)> "Siege of Malta (World War II)"), a British possession. From late summer to early autumn, Italy [conquered British Somaliland](/wiki/Italian_invasion_of_British_Somaliland "Italian invasion of British Somaliland") and made an [incursion into British-held Egypt](/wiki/Italian_invasion_of_Egypt "Italian invasion of Egypt"). In October, [Italy attacked Greece](/wiki/Greco-Italian_War "Greco-Italian War"), but the attack was repulsed with heavy Italian casualties; the campaign ended within months with minor territorial changes.\[[118]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClogg2002118-121 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClogg2002118-121") To assist Italy and prevent Britain from gaining a foothold, Germany prepared to invade the Balkans, which would threaten Romanian oil fields and strike against British dominance of the Mediterranean.\[[119]\](#cite_note-122 "#cite_note-122")

[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-783-0109-11%2C_Nordafrika%2C_Panzer_III_in_Fahrt.jpg/250px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-783-0109-11%2C_Nordafrika%2C_Panzer_III_in_Fahrt.jpg' alt='' title='' width='250' height='152' />](/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-783-0109-11,_Nordafrika,_Panzer_III_in_Fahrt.jpg "/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-783-0109-11,_Nordafrika,_Panzer_III_in_Fahrt.jpg")

German [Panzer III](/wiki/Panzer_III "Panzer III") of the [Afrika Korps](/wiki/Afrika_Korps "Afrika Korps") advancing across the North African desert, April 1941

In December 1940, British Empire forces began [counter-offensives](/wiki/Operation_Compass "Operation Compass") against Italian forces in Egypt and [Italian East Africa](</wiki/East_African_campaign_(World_War_II)> "East African campaign (World War II)").\[[120]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJowett20019–10-123 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJowett20019–10-123") The offensives were successful; by early February 1941, Italy had lost control of eastern Libya, and large numbers of Italian troops had been taken prisoner. The [Italian Navy](/wiki/Regia_Marina "Regia Marina") also suffered significant defeats, with the Royal Navy putting three Italian battleships out of commission after a [carrier attack at Taranto](/wiki/Battle_of_Taranto "Battle of Taranto"), and neutralising several more warships at the [Battle of Cape Matapan](/wiki/Battle_of_Cape_Matapan "Battle of Cape Matapan").\[[121]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson2006106-124 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson2006106-124")

Italian defeats prompted Germany to [deploy an expeditionary force](/wiki/Operation_Sonnenblume "Operation Sonnenblume") to North Africa; at the end of March 1941, [Rommel](/wiki/Erwin_Rommel "Erwin Rommel")'s [Afrika Korps](/wiki/Afrika_Korps "Afrika Korps") [launched an offensive](/wiki/Western_Desert_campaign "Western Desert campaign") which drove back Commonwealth forces.\[[122]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaurier20017–8-125 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaurier20017–8-125") In less than a month, Axis forces advanced to western Egypt and [besieged the port of Tobruk](/wiki/Siege_of_Tobruk "Siege of Tobruk").\[[123]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMurrayMillett2001263–276-126 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMurrayMillett2001263–276-126")

By late March 1941, [Bulgaria](</wiki/Tsardom_of_Bulgaria_(1908%E2%80%931946)> "Tsardom of Bulgaria (1908–1946)") and [Yugoslavia](/wiki/Yugoslavia "Yugoslavia") signed the [Tripartite Pact](/wiki/Tripartite_Pact "Tripartite Pact"); however, the Yugoslav government was [overthrown two days later](/wiki/Yugoslav_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat "Yugoslav coup d'état") by pro-British nationalists. Germany and Italy responded with simultaneous invasions of both [Yugoslavia](/wiki/Invasion_of_Yugoslavia "Invasion of Yugoslavia") and [Greece](/wiki/German_invasion_of_Greece "German invasion of Greece"), commencing on 6 April 1941; both nations were forced to surrender within the month.\[[124]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert1989174–175-127 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert1989174–175-127") The airborne [invasion of the Greek island of Crete](/wiki/Battle_of_Crete "Battle of Crete") at the end of May completed the German conquest of the Balkans.\[[125]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert1989184–187-128 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert1989184–187-128") Partisan warfare subsequently broke out against the [Axis occupation of Yugoslavia](/wiki/World_War_II_in_Yugoslavia "World War II in Yugoslavia"), which continued until the end of the war.\[[126]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert1989208,\_575,\_604-129 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert1989208,\_575,\_604-129")

In the Middle East in May, Commonwealth forces [quashed an uprising in Iraq](/wiki/Anglo-Iraqi_War "Anglo-Iraqi War") which had been supported by German aircraft from bases within Vichy-controlled [Syria](/wiki/Mandate_for_Syria_and_the_Lebanon "Mandate for Syria and the Lebanon").\[[127]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWatson200380-130 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWatson200380-130") Between June and July, British-led forces [invaded and occupied the French possessions of Syria and Lebanon](/wiki/Syria%E2%80%93Lebanon_campaign "Syria–Lebanon campaign"), assisted by the [Free French](/wiki/Free_France "Free France").\[[128]\](#cite_note-131 "#cite_note-131")

### Axis attack on the Soviet Union (1941)

Main article: [Eastern Front (World War II)](</wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)> "Eastern Front (World War II)")
[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Second_world_war_europe_animation_large_de.gif/330px-Second_world_war_europe_animation_large_de.gif' alt='' title='' width='300' height='313' />](/wiki/File:Second_world_war_europe_animation_large_de.gif "/wiki/File:Second_world_war_europe_animation_large_de.gif")

[European theatre of World War II](/wiki/European_theatre_of_World_War_II "European theatre of World War II") animation map, 1939–1945 – Red: [Western Allies](/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II "Allies of World War II") and the Soviet Union after 1941; Green: [Soviet Union](/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union") before 1941; Blue: [Axis powers](/wiki/Axis_powers "Axis powers")

With the situation in Europe and Asia relatively stable, Germany, Japan, and the Soviet Union made preparations for war. With the Soviets wary of mounting tensions with Germany, and the Japanese planning to take advantage of the European War by seizing resource-rich European possessions in [Southeast Asia](/wiki/Southeast_Asia "Southeast Asia"), the two powers signed the [Soviet–Japanese Neutrality Pact](/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Japanese_Neutrality_Pact "Soviet–Japanese Neutrality Pact") in April 1941.\[[129]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGarver1988114-132 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGarver1988114-132") By contrast, the Germans were steadily making preparations for an attack on the Soviet Union, massing forces on the Soviet border.\[[130]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeinberg2005195-133 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeinberg2005195-133")

Hitler believed that the United Kingdom's refusal to end the war was based on the hope that the United States and the Soviet Union would enter the war against Germany sooner or later.\[[131]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMurray1983[httpswwwibiblioorghyperwarAAFAAF-LuftwaffeAAF-Luftwaffe-3html_69]-134 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMurray1983[httpswwwibiblioorghyperwarAAFAAF-LuftwaffeAAF-Luftwaffe-3html_69]-134") On 31 July 1940, Hitler decided that the Soviet Union should be eliminated and aimed for the conquest of [Ukraine](/wiki/Ukrainian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic"), the [Baltic states](/wiki/Baltic_states "Baltic states") and [Byelorussia](/wiki/Byelorussian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Byelorussian Soviet Socialist Republic").\[[132]\](#cite_note-GSWW4_26-135 "#cite_note-GSWW4_26-135") However, other senior German officials like Ribbentrop saw an opportunity to create a Euro-Asian bloc against the British Empire by inviting the Soviet Union into the Tripartite Pact.\[[133]\](#cite_note-GSWW4_38-136 "#cite_note-GSWW4_38-136") In November 1940, [negotiations took place](/wiki/German%E2%80%93Soviet_Axis_talks "German–Soviet Axis talks") to determine if the Soviet Union would join the pact. The Soviets showed some interest but asked for concessions from Finland, Bulgaria, Turkey, and Japan that Germany considered unacceptable. On 18 December 1940, Hitler issued the directive to prepare for an invasion of the Soviet Union.\[[134]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer1990810–812-137 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer1990810–812-137")

On 22 June 1941, Germany, supported by Italy and Romania, invaded the Soviet Union in [Operation Barbarossa](/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa "Operation Barbarossa"), with Germany accusing the Soviets of [plotting against them](/wiki/Soviet_offensive_plans_controversy "Soviet offensive plans controversy"); they were joined shortly by Finland and Hungary.\[[135]\](#cite\*note-Events1941-138 "#cite\*note-Events1941-138") The primary targets of this surprise offensive\[[136]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTESella1978555-139 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTESella1978555-139") were the [Baltic region](/wiki/Baltic_region "Baltic region"), Moscow and Ukraine, with the [ultimate goal](</wiki/Strategic_goal*(military)> "Strategic goal (military)") of ending the 1941 campaign near the [Arkhangelsk–Astrakhan line](/wiki/A%E2%80%93A_line "A–A line")—from the [Caspian](/wiki/Caspian_Sea "Caspian Sea") to the [White Seas](/wiki/White_Sea "White Sea"). Hitler's objectives were to eliminate the Soviet Union as a military power, exterminate [Communism](/wiki/Communism "Communism"), generate \*[Lebensraum](/wiki/Lebensraum "Lebensraum")\_ ("living space")\[[137]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw200766–69-140 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw200766–69-140") by [dispossessing the native population](/wiki/Generalplan_Ost "Generalplan Ost"),\[[138]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTESteinberg1995-141 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTESteinberg1995-141") and guarantee access to the strategic resources needed to defeat Germany's remaining rivals.\[[139]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHauner1978-142 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHauner1978-142")

Although the [Red Army](/wiki/Red_Army "Red Army") was preparing for strategic [counter-offensives](/wiki/Counter-offensive "Counter-offensive") before the war,\[[140]\](#cite*note-FOOTNOTERoberts1995-143 "#cite*note-FOOTNOTERoberts1995-143") \_Operation\* _Barbarossa_ forced the [Soviet supreme command](/wiki/Stavka "Stavka") to adopt [strategic defence](/wiki/Strategic_defence "Strategic defence"). During the summer, the Axis made significant gains into Soviet territory, inflicting immense losses in both personnel and materiel. By mid-August, however, the German [Army High Command](/wiki/Oberkommando_des_Heeres "Oberkommando des Heeres") decided to [suspend the offensive](</wiki/Battle_of_Smolensk*(1941)> "Battle of Smolensk (1941)") of a considerably depleted [Army Group Centre](/wiki/Army_Group_Centre "Army Group Centre"), and to divert the [2nd Panzer Group](/wiki/2nd_Panzer_Army "2nd Panzer Army") to reinforce troops advancing towards central Ukraine and Leningrad.\[[141]\](#cite\*note-FOOTNOTEWilt1981-144 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilt1981-144") The [Kiev offensive](</wiki/Battle_of_Kiev*(1941)> "Battle of Kiev (1941)") was overwhelmingly successful, resulting in encirclement and elimination of four Soviet armies, and made possible further [advance into Crimea](/wiki/Crimean_campaign "Crimean campaign") and industrially-developed Eastern Ukraine (the [First Battle of Kharkov](/wiki/First_Battle_of_Kharkov "First Battle of Kharkov")).\[[142]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEErickson2003114–137-145 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEErickson2003114–137-145")

[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/RIAN_archive_2153_After_bombing.jpg/250px-RIAN_archive_2153_After_bombing.jpg' alt='' title='' width='250' height='153' />](/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_2153_After_bombing.jpg "/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_2153_After_bombing.jpg")

Russian civilians leaving destroyed houses after a German bombardment during the [siege of Leningrad](/wiki/Siege_of_Leningrad "Siege of Leningrad") ([Saint Petersburg](/wiki/Saint_Petersburg "Saint Petersburg")), 10 December 1942

The diversion of three-quarters of the Axis troops and the majority of their air forces from France and the central Mediterranean to the [Eastern Front](</wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)> "Eastern Front (World War II)")\[[143]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGlantz20019-146 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGlantz20019-146") prompted the United Kingdom to reconsider its [grand strategy](/wiki/Grand_strategy "Grand strategy").\[[144]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFarrell1993-147 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFarrell1993-147") In July, the UK and the Soviet Union formed a [military alliance against Germany](/wiki/Anglo-Soviet_Agreement "Anglo-Soviet Agreement")\[[145]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeeble199029-148 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeeble199029-148") and in August, the United Kingdom and the United States jointly issued the [Atlantic Charter](/wiki/Atlantic_Charter "Atlantic Charter"), which outlined British and American goals for the post-war world.\[[146]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor2012220-149 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor2012220-149") In late August the British and Soviets [invaded neutral Iran](/wiki/Anglo-Soviet_invasion_of_Iran "Anglo-Soviet invasion of Iran") to secure the [Persian Corridor](/wiki/Persian_Corridor "Persian Corridor"), Iran's [oil fields](/wiki/Oil_fields "Oil fields"), and preempt any Axis advances through Iran toward the Baku oil fields or India.\[[147]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBueno_de_MesquitaSmithSiversonMorrow2003425-150 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBueno_de_MesquitaSmithSiversonMorrow2003425-150")

By October, Axis powers had achieved [operational objectives](/wiki/Operational_objective "Operational objective") in Ukraine and the Baltic region, with only the sieges of [Leningrad](/wiki/Siege_of_Leningrad "Siege of Leningrad")\[[148]\](#cite*note-FOOTNOTEKleinfeld1983-151 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKleinfeld1983-151") and [Sevastopol](</wiki/Siege_of_Sevastopol*(1941%E2%80%931942)> "Siege of Sevastopol (1941–1942)") continuing.\[[149]\](#cite*note-FOOTNOTEJukes2001113-152 "#cite*note-FOOTNOTEJukes2001113-152") A major [offensive against Moscow](/wiki/Battle_of_Moscow "Battle of Moscow") was renewed; after two months of fierce battles in increasingly harsh weather, the German army almost reached the outer suburbs of Moscow, where the exhausted troops\[[150]\](#cite_note-153 "#cite_note-153") were forced to suspend the offensive.\[[151]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReinhardt1992227-154 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReinhardt1992227-154") Large territorial gains were made by Axis forces, but their campaign had failed to achieve its main objectives: two key cities remained in Soviet hands, the Soviet [capability to resist](/wiki/Military_capability "Military capability") was not broken, and the Soviet Union retained a considerable part of its military potential. The \_blitzkrieg* [phase](</wiki/Phase*(combat)> "Phase (combat)") of the war in Europe had ended.\[[152]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMilward1964-155 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMilward1964-155")
