By early December, freshly mobilised [reserves](/wiki/Military_reserve_force "Military reserve force")\[[153]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTERotundo1986-156 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTERotundo1986-156") allowed the Soviets to achieve numerical parity with Axis troops.\[[154]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGlantz200126-157 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGlantz200126-157") This, as well as [intelligence data](/wiki/Richard_Sorge#Wartime_intelligence "Richard Sorge") which established that a minimal number of Soviet troops in the East would be sufficient to deter any attack by the Japanese [Kwantung Army](/wiki/Kwantung_Army "Kwantung Army"),\[[155]\](#cite_note-158 "#cite_note-158") allowed the Soviets to begin a [massive counter-offensive](/wiki/Winter_campaign_of_1941%E2%80%931942 "Winter campaign of 1941–1942") that started on 5 December all along the front and pushed German troops 100–250 kilometres (62–155 mi) west.\[[156]\](#cite_note-159 "#cite_note-159")

### War breaks out in the Pacific (1941)

Main article: [Pacific War](/wiki/Pacific_War "Pacific War")
[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/228_regiment_in_HK.jpg/250px-228_regiment_in_HK.jpg' alt='' title='' width='250' height='160' />](/wiki/File:228_regiment_in_HK.jpg "/wiki/File:228_regiment_in_HK.jpg")

Japanese soldiers [entering Hong Kong](/wiki/Battle_of_Hong_Kong "Battle of Hong Kong"), 8 December 1941

Following the Japanese [false flag](/wiki/False_flag "False flag") [Mukden incident](/wiki/Mukden_incident "Mukden incident") in 1931, the Japanese shelling of the American [gunboat _USS Panay_](/wiki/USS_Panay_incident "USS Panay incident") in 1937, and the 1937–1938 [Nanjing Massacre](/wiki/Nanjing_Massacre "Nanjing Massacre"), [Japanese-American relations deteriorated](/wiki/Japan%E2%80%93United_States_relations#1937%E2%80%931941 "Japan–United States relations"). In 1939, the United States notified Japan that it would not be extending its trade treaty and American public opinion opposing Japanese expansionism led to a series of economic sanctions—the [Export Control Acts](/wiki/Export_Control_Act "Export Control Act")—which banned US exports of chemicals, minerals and military parts to Japan, and increased economic pressure on the Japanese regime.\[[113]\](#cite\*note-ibiblio_1940-116 "#cite_note-ibiblio_1940-116")\[[157]\](#cite_note-160 "#cite_note-160")\[[158]\](#cite_note-ReferenceC-161 "#cite_note-ReferenceC-161") During 1939 Japan launched its [first attack against Changsha](</wiki/Battle_of_Changsha*(1939)> "Battle of Changsha (1939)"), but was repulsed by late September.\[[159]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJowettAndrew200214-162 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJowettAndrew200214-162") Despite [several offensives](/wiki/1939%E2%80%931940_Winter_Offensive "1939–1940 Winter Offensive") by both sides, by 1940 the war between China and Japan was at a stalemate. To increase pressure on China by blocking supply routes, and to better position Japanese forces in the event of a war with the Western powers, Japan invaded and [occupied northern Indochina](/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_French_Indochina "Japanese invasion of French Indochina") in September 1940.\[[160]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOveryWheatcroft1999289-163 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOveryWheatcroft1999289-163")

Chinese nationalist forces launched a large-scale [counter-offensive](/wiki/1939%E2%80%931940_Winter_Offensive "1939–1940 Winter Offensive") in early 1940. In August, [Chinese communists](/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Party "Chinese Communist Party") launched an [offensive in Central China](/wiki/Hundred_Regiments_Offensive "Hundred Regiments Offensive"); in retaliation, Japan instituted [harsh measures](/wiki/Three_Alls_policy "Three Alls policy") in occupied areas to reduce human and material resources for the communists.\[[161]\](#cite\*note-FOOTNOTEJoes2004224-164 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJoes2004224-164") Continued antipathy between Chinese communist and nationalist forces [culminated in armed clashes in January 1941](/wiki/New_Fourth_Army_incident "New Fourth Army incident"), effectively ending their co-operation.\[[162]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFairbankGoldman2006320-165 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFairbankGoldman2006320-165") In March, the Japanese 11th army attacked the headquarters of the Chinese 19th army but was repulsed during the [Battle of Shanggao](/wiki/Battle_of_Shanggao "Battle of Shanggao").\[[163]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHsuChang197130-166 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHsuChang197130-166") In September, Japan attempted to [take the city of Changsha](</wiki/Battle_of_Changsha*(1941)> "Battle of Changsha (1941)") again and clashed with Chinese nationalist forces.\[[164]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHsuChang197133-167 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHsuChang197133-167")

German successes in Europe prompted Japan to increase pressure on European governments in [Southeast Asia](/wiki/Southeast_Asia "Southeast Asia"). The Dutch government agreed to provide Japan with oil supplies from the [Dutch East Indies](/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies "Dutch East Indies"), but negotiations for additional access to their resources ended in failure in June 1941.\[[165]\](#cite_note-168 "#cite_note-168") In July 1941 Japan sent troops to southern Indochina, thus threatening British and Dutch possessions in the Far East. The United States, the United Kingdom, and other Western governments reacted to this move with a freeze on Japanese assets and a total oil [embargo](/wiki/Economic_sanctions "Economic sanctions").\[[166]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson1975201-169 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson1975201-169")\[[167]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvansPeattie2012456-170 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvansPeattie2012456-170") At the same time, Japan was [planning an invasion of the Soviet Far East](/wiki/Kantokuen "Kantokuen"), intending to take advantage of the German invasion in the west, but abandoned the operation after the sanctions.\[[168]\](#cite_note-171 "#cite_note-171")

Since early 1941, the United States and Japan had been engaged in negotiations in an attempt to improve their strained relations and end the war in China. During these negotiations, Japan advanced a number of proposals which were dismissed by the Americans as inadequate.\[[169]\](#cite_note-USAWWIIcp5-172 "#cite_note-USAWWIIcp5-172") At the same time the United States, the United Kingdom, and the Netherlands engaged in secret discussions for the joint defence of their territories, in the event of a Japanese attack against any of them.\[[170]\](#cite_note-USAWWIIcp4-173 "#cite_note-USAWWIIcp4-173") Roosevelt reinforced [the Philippines](/wiki/Commonwealth_of_the_Philippines "Commonwealth of the Philippines") (an American protectorate scheduled for independence in 1946) and warned Japan that the United States would react to Japanese attacks against any "neighboring countries".\[[170]\](#cite_note-USAWWIIcp4-173 "#cite_note-USAWWIIcp4-173")

[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/The_USS_Arizona_%28BB-39%29_burning_after_the_Japanese_attack_on_Pearl_Harbor_-_NARA_195617_-_Edit.jpg/250px-The_USS_Arizona_%28BB-39%29_burning_after_the_Japanese_attack_on_Pearl_Harbor_-_NARA_195617_-_Edit.jpg' alt='' title='' width='250' height='198' />](</wiki/File:The_USS_Arizona_(BB-39)_burning_after_the_Japanese_attack_on_Pearl_Harbor_-_NARA_195617_-_Edit.jpg> "/wiki/File:The_USS_Arizona_(BB-39)_burning_after_the_Japanese_attack_on_Pearl_Harbor_-_NARA_195617_-_Edit.jpg")

The [USS *Arizona*](/wiki/USS_Arizona "USS Arizona") was a total loss in the [Japanese surprise air attack](/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor "Attack on Pearl Harbor") on the [United States Pacific Fleet](/wiki/United_States_Pacific_Fleet "United States Pacific Fleet") at [Pearl Harbor](/wiki/Pearl_Harbor "Pearl Harbor"), Sunday 7 December 1941

Frustrated at the lack of progress and feeling the pinch of the American–British–Dutch sanctions, Japan prepared for war. Emperor [Hirohito](/wiki/Hirohito "Hirohito"), after initial hesitation about Japan's chances of victory,\[[171]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBix2000399–414-174 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBix2000399–414-174") began to favour Japan's entry into the war.\[[172]\](#cite_note-175 "#cite_note-175") As a result, Prime Minister [Fumimaro Konoe](/wiki/Fumimaro_Konoe "Fumimaro Konoe") resigned.\[[173]\](#cite_note-176 "#cite_note-176")\[[174]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBix2000417–420-177 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBix2000417–420-177") Hirohito refused the recommendation to appoint [Prince Naruhiko Higashikuni](/wiki/Prince_Naruhiko_Higashikuni "Prince Naruhiko Higashikuni") in his place, choosing War Minister [Hideki Tojo](/wiki/Hideki_Tojo "Hideki Tojo") instead.\[[175]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBix2000418-178 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBix2000418-178") On 3 November, Nagano explained in detail the plan of the [attack on Pearl Harbor](/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor "Attack on Pearl Harbor") to the Emperor.\[[176]\](#cite_note-179 "#cite_note-179") On 5 November, Hirohito approved in imperial conference the operations plan for the war.\[[177]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBix2000424-180 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBix2000424-180") On 20 November, the new government presented an interim proposal as its final offer. It called for the end of American aid to China and for lifting the embargo on the supply of oil and other resources to Japan. In exchange, Japan promised not to launch any attacks in Southeast Asia and to withdraw its forces from southern Indochina.\[[169]\](#cite_note-USAWWIIcp5-172 "#cite_note-USAWWIIcp5-172") The American counter-proposal of 26 November required that Japan evacuate all of China without conditions and conclude non-aggression pacts with all Pacific powers.\[[178]\](#cite_note-181 "#cite_note-181") That meant Japan was essentially forced to choose between abandoning its ambitions in China, or seizing the natural resources it needed in the Dutch East Indies by force;\[[179]\](#cite_note-182 "#cite_note-182")\[[180]\](#cite_note-183 "#cite_note-183") the Japanese military did not consider the former an option, and many officers considered the oil embargo an unspoken declaration of war.\[[181]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTELightbody2004125-184 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTELightbody2004125-184")

Japan planned to seize European colonies in Asia to create a large defensive perimeter stretching into the Central Pacific. The Japanese would then be free to exploit the resources of Southeast Asia while exhausting the over-stretched Allies by fighting a defensive war.\[[182]\](#cite*note-185 "#cite_note-185")\[[183]\](#cite_note-186 "#cite_note-186") To prevent American intervention while securing the perimeter, it was further planned to neutralise the [United States Pacific Fleet](/wiki/United_States_Pacific_Fleet "United States Pacific Fleet") and the American military presence in the Philippines from the outset.\[[184]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWood200711–12-187 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWood200711–12-187") On 7 December 1941 (8 December in Asian time zones), Japan attacked British and American holdings with near-simultaneous [offensives against Southeast Asia and the Central Pacific](</wiki/Japanese_expansion*(1941%E2%80%9342)> "Japanese expansion (1941–42)").\[[185]\](#cite*note-FOOTNOTEWohlstetter1962341–343-188 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWohlstetter1962341–343-188") These included an [attack on the American fleets at Pearl Harbor](/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor "Attack on Pearl Harbor") and [the Philippines](</wiki/Philippines_campaign*(1941%E2%80%931942)> "Philippines campaign (1941–1942)"), as well as invasions of [Guam](</wiki/Battle_of_Guam_(1941)> "Battle of Guam (1941)"), [Wake Island](/wiki/Battle_of_Wake_Island "Battle of Wake Island"), [Malaya](/wiki/Malayan_campaign "Malayan campaign"),\[[185]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWohlstetter1962341–343-188 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWohlstetter1962341–343-188") [Thailand](/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_Thailand "Japanese invasion of Thailand"), and [Hong Kong](/wiki/Battle_of_Hong_Kong "Battle of Hong Kong").\[[186]\](#cite_note-189 "#cite_note-189")

These attacks led the [United States](/wiki/United_States_declaration_of_war_on_Japan "United States declaration of war on Japan"), [United Kingdom](/wiki/United_Kingdom_declaration_of_war_on_Japan "United Kingdom declaration of war on Japan"), China, Australia, and several other states to formally declare war on Japan, whereas the Soviet Union, being heavily involved in large-scale hostilities with European Axis countries, maintained its neutrality agreement with Japan.\[[187]\](#cite_note-190 "#cite_note-190") Germany, followed by the other Axis states, declared war on the United States\[[188]\](#cite_note-191 "#cite_note-191") in solidarity with Japan, citing as justification the American attacks on German war vessels that had been ordered by Roosevelt.\[[135]\](#cite_note-Events1941-138 "#cite_note-Events1941-138")\[[189]\](#cite_note-192 "#cite_note-192")

### Axis advance stalls (1942–1943)

On 1 January 1942, the [Allied Big Four](/wiki/Four_Policemen "Four Policemen")\[[190]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBosworthMaiolo2015313–314-193 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBosworthMaiolo2015313–314-193")—the Soviet Union, China, the United Kingdom, and the United States—and 22 smaller or exiled governments issued the [Declaration by United Nations](/wiki/Declaration_by_United_Nations "Declaration by United Nations"), thereby affirming the [Atlantic Charter](/wiki/Atlantic_Charter "Atlantic Charter")\[[191]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMingstKarns200722-194 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMingstKarns200722-194") and agreeing not to sign a [separate peace](/wiki/Separate_peace "Separate peace") with the Axis powers.\[[192]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer1990904-195 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer1990904-195")

During 1942, Allied officials debated on the appropriate [grand strategy](/wiki/Grand_strategy "Grand strategy") to pursue. All agreed that [defeating Germany](/wiki/Europe_first "Europe first") was the primary objective. The Americans favoured a straightforward, [large-scale attack](/wiki/Operation_Sledgehammer "Operation Sledgehammer") on Germany through France. The Soviets demanded a second front. The British argued that military operations should target peripheral areas to wear out German strength, leading to increasing demoralisation, and bolstering resistance forces; Germany itself would be subject to a heavy bombing campaign. An offensive against Germany would then be launched primarily by Allied armour, without using large-scale armies.\[[193]\](#cite_note-196 "#cite_note-196") Eventually, the British persuaded the Americans that a landing in France was infeasible in 1942 and they should instead focus on driving the Axis out of North Africa.\[[194]\](#cite_note-197 "#cite_note-197")

At the [Casablanca Conference](/wiki/Casablanca_Conference "Casablanca Conference") in early 1943, the Allies reiterated the statements issued in the 1942 Declaration and demanded the [unconditional surrender](/wiki/Unconditional_surrender "Unconditional surrender") of their enemies. The British and Americans agreed to continue to press the initiative in the Mediterranean by invading Sicily to fully secure the Mediterranean supply routes.\[[195]\](#cite_note-198 "#cite_note-198") Although the British argued for further operations in the Balkans to bring Turkey into the war, in May 1943, the Americans extracted a British commitment to limit Allied operations in the Mediterranean to an invasion of the Italian mainland, and to invade France in 1944.\[[196]\](#cite_note-199 "#cite_note-199")

### Pacific (1942–1943)

[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Second_world_war_asia_1937-1942_map_en6.png/500px-Second_world_war_asia_1937-1942_map_en6.png' alt='' title='' width='350' height='269' />](/wiki/File:Second_world_war_asia_1937-1942_map_en6.png "/wiki/File:Second_world_war_asia_1937-1942_map_en6.png")

Map of Japanese military advances through mid-1942

By the end of April 1942, Japan and its ally [Thailand](/wiki/Thailand_in_World_War_II "Thailand in World War II") had almost conquered [Burma](/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_Burma "Japanese invasion of Burma"), [Malaya](/wiki/Malayan_campaign "Malayan campaign"), [the Dutch East Indies](/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies_campaign "Dutch East Indies campaign"), [Singapore](/wiki/Fall_of_Singapore "Fall of Singapore"), and [Rabaul](</wiki/Battle_of_Rabaul_(1942)> "Battle of Rabaul (1942)"), inflicting severe losses on Allied troops and taking a large number of prisoners.\[[197]\](#cite*note-FOOTNOTEBeevor2012247–267,\_345-200 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor2012247–267,\_345-200") Despite stubborn [resistance by Filipino and US forces](</wiki/Philippines_campaign*(1941%E2%80%931942)> "Philippines campaign (1941–1942)"), the [Philippine Commonwealth](/wiki/Commonwealth_of_the_Philippines "Commonwealth of the Philippines") was eventually captured in May 1942, forcing its government into exile.\[[198]\](#cite*note-FOOTNOTELewis1953p.*529*(Table*11)-201 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewis1953p.\_529*(Table_11)-201") On 16 April, in Burma, 7,000 British soldiers were encircled by the Japanese 33rd Division during the [Battle of Yenangyaung](/wiki/Battle_of_Yenangyaung "Battle of Yenangyaung") and rescued by the Chinese 38th Division.\[[199]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlim195671–74-202 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlim195671–74-202") Japanese forces also achieved naval victories in the [South China Sea](/wiki/Sinking_of_Prince_of_Wales_and_Repulse "Sinking of Prince of Wales and Repulse"), [Java Sea](/wiki/Battle_of_the_Java_Sea "Battle of the Java Sea"), and [Indian Ocean](/wiki/Indian_Ocean_raid "Indian Ocean raid"),\[[200]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrove1995362-203 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrove1995362-203") and [bombed the Allied naval base](/wiki/Bombing_of_Darwin "Bombing of Darwin") at [Darwin](/wiki/Darwin,_Northern_Territory "Darwin, Northern Territory"), Australia. In January 1942, the only Allied success against Japan was a Chinese [victory at Changsha](</wiki/Battle_of_Changsha*(1941%E2%80%931942)> "Battle of Changsha (1941–1942)").\[[201]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTECh'i1992158-204 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTECh'i1992158-204") These easy victories over the unprepared US and European opponents left Japan overconfident, and overextended.\[[202]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPerez1998145-205 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPerez1998145-205")

In early May 1942, Japan initiated operations to [capture Port Moresby](/wiki/Operation_Mo "Operation Mo") by [amphibious assault](/wiki/Amphibious_warfare "Amphibious warfare") and thus sever communications and supply lines between the United States and Australia. The planned invasion was thwarted when an Allied task force, centred on two American fleet carriers, fought Japanese naval forces to a draw in the [Battle of the Coral Sea](/wiki/Battle_of_the_Coral_Sea "Battle of the Coral Sea").\[[203]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaddox1992111–112-206 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaddox1992111–112-206") Japan's next plan, motivated by the earlier [Doolittle Raid](/wiki/Doolittle_Raid "Doolittle Raid"), was to seize [Midway Atoll](/wiki/Midway_Atoll "Midway Atoll") and lure American carriers into battle to be eliminated; as a diversion, Japan would also send forces to [occupy the Aleutian Islands](/wiki/Aleutian_Islands_campaign "Aleutian Islands campaign") in Alaska.\[[204]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTESalecker2001186-207 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTESalecker2001186-207") In mid-May, Japan started the [Zhejiang-Jiangxi campaign](/wiki/Zhejiang-Jiangxi_campaign "Zhejiang-Jiangxi campaign") in China, with the goal of inflicting retribution on the Chinese who aided the surviving American airmen in the Doolittle Raid by destroying Chinese air bases and fighting against the Chinese 23rd and 32nd Army Groups.\[[205]\](#cite_note-208 "#cite_note-208")\[[206]\](#cite_note-209 "#cite_note-209") In early June, Japan put its operations into action, but the Americans had broken [Japanese naval codes](/wiki/Japanese_naval_codes "Japanese naval codes") in late May and were fully aware of the plans and order of battle, and used this knowledge to achieve a decisive [victory at Midway](/wiki/Battle_of_Midway "Battle of Midway") over the [Imperial Japanese Navy](/wiki/Imperial_Japanese_Navy "Imperial Japanese Navy").\[[207]\](#cite_note-210 "#cite_note-210")

With its capacity for aggressive action greatly diminished as a result of the Midway battle, Japan attempted to capture [Port Moresby](/wiki/Port_Moresby "Port Moresby") by an [overland campaign](/wiki/Kokoda_Track_campaign "Kokoda Track campaign") in the [Territory of Papua](/wiki/Territory_of_Papua "Territory of Papua").\[[208]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeinberg2005339-211 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeinberg2005339-211") The Americans planned a counterattack against Japanese positions in the southern [Solomon Islands](/wiki/Solomon_Islands "Solomon Islands"), primarily [Guadalcanal](/wiki/Guadalcanal "Guadalcanal"), as a first step towards capturing [Rabaul](/wiki/Rabaul "Rabaul"), the main Japanese base in Southeast Asia.\[[209]\](#cite_note-212 "#cite_note-212")

Both plans started in July, but by mid-September, the [Battle for Guadalcanal](/wiki/Guadalcanal_campaign "Guadalcanal campaign") took priority for the Japanese, and troops in New Guinea were ordered to withdraw from the Port Moresby area to the [northern part of the island](/wiki/Oro_Province "Oro Province"), where they faced Australian and United States troops in the [Battle of Buna–Gona](/wiki/Battle_of_Buna%E2%80%93Gona "Battle of Buna–Gona").\[[210]\](#cite\*note-FOOTNOTESwain2001197-213 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTESwain2001197-213") Guadalcanal soon became a focal point for both sides with heavy commitments of troops and ships in the battle for Guadalcanal. By the start of 1943, the Japanese were defeated on the island and [withdrew their troops](/wiki/Operation_Ke "Operation Ke").\[[211]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHane2001340-214 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHane2001340-214") In Burma, Commonwealth forces mounted two operations. The first was a disastrous [offensive into the Arakan region](</wiki/Arakan_campaign*(1942%E2%80%931943)> "Arakan campaign (1942–1943)") in late 1942 that forced a retreat back to India by May 1943.\[[212]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarston2005111-215 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarston2005111-215") The second was the [insertion of irregular forces](/wiki/Operation_Longcloth "Operation Longcloth") behind Japanese frontlines in February which, by the end of April, had achieved mixed results.\[[213]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrayley20029-216 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrayley20029-216")

### Eastern Front (1942–1943)

[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/RIAN_archive_44732_Soviet_soldiers_attack_house.jpg/500px-RIAN_archive_44732_Soviet_soldiers_attack_house.jpg' alt='' title='' width='380' height='136' />](/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_44732_Soviet_soldiers_attack_house.jpg "/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_44732_Soviet_soldiers_attack_house.jpg")

[Red Army](/wiki/Red_Army "Red Army") soldiers on the counterattack during the [Battle of Stalingrad](/wiki/Battle_of_Stalingrad "Battle of Stalingrad"), February 1943

# \<<\<<\<<< HEAD Despite considerable losses, in early 1942 Germany and its allies stopped a major Soviet offensive in [central](/wiki/Central_Russia "Central Russia") and [southern Russia](/wiki/Southern_Russia "Southern Russia"), keeping most territorial gains they had achieved during the previous year.\[[214]\](#cite\*note-FOOTNOTEGlantz200131-217 "#cite*note-FOOTNOTEGlantz200131-217") In May, the Germans defeated Soviet offensives in the [Kerch Peninsula](/wiki/Battle_of_the_Kerch_Peninsula "Battle of the Kerch Peninsula") and at [Kharkov](/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Kharkov "Second Battle of Kharkov"),\[[215]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTERead2004764-218 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTERead2004764-218") and then in June 1942 launched their main [summer offensive](/wiki/Case_Blue "Case Blue") against southern Russia, to seize the [oil fields of the Caucasus](/wiki/Petroleum_industry_in_Azerbaijan "Petroleum industry in Azerbaijan") and occupy the [Kuban](/wiki/Kuban "Kuban") [steppe](/wiki/Steppe "Steppe"), while maintaining positions on the northern and central areas of the front. The Germans split [Army Group South](/wiki/Army_Group_South "Army Group South") into two groups: [Army Group A](/wiki/Army_Group_A "Army Group A") advanced to the lower [Don River](</wiki/Don*(river)> "Don (river)") and struck south-east to the Caucasus, while [Army Group B](/wiki/Army_Group_B "Army Group B") headed towards the [Volga River](/wiki/Volga "Volga"). The Soviets decided to make their stand at Stalingrad on the Volga.\[[216]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies2006p.\_100*(2008\*ed.)-219 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies2006p.\_100\*(2008_ed.)-219")

Despite considerable losses, in early 1942 Germany and its allies stopped a major Soviet offensive in [central](/wiki/Central_Russia "Central Russia") and [southern Russia](/wiki/Southern_Russia "Southern Russia"), keeping most territorial gains they had achieved during the previous year.\[[214]\](#cite\*note-FOOTNOTEGlantz200131-217 "#cite\*note-FOOTNOTEGlantz200131-217") In May, the Germans defeated Soviet offensives in the [Kerch Peninsula](/wiki/Battle_of_the_Kerch_Peninsula "Battle of the Kerch Peninsula") and at [Kharkov](/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Kharkov "Second Battle of Kharkov"),\[[215]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTERead2004764-218 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTERead2004764-218") and then in June 1942 launched their main [summer offensive](/wiki/Case_Blue "Case Blue") against southern Russia, to seize the [oil fields of the Caucasus](/wiki/Petroleum_industry_in_Azerbaijan "Petroleum industry in Azerbaijan") and occupy the [Kuban](/wiki/Kuban "Kuban") [steppe](/wiki/Steppe "Steppe"), while maintaining positions on the northern and central areas of the front. The Germans split [Army Group South](/wiki/Army_Group_South "Army Group South") into two groups: [Army Group A](/wiki/Army_Group_A "Army Group A") advanced to the lower [Don River](</wiki/Don*(river)> "Don (river)") and struck south-east to the Caucasus, while [Army Group B](/wiki/Army_Group_B "Army Group B") headed towards the [Volga River](/wiki/Volga "Volga"). The Soviets decided to make their stand at Stalingrad on the Volga.\[[216]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies2006p.\_100\*(2008\*ed.)-219 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies2006p.\_100\*(2008_ed.)-219")

> > > > > > > origin/main

By mid-November, the Germans had [nearly taken Stalingrad](/wiki/Battle_of_Stalingrad "Battle of Stalingrad") in bitter [street fighting](/wiki/Urban_warfare "Urban warfare"). The Soviets began their second winter counter-offensive, starting with an [encirclement of German forces at Stalingrad](/wiki/Operation_Uranus "Operation Uranus"),\[[217]\](#cite\*note-FOOTNOTEBeevor1998239–265-220 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor1998239–265-220") and an assault on the [Rzhev salient near Moscow](/wiki/Operation_Mars "Operation Mars"), though the latter failed disastrously.\[[218]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack2003119-221 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack2003119-221") By early February 1943, the German Army had taken tremendous losses; German troops at Stalingrad had been defeated,\[[219]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor1998383–391-222 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor1998383–391-222") and the front-line had been pushed back beyond its position before the summer offensive. In mid-February, after the Soviet push had tapered off, the Germans launched another [attack on Kharkov](/wiki/Third_Battle_of_Kharkov "Third Battle of Kharkov"), creating a [salient](</wiki/Salient*(military)> "Salient (military)") in their front line around the Soviet city of [Kursk](/wiki/Kursk "Kursk").\[[220]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEErickson2001142-223 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEErickson2001142-223")

### Western Europe/Atlantic and Mediterranean (1942–1943)

[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/8th_AF_Bombing_Marienburg.JPEG/250px-8th_AF_Bombing_Marienburg.JPEG' alt='' title='' width='250' height='201' />](/wiki/File:8th_AF_Bombing_Marienburg.JPEG "/wiki/File:8th_AF_Bombing_Marienburg.JPEG")

American [Eighth Air Force](/wiki/Eighth_Air_Force "Eighth Air Force") [Boeing B-17 Flying Fortress](/wiki/Boeing_B-17_Flying_Fortress "Boeing B-17 Flying Fortress") bombing raid on the Focke-Wulf factory in Germany, 9 October 1943

Exploiting poor American naval command decisions, [the German navy ravaged Allied shipping off the American Atlantic coast](/wiki/Second_Happy_Time "Second Happy Time").\[[221]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMilner199052-224 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMilner199052-224") By November 1941, Commonwealth forces had launched a counter-offensive in North Africa, [Operation Crusader](/wiki/Operation_Crusader "Operation Crusader"), and reclaimed all the gains the Germans and Italians had made.\[[222]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor2012224–228-225 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor2012224–228-225") The Germans also launched a North African offensive in January, pushing the British back to positions at the [Gazala line](/wiki/Battle_of_Gazala#Gazala_line "Battle of Gazala") by early February,\[[223]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMolinari200791-226 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMolinari200791-226") followed by a temporary lull in combat which Germany used to prepare for their upcoming offensives.\[[224]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMitcham200731-227 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMitcham200731-227") Concerns that the Japanese might use bases in [Vichy-held Madagascar](/wiki/French_Madagascar "French Madagascar") caused the British to [invade the island](/wiki/Battle_of_Madagascar "Battle of Madagascar") in early May 1942.\[[225]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor2012380–381-228 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor2012380–381-228") An Axis [offensive in Libya](/wiki/Battle_of_Gazala "Battle of Gazala") forced an Allied retreat deep inside Egypt until Axis forces were [stopped at El Alamein](/wiki/First_Battle_of_El_Alamein "First Battle of El Alamein").\[[226]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTERich1992178-229 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTERich1992178-229") On the Continent, raids of Allied [commandos](/wiki/Commando "Commando") on strategic targets, culminating in the failed [Dieppe Raid](/wiki/Dieppe_Raid "Dieppe Raid"),\[[227]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon2004129-230 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon2004129-230") demonstrated the Western Allies' inability to launch an invasion of continental Europe without much better preparation, equipment, and operational security.\[[228]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillands200560-231 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillands200560-231")

In August 1942, the Allies succeeded in repelling a [second attack against El Alamein](/wiki/Battle_of_Alam_el_Halfa "Battle of Alam el Halfa")\[[229]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeegan1997277-232 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeegan1997277-232") and, at a high cost, managed to [deliver desperately needed supplies to the besieged Malta](/wiki/Operation_Pedestal "Operation Pedestal").\[[230]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2002-233 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2002-233") A few months later, the Allies [commenced an attack of their own](/wiki/Second_Battle_of_El_Alamein "Second Battle of El Alamein") in Egypt, dislodging the Axis forces and beginning a drive west across Libya.\[[231]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomasAndrew19988-234 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomasAndrew19988-234") This attack was followed up shortly after by [Anglo-American landings in French North Africa](/wiki/Operation_Torch "Operation Torch"), which resulted in the region joining the Allies.\[[232]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoss199738-235 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoss199738-235") Hitler responded to the French colony's defection by ordering the [occupation of Vichy France](/wiki/Case_Anton "Case Anton");\[[232]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoss199738-235 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoss199738-235") although Vichy forces did not resist this violation of the armistice, they managed to [scuttle their fleet](/wiki/Scuttling_of_the_French_fleet_at_Toulon "Scuttling of the French fleet at Toulon") to prevent its capture by German forces.\[[232]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoss199738-235 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoss199738-235")\[[233]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBonnerBonner200124-236 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBonnerBonner200124-236") Axis forces in Africa withdrew into [Tunisia](/wiki/Tunisia "Tunisia"), which was [conquered by the Allies](/wiki/Tunisian_campaign "Tunisian campaign") in May 1943.\[[232]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoss199738-235 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoss199738-235")\[[234]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollier200311-237 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollier200311-237")

In June 1943, the British and Americans began [a strategic bombing campaign](/wiki/Combined_Bomber_Offensive "Combined Bomber Offensive") against Germany with a goal to disrupt the war economy, reduce morale, and "[de-house](/wiki/Dehousing "Dehousing")" the civilian population.\[[235]\](#cite_note-238 "#cite_note-238") The [firebombing of Hamburg](/wiki/Bombing_of_Hamburg_in_World_War_II "Bombing of Hamburg in World War II") was among the first attacks in this campaign, inflicting significant casualties and considerable losses on infrastructure of this important industrial centre.\[[236]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOvery1995119–120-239 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOvery1995119–120-239")

### Allies gain momentum (1943–1944)

[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/SBD_VB-16_over_USS_Washington_1943.jpg/250px-SBD_VB-16_over_USS_Washington_1943.jpg' alt='' title='' width='250' height='195' />](/wiki/File:SBD_VB-16_over_USS_Washington_1943.jpg "/wiki/File:SBD_VB-16_over_USS_Washington_1943.jpg")

[US Navy](/wiki/United_States_Navy "United States Navy") [SBD-5](/wiki/Douglas_SBD_Dauntless "Douglas SBD Dauntless") [scout plane](/wiki/Scout_plane "Scout plane") flying patrol over [USS *Washington*](</wiki/USS_Washington_(BB-56)> "USS Washington (BB-56)") and [USS *Lexington*](</wiki/USS_Lexington_(CV-16)> "USS Lexington (CV-16)") during the [Gilbert and Marshall Islands campaign](/wiki/Gilbert_and_Marshall_Islands_campaign "Gilbert and Marshall Islands campaign"), 1943

After the Guadalcanal campaign, the Allies initiated several operations against Japan in the Pacific. In May 1943, Canadian and US forces were sent to [eliminate Japanese forces from the Aleutians](/wiki/Aleutian_Islands_campaign#Allied_response "Aleutian Islands campaign").\[[237]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThompsonRandall2008164-240 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThompsonRandall2008164-240") Soon after, the United States, with support from Australia, New Zealand and Pacific Islander forces, began major ground, sea and air operations to [isolate Rabaul by capturing surrounding islands](/wiki/Operation_Cartwheel "Operation Cartwheel"), and [breach the Japanese Central Pacific perimeter at the Gilbert and Marshall Islands](/wiki/Gilbert_and_Marshall_Islands_campaign "Gilbert and Marshall Islands campaign").\[[238]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy2001610-241 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy2001610-241") By the end of March 1944, the Allies had completed both of these objectives and had also [neutralised the major Japanese base at Truk](/wiki/Operation_Hailstone "Operation Hailstone") in the [Caroline Islands](/wiki/Caroline_Islands "Caroline Islands"). In April, the Allies launched an operation to [retake Western New Guinea](/wiki/Western_New_Guinea_campaign "Western New Guinea campaign").\[[239]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTERottman2002228-242 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTERottman2002228-242")

In the Soviet Union, both the Germans and the Soviets spent the spring and early summer of 1943 preparing for large offensives in [central Russia](/wiki/Central_Russia "Central Russia"). On 5 July 1943, Germany [attacked Soviet forces around the Kursk Bulge](/wiki/Battle_of_Kursk "Battle of Kursk"). Within a week, German forces had exhausted themselves against the Soviets' well-constructed defences,\[[240]\](#cite_note-243 "#cite_note-243") and for the first time in the war, Hitler cancelled an operation before it had achieved tactical or operational success.\[[241]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2001592-244 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2001592-244") This decision was partially affected by the Western Allies' [invasion of Sicily](/wiki/Allied_invasion_of_Sicily "Allied invasion of Sicily") launched on 9 July, which, combined with previous Italian failures, resulted in the [ousting and arrest of Mussolini](/wiki/Fall_of_the_Fascist_regime_in_Italy "Fall of the Fascist regime in Italy") later that month.\[[242]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEO'Reilly200132-245 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEO'Reilly200132-245")

On 12 July 1943, the Soviets launched their own [counter-offensives](/wiki/Operation_Kutuzov "Operation Kutuzov"), thereby dispelling any chance of German victory or even stalemate in the east. The Soviet victory at Kursk marked the end of German superiority,\[[243]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBellamy2007595-246 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBellamy2007595-246") giving the Soviet Union the initiative on the Eastern Front.\[[244]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEO'Reilly200135-247 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEO'Reilly200135-247")\[[245]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHealy199290-248 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHealy199290-248") The Germans tried to stabilise their eastern front along the hastily fortified [Panther–Wotan line](/wiki/Panther%E2%80%93Wotan_line "Panther–Wotan line"), but the Soviets broke through it at [Smolensk](/wiki/Smolensk_operation "Smolensk operation") and the [Lower Dnieper Offensive](/wiki/Battle_of_the_Dnieper "Battle of the Dnieper").\[[246]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGlantz200150–55-249 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGlantz200150–55-249")

On 3 September 1943, the Western Allies [invaded the Italian mainland](/wiki/Allied_invasion_of_Italy "Allied invasion of Italy"), following [Italy's armistice with the Allies](/wiki/Armistice_of_Cassibile "Armistice of Cassibile") and the ensuing German occupation of Italy.\[[247]\](#cite_note-250 "#cite_note-250") Germany, with the help of fascists, responded to the armistice by [disarming Italian forces](/wiki/Operation_Achse "Operation Achse") that were in many places without superior orders, seizing military control of Italian areas,\[[248]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMazower2008362-251 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMazower2008362-251") and creating a series of defensive lines.\[[249]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHartHartHughes2000151-252 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHartHartHughes2000151-252") German special forces then [rescued Mussolini](/wiki/Gran_Sasso_raid "Gran Sasso raid"), who then soon established a new client state in German-occupied Italy named the [Italian Social Republic](/wiki/Italian_Social_Republic "Italian Social Republic"),\[[250]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlinkhorn200652-253 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlinkhorn200652-253") causing an [Italian civil war](/wiki/Italian_Civil_War "Italian Civil War"). The Western Allies fought through several lines until reaching the [main German defensive line](/wiki/Winter_Line "Winter Line") in mid-November.\[[251]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReadFisher2002129-254 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReadFisher2002129-254")

[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Soviet_troops_and_T-34_tanks_counterattacking_Kursk_Voronezh_Front_July_1943.jpg/250px-Soviet_troops_and_T-34_tanks_counterattacking_Kursk_Voronezh_Front_July_1943.jpg' alt='' title='' width='250' height='141' />](/wiki/File:Soviet_troops_and_T-34_tanks_counterattacking_Kursk_Voronezh_Front_July_1943.jpg "/wiki/File:Soviet_troops_and_T-34_tanks_counterattacking_Kursk_Voronezh_Front_July_1943.jpg")

[Red Army](/wiki/Red_Army "Red Army") troops in a counter-offensive on German positions at the [Battle of Kursk](/wiki/Battle_of_Kursk "Battle of Kursk"), July 1943

German operations in the Atlantic also suffered. By [May 1943, as Allied counter-measures became increasingly effective](</wiki/Black_May_(1943)> "Black May (1943)"), the resulting sizeable German submarine losses forced a temporary halt of the German Atlantic naval campaign.\[[252]\](#cite_note-255 "#cite_note-255") In November 1943, [Franklin D. Roosevelt](/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt "Franklin D. Roosevelt") and Winston Churchill met with [Chiang Kai-shek](/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek "Chiang Kai-shek") [in Cairo](/wiki/Cairo_Conference "Cairo Conference") and then with Joseph Stalin [in Tehran](/wiki/Tehran_Conference "Tehran Conference").\[[253]\](#cite_note-Kolko_1990_211,235,267_268-256 "#cite_note-Kolko_1990_211,235,267_268-256") The former conference determined the post-war return of Japanese territory\[[254]\](#cite_note-Iriye_1981_154-257 "#cite_note-Iriye_1981_154-257") and the military planning for the [Burma campaign](/wiki/Burma_campaign "Burma campaign"),\[[255]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMitter2014286-258 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMitter2014286-258") while the latter included agreement that the Western Allies would invade Europe in 1944 and that the Soviet Union would declare war on Japan within three months of Germany's defeat.\[[256]\](#cite_note-polley148-259 "#cite_note-polley148-259")

From November 1943, during the seven-week [Battle of Changde](/wiki/Battle_of_Changde "Battle of Changde"), the Chinese awaited allied relief as they forced Japan to fight a costly war of attrition.\[[257]\](#cite_note-Beevor_2012_268_274-260 "#cite_note-Beevor_2012_268_274-260")\[[258]\](#cite_note-H161-261 "#cite_note-H161-261")\[[259]\](#cite_note-Hsu_Chang_412-416-262 "#cite_note-Hsu_Chang_412-416-262") In January 1944, the Allies launched a [series of attacks in Italy against the line at Monte Cassino](/wiki/Battle_of_Monte_Cassino "Battle of Monte Cassino") and tried to outflank it with [landings at Anzio](/wiki/Battle_of_Anzio "Battle of Anzio").\[[260]\](#cite_note-263 "#cite_note-263")

On 27 January 1944, [Soviet](/wiki/Leningrad_Front "Leningrad Front") troops launched [a major offensive](/wiki/Siege_of_Leningrad#Soviet_relief_of_the_siege "Siege of Leningrad") that expelled German forces from the [Leningrad region](/wiki/Leningrad_Oblast "Leningrad Oblast"), thereby ending the [most lethal siege in history](/wiki/List_of_battles_by_casualties#Sieges_and_urban_combat "List of battles by casualties").\[[261]\](#cite\*note-Glantz_2002_327_366-264 "#cite_note-Glantz_2002_327_366-264") The [following Soviet offensive](/wiki/Leningrad%E2%80%93Novgorod_offensive "Leningrad–Novgorod offensive") was [halted on the pre-war Estonian border](</wiki/Battle_of_Narva*(1944)> "Battle of Narva (1944)") by the German [Army Group North](/wiki/Army_Group_North "Army Group North") aided by [Estonians](/wiki/German_occupation_of_Estonia_during_World_War_II#Estonians_in_Nazi_German_military_units "German occupation of Estonia during World War II") hoping to [re-establish national independence](/wiki/Estonian_government-in-exile#Failure_to_reestablish_independence "Estonian government-in-exile"). This delay slowed subsequent Soviet operations in the [Baltic Sea](/wiki/Baltic_Sea "Baltic Sea") region.\[[262]\](#cite_note-Glantz_2002_367_414-265 "#cite_note-Glantz_2002_367_414-265") By late May 1944, the Soviets had [liberated Crimea](/wiki/Crimean_offensive "Crimean offensive"), [largely expelled Axis forces from Ukraine](/wiki/Dnieper%E2%80%93Carpathian_offensive "Dnieper–Carpathian offensive"), and made [incursions into Romania](/wiki/First_Jassy%E2%80%93Kishinev_offensive "First Jassy–Kishinev offensive"), which were repulsed by the Axis troops.\[[263]\](#cite_note-Chubarov_2001_122-266 "#cite_note-Chubarov_2001_122-266") The Allied offensives in Italy had succeeded and, at the expense of allowing several German divisions to retreat, Rome was captured on 4 June.\[[264]\](#cite_note-267 "#cite_note-267")

The Allies had mixed success in mainland Asia. In March 1944, the Japanese launched the first of two invasions, [an operation against Allied positions in Assam, India](/wiki/Operation_U-Go "Operation U-Go"),\[[265]\](#cite\*note-Lightbody_2004_224-268 "#cite_note-Lightbody_2004_224-268") and soon besieged Commonwealth positions at [Imphal](/wiki/Battle_of_Imphal "Battle of Imphal") and [Kohima](/wiki/Battle_of_Kohima "Battle of Kohima").\[[266]\](#cite_note-Zeiler-269 "#cite_note-Zeiler-269") In May 1944, British and Indian forces mounted a counter-offensive that drove Japanese troops back to Burma by July,\[[266]\](#cite_note-Zeiler-269 "#cite_note-Zeiler-269") and Chinese forces that had [invaded northern Burma](/wiki/Battle_of_Northern_Burma_and_Western_Yunnan "Battle of Northern Burma and Western Yunnan") in late 1943 [besieged Japanese troops](/wiki/Siege_of_Myitkyina "Siege of Myitkyina") in [Myitkyina](/wiki/Myitkyina "Myitkyina").\[[267]\](#cite_note-270 "#cite_note-270") The [second Japanese invasion](/wiki/Operation_Ichi-Go "Operation Ichi-Go") of China aimed to destroy China's main fighting forces, secure railways between Japanese-held territory and capture Allied airfields.\[[268]\](#cite_note-271 "#cite_note-271") By June, the Japanese had conquered the province of [Henan](/wiki/Henan "Henan") and begun a [new attack on Changsha](</wiki/Battle_of_Changsha*(1944)> "Battle of Changsha (1944)").\[[269]\](#cite_note-272 "#cite_note-272")

### Allies close in (1944)

[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Approaching_Omaha.jpg/250px-Approaching_Omaha.jpg' alt='' title='' width='250' height='179' />](/wiki/File:Approaching_Omaha.jpg "/wiki/File:Approaching_Omaha.jpg")

American troops approaching [Omaha Beach](/wiki/Omaha_Beach "Omaha Beach") during the [invasion of Normandy](/wiki/Operation_Overlord "Operation Overlord") on [D-Day](/wiki/Normandy_landings "Normandy landings"), 6 June 1944

On 6 June 1944 (commonly known as [D-Day](/wiki/Normandy_landings "Normandy landings")), after three years of Soviet pressure,\[[270]\](#cite_note-rees406-273 "#cite_note-rees406-273") the Western Allies [invaded northern France](/wiki/Operation_Overlord "Operation Overlord"). After reassigning several Allied divisions from Italy, they also [attacked southern France](/wiki/Operation_Dragoon "Operation Dragoon").\[[271]\](#cite_note-Weinberg_2005_695-274 "#cite_note-Weinberg_2005_695-274") These landings were successful and led to the defeat of the [German Army units in France](/wiki/Falaise_pocket "Falaise pocket"). [Paris](/wiki/Paris "Paris") was [liberated](/wiki/Liberation_of_Paris "Liberation of Paris") on 25 August by the [local resistance](/wiki/French_Resistance "French Resistance") assisted by the [Free French Forces](/wiki/Free_French_Forces "Free French Forces"), both led by General [Charles de Gaulle](/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle "Charles de Gaulle"),\[[272]\](#cite_note-275 "#cite_note-275") and the Western Allies continued to [push back German forces](/wiki/Siegfried_Line_campaign "Siegfried Line campaign") in western Europe during the latter part of the year. An attempt to advance into northern Germany spearheaded by [a major airborne operation](/wiki/Operation_Market_Garden "Operation Market Garden") in the Netherlands failed.\[[273]\](#cite_note-276 "#cite_note-276") After that, the Western Allies slowly pushed into Germany, but [failed to cross the Ruhr river](/wiki/Operation_Queen "Operation Queen"). In Italy, the Allied advance slowed due to the [last major German defensive line](/wiki/Gothic_Line "Gothic Line").\[[274]\](#cite_note-277 "#cite_note-277")

On 22 June, the Soviets launched a strategic offensive in Belarus ("[Operation Bagration](/wiki/Operation_Bagration "Operation Bagration")") that nearly destroyed the German [Army Group Centre](/wiki/Army_Group_Centre "Army Group Centre").\[[275]\](#cite\*note-Zaloga_1996_7-278 "#cite_note-Zaloga_1996_7-278") Soon after that, [another Soviet strategic offensive](/wiki/Lvov%E2%80%93Sandomierz_offensive "Lvov–Sandomierz offensive") forced German troops from Western Ukraine and Eastern Poland. The Soviets formed the [Polish Committee of National Liberation](/wiki/Polish_Committee_of_National_Liberation "Polish Committee of National Liberation") to control territory in Poland and combat the Polish [Armia Krajowa](/wiki/Home_Army "Home Army"); the Soviet Red Army remained in the [Praga](/wiki/Praga "Praga") district on the other side of the [Vistula](/wiki/Vistula "Vistula") and watched passively as the Germans quelled the [Warsaw Uprising](/wiki/Warsaw_Uprising "Warsaw Uprising") initiated by the Armia Krajowa.\[[276]\](#cite_note-279 "#cite_note-279") The [national uprising](/wiki/Slovak_National_Uprising "Slovak National Uprising") in [Slovakia](</wiki/Slovak_Republic*(1939%E2%80%931945)> "Slovak Republic (1939–1945)") was also quelled by the Germans.\[[277]\](#cite_note-280 "#cite_note-280") The Soviet [Red Army](/wiki/Red_Army "Red Army")'s [strategic offensive in eastern Romania](/wiki/Second_Jassy%E2%80%93Kishinev_offensive "Second Jassy–Kishinev offensive") cut off and destroyed the [considerable German troops there](/wiki/Army_Group_South_Ukraine "Army Group South Ukraine") and triggered [a successful coup d'état in Romania](/wiki/1944_Romanian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat "1944 Romanian coup d'état") and [in Bulgaria](/wiki/1944_Bulgarian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat "1944 Bulgarian coup d'état"), followed by those countries' shift to the Allied side.\[[278]\](#cite_note-countrystudies.us-281 "#cite_note-countrystudies.us-281")

[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Douglas_MacArthur_lands_Leyte1.jpg/250px-Douglas_MacArthur_lands_Leyte1.jpg' alt='' title='' width='250' height='187' />](/wiki/File:Douglas_MacArthur_lands_Leyte1.jpg "/wiki/File:Douglas_MacArthur_lands_Leyte1.jpg")

[General](</wiki/General_(United_States)> "General (United States)") [Douglas MacArthur](/wiki/Douglas_MacArthur "Douglas MacArthur") returns to the [Philippines](/wiki/Commonwealth_of_the_Philippines "Commonwealth of the Philippines") during the [Battle of Leyte](/wiki/Battle_of_Leyte "Battle of Leyte"), 20 October 1944

In September 1944, Soviet troops advanced into [Yugoslavia](/wiki/Democratic_Federal_Yugoslavia "Democratic Federal Yugoslavia") and forced the rapid withdrawal of German Army Groups [E](/wiki/Army_Group_E "Army Group E") and [F](/wiki/Army_Group_F "Army Group F") in [Greece](/wiki/Axis_occupation_of_Greece "Axis occupation of Greece"), [Albania](/wiki/German_occupation_of_Albania "German occupation of Albania"), and Yugoslavia to rescue them from being cut off.\[[279]\](#cite_note-Evans_2008_653-282 "#cite_note-Evans_2008_653-282") By this point, the communist-led [Partisans](/wiki/Yugoslav_Partisans "Yugoslav Partisans") under Marshal [Josip Broz Tito](/wiki/Josip_Broz_Tito "Josip Broz Tito"), who had led an [increasingly successful guerrilla campaign](/wiki/World_War_II_in_Yugoslavia "World War II in Yugoslavia") against the occupation since 1941, controlled much of the territory of Yugoslavia and engaged in delaying efforts against German forces further south. In northern [Serbia](/wiki/Territory_of_the_Military_Commander_in_Serbia "Territory of the Military Commander in Serbia"), the Soviet [Red Army](/wiki/Red_Army "Red Army"), with limited support from Bulgarian forces, assisted the Partisans in a joint [liberation of the capital city of Belgrade](/wiki/Belgrade_offensive "Belgrade offensive") on 20 October. A few days later, the Soviets launched a [massive assault](/wiki/Budapest_offensive "Budapest offensive") against [German-occupied](/wiki/Operation_Panzerfaust "Operation Panzerfaust") Hungary that lasted until [the fall of Budapest](/wiki/Siege_of_Budapest "Siege of Budapest") in February 1945.\[[280]\](#cite_note-283 "#cite_note-283") Unlike impressive Soviet victories in the Balkans, [bitter Finnish resistance](/wiki/Continuation_War "Continuation War") to the [Soviet offensive](/wiki/Vyborg%E2%80%93Petrozavodsk_offensive "Vyborg–Petrozavodsk offensive") in the [Karelian Isthmus](/wiki/Karelian_Isthmus "Karelian Isthmus") denied the Soviets occupation of Finland and led to a [Soviet-Finnish armistice](/wiki/Moscow_Armistice "Moscow Armistice") on relatively mild conditions,\[[281]\](#cite_note-284 "#cite_note-284") although Finland was forced to [fight their former German allies](/wiki/Lapland_War "Lapland War").\[[282]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer19901085-285 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer19901085-285")

By the start of July 1944, Commonwealth forces in Southeast Asia had repelled the Japanese sieges in [Assam](/wiki/Assam "Assam"), pushing the Japanese back to the [Chindwin River](/wiki/Chindwin_River "Chindwin River")\[[283]\](#cite\*note-Marston_2005_120-286 "#cite_note-Marston_2005_120-286") while the Chinese captured Myitkyina. In September 1944, Chinese forces [captured Mount Song](/wiki/Battle_of_Mount_Song "Battle of Mount Song") and reopened the [Burma Road](/wiki/Burma_Road "Burma Road").\[[284]\](#cite_note-287 "#cite_note-287") In China, the Japanese had more successes, having finally [captured Changsha](</wiki/Battle_of_Changsha*(1944)> "Battle of Changsha (1944)") in mid-June and the city of [Hengyang](/wiki/Battle_of_Hengyang "Battle of Hengyang") by early August.\[[285]\](#cite_note-288 "#cite_note-288") Soon after, they invaded the province of [Guangxi](/wiki/Guangxi "Guangxi"), winning major engagements against Chinese forces at [Guilin and Liuzhou](/wiki/Battle_of_Guilin%E2%80%93Liuzhou "Battle of Guilin–Liuzhou") by the end of November\[[286]\](#cite_note-289 "#cite_note-289") and successfully linking up their forces in China and Indochina by mid-December.\[[287]\](#cite_note-Drea_2003_54-290 "#cite_note-Drea_2003_54-290")

In the Pacific, US forces continued to push back the Japanese perimeter. In mid-June 1944, they began their [offensive against the Mariana and Palau islands](/wiki/Mariana_and_Palau_Islands_campaign "Mariana and Palau Islands campaign") and decisively defeated Japanese forces in the [Battle of the Philippine Sea](/wiki/Battle_of_the_Philippine_Sea "Battle of the Philippine Sea"). These defeats led to the resignation of the Japanese Prime Minister, [Hideki Tojo](/wiki/Hideki_Tojo "Hideki Tojo"), and provided the United States with air bases to launch intensive heavy bomber attacks on the Japanese home islands. In late October, American forces [invaded the Filipino island of Leyte](/wiki/Battle_of_Leyte "Battle of Leyte"); soon after, Allied naval forces scored another large victory in the [Battle of Leyte Gulf](/wiki/Battle_of_Leyte_Gulf "Battle of Leyte Gulf"), one of the largest naval battles in history.\[[288]\](#cite_note-291 "#cite_note-291")

### Axis collapse and Allied victory (1944–1945)

[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Yalta_Conference_%28Churchill%2C_Roosevelt%2C_Stalin%29_%28B%26W%29.jpg/250px-Yalta_Conference_%28Churchill%2C_Roosevelt%2C_Stalin%29_%28B%26W%29.jpg' alt='' title='' width='250' height='206' />](</wiki/File:Yalta_Conference_(Churchill,_Roosevelt,_Stalin)_(B%26W).jpg> "/wiki/File:Yalta_Conference_(Churchill,_Roosevelt,_Stalin)_(B%26W).jpg")

[Yalta Conference](/wiki/Yalta_Conference "Yalta Conference") held in February 1945, with [Winston Churchill](/wiki/Winston_Churchill "Winston Churchill"), [Franklin D. Roosevelt](/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt "Franklin D. Roosevelt"), and [Joseph Stalin](/wiki/Joseph_Stalin "Joseph Stalin")

On 16 December 1944, Germany made a last attempt to split the Allies on the Western Front by using most of its remaining reserves to launch [a massive counter-offensive in the Ardennes](/wiki/Battle_of_the_Bulge "Battle of the Bulge") and [along the French-German border](</wiki/Operation_Northwind_(1944)> "Operation Northwind (1944)"), hoping to encircle large portions of Western Allied troops and prompt a political settlement after capturing their primary supply port at [Antwerp](/wiki/Antwerp "Antwerp"). By 16 January 1945, this offensive had been repulsed with no strategic objectives fulfilled.\[[289]\](#cite_note-parkerxiii-292 "#cite_note-parkerxiii-292") In Italy, the Western Allies remained stalemated at the German defensive line. In mid-January 1945, the Red Army attacked in Poland, [pushing from the Vistula to the Oder](/wiki/Vistula%E2%80%93Oder_offensive "Vistula–Oder offensive") river in Germany, and [overran East Prussia](/wiki/East_Prussian_offensive "East Prussian offensive").\[[290]\](#cite_note-293 "#cite_note-293") On 4 February Soviet, British, and US leaders met for the [Yalta Conference](/wiki/Yalta_Conference "Yalta Conference"). They agreed on the occupation of post-war Germany, and on when the Soviet Union would join the war against Japan.\[[291]\](#cite_note-294 "#cite_note-294")

In February, the Soviets [entered Silesia](/wiki/Silesian_offensives "Silesian offensives") and [Pomerania](/wiki/East_Pomeranian_offensive "East Pomeranian offensive"), while the [Western Allies entered western Germany](/wiki/Western_Allied_invasion_of_Germany "Western Allied invasion of Germany") and closed to the [Rhine](/wiki/Rhine "Rhine") river. By March, the Western Allies crossed the Rhine [north](/wiki/Operation_Plunder "Operation Plunder") and [south](/wiki/Remagen "Remagen") of the [Ruhr](</wiki/Ruhr_(river)> "Ruhr (river)"), [encircling the German Army Group B](/wiki/Ruhr_pocket "Ruhr pocket").\[[292]\](#cite\*note-295 "#cite_note-295") In early March, in an attempt to protect its last oil reserves in Hungary and retake Budapest, Germany launched [its last major offensive](/wiki/Operation_Spring_Awakening "Operation Spring Awakening") against Soviet troops near [Lake Balaton](/wiki/Lake_Balaton "Lake Balaton"). Within two weeks, the offensive had been repulsed, the Soviets advanced to [Vienna](/wiki/Vienna_offensive "Vienna offensive"), and captured the city. In early April, Soviet troops [captured Königsberg](/wiki/Battle_of_K%C3%B6nigsberg "Battle of Königsberg"), while the Western Allies finally [pushed forward in Italy](/wiki/Spring_1945_offensive_in_Italy "Spring 1945 offensive in Italy") and swept across western Germany capturing [Hamburg](/wiki/Capture_of_Hamburg "Capture of Hamburg") and [Nuremberg](</wiki/Battle_of_Nuremberg*(1945)> "Battle of Nuremberg (1945)"). [American and Soviet forces met at the Elbe river](/wiki/Elbe_Day "Elbe Day") on 25 April, leaving unoccupied pockets in southern Germany and around Berlin.

Soviet troops [stormed and captured Berlin](/wiki/Battle_of_Berlin "Battle of Berlin") in late April.\[[293]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2001793–829-296 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2001793–829-296") In Italy, [German forces surrendered](/wiki/Surrender_of_Caserta "Surrender of Caserta") on 29 April, while the [Italian Social Republic](/wiki/Italian_Social_Republic "Italian Social Republic") capitulated two days later. On 30 April, the [Reichstag](/wiki/Reichstag_building "Reichstag building") was captured, signalling the military defeat of Nazi Germany.\[[294]\](#cite_note-Shepardson_1998-297 "#cite_note-Shepardson_1998-297")

Major changes in leadership occurred on both sides during this period. On 12 April, President Roosevelt died and was succeeded by his vice president, [Harry S. Truman](/wiki/Harry_S._Truman "Harry S. Truman").\[[295]\](#cite*note-298 "#cite_note-298") Benito Mussolini [was killed](/wiki/Death_of_Benito_Mussolini "Death of Benito Mussolini") by [Italian partisans](/wiki/Italian_resistance_movement "Italian resistance movement") on 28 April.\[[296]\](#cite_note-O'Reilly_2001_244-299 "#cite_note-O'Reilly_2001_244-299") On 30 April, [Hitler committed suicide](/wiki/Death_of_Adolf_Hitler "Death of Adolf Hitler") in his [headquarters](/wiki/F%C3%BChrerbunker "Führerbunker"), and was succeeded by [Grand Admiral](/wiki/Grand_Admiral "Grand Admiral") [Karl Dönitz](/wiki/Karl_D%C3%B6nitz "Karl Dönitz") (as [President of the Reich](</wiki/President_of_Germany*(1919%E2%80%931945)> "President of Germany (1919–1945)")) and [Joseph Goebbels](/wiki/Joseph_Goebbels "Joseph Goebbels") (as [Chancellor of the Reich](/wiki/Chancellor_of_the_Reich "Chancellor of the Reich")); Goebbels also committed suicide on the following day and was replaced by [Lutz Graf Schwerin von Krosigk](/wiki/Lutz_Graf_Schwerin_von_Krosigk "Lutz Graf Schwerin von Krosigk"), in what would later be known as the [Flensburg Government](/wiki/Flensburg_Government "Flensburg Government"). [Total and unconditional surrender](/wiki/German_Instrument_of_Surrender "German Instrument of Surrender") in Europe was signed [on 7 and 8 May](/wiki/Victory_in_Europe_Day "Victory in Europe Day"), to be effective by the end of [8 May](</wiki/Victory_Day_(9_May)> "Victory Day (9 May)").\[[297]\](#cite*note-Evans_2008_737-300 "#cite_note-Evans_2008_737-300") German Army Group Centre [resisted in Prague](/wiki/Prague_offensive "Prague offensive") until 11 May.\[[298]\](#cite_note-Glantz_1998_34-301 "#cite_note-Glantz_1998_34-301") On 23 May all remaining members of the German government were arrested by the Allied Forces in [Flensburg](/wiki/Flensburg "Flensburg"), while on 5 June all German political and military institutions were transferred under the control of the Allies through the [Berlin Declaration](</wiki/Berlin_Declaration*(1945)> "Berlin Declaration (1945)").\[[299]\](#cite_note-302 "#cite_note-302")

In the Pacific theatre, American forces accompanied by the forces of the [Philippine Commonwealth](/wiki/Commonwealth_of_the_Philippines "Commonwealth of the Philippines") advanced [in the Philippines](</wiki/Philippines_campaign_(1944%E2%80%931945)> "Philippines campaign (1944–1945)"), [clearing Leyte](/wiki/Battle_of_Leyte "Battle of Leyte") by the end of April 1945. They [landed on Luzon](/wiki/Battle_of_Luzon "Battle of Luzon") in January 1945 and [recaptured Manila](</wiki/Battle_of_Manila_(1945)> "Battle of Manila (1945)") in March. Fighting continued on Luzon, [Mindanao](/wiki/Battle_of_Mindanao "Battle of Mindanao"), and other islands of the Philippines until the [end of the war](/wiki/End_of_World_War_II_in_Asia "End of World War II in Asia").\[[300]\](#cite_note-303 "#cite_note-303") Meanwhile, the [United States Army Air Forces](/wiki/United_States_Army_Air_Forces "United States Army Air Forces") launched [a massive firebombing campaign](/wiki/Air_raids_on_Japan "Air raids on Japan") of strategic cities in Japan in an effort to destroy Japanese war industry and civilian morale. A devastating [bombing raid on Tokyo of 9–10 March](/wiki/Bombing_of_Tokyo "Bombing of Tokyo") was the deadliest conventional bombing raid in history.\[[301]\](#cite_note-304 "#cite_note-304")

[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Mamoru_Shigemitsu_signs_the_Instrument_of_Surrender%2C_officially_ending_the_Second_World_War.jpg/250px-Mamoru_Shigemitsu_signs_the_Instrument_of_Surrender%2C_officially_ending_the_Second_World_War.jpg' alt='' title='' width='250' height='200' />](/wiki/File:Mamoru_Shigemitsu_signs_the_Instrument_of_Surrender,_officially_ending_the_Second_World_War.jpg "/wiki/File:Mamoru_Shigemitsu_signs_the_Instrument_of_Surrender,_officially_ending_the_Second_World_War.jpg")

Japanese foreign affairs minister [Mamoru Shigemitsu](/wiki/Mamoru_Shigemitsu "Mamoru Shigemitsu") signs the [Japanese Instrument of Surrender](/wiki/Japanese_Instrument_of_Surrender "Japanese Instrument of Surrender") on board [USS *Missouri*](</wiki/USS_Missouri_(BB-63)> "USS Missouri (BB-63)"), 2 September 1945

In May 1945, Australian troops [landed in Borneo](/wiki/Borneo_campaign "Borneo campaign"), overrunning the oilfields there. British, American, and Chinese forces defeated the Japanese in northern [Burma](/wiki/Burma_campaign "Burma campaign") in March, and the British pushed on to reach [Rangoon](/wiki/Yangon "Yangon") by 3 May.\[[302]\](#cite_note-Drea_2003_57-305 "#cite_note-Drea_2003_57-305") Chinese forces started a counterattack in the [Battle of West Hunan](/wiki/Battle_of_West_Hunan "Battle of West Hunan") that occurred between 6 April and 7 June 1945. American naval and amphibious forces also moved towards Japan, taking [Iwo Jima](/wiki/Battle_of_Iwo_Jima "Battle of Iwo Jima") by March, and [Okinawa](/wiki/Battle_of_Okinawa "Battle of Okinawa") by the end of June.\[[303]\](#cite_note-306 "#cite_note-306") At the same time, a naval blockade by [submarines](/wiki/Allied_submarines_in_the_Pacific_War "Allied submarines in the Pacific War") was strangling Japan's economy and drastically reducing its ability to supply overseas forces.\[[304]\](#cite_note-results_of_german_and_american_submarines-307 "#cite_note-results_of_german_and_american_submarines-307")\[[305]\](#cite_note-308 "#cite_note-308")

On 11 July, Allied leaders [met in Potsdam, Germany](/wiki/Potsdam_Conference "Potsdam Conference"). They [confirmed earlier agreements](/wiki/Potsdam_Agreement "Potsdam Agreement") about Germany,\[[306]\](#cite_note-Williams_2006_90-309 "#cite_note-Williams_2006_90-309") and the American, British and Chinese governments reiterated the demand for unconditional surrender of Japan, specifically stating that "[the alternative for Japan is prompt and utter destruction](/wiki/Potsdam_Declaration "Potsdam Declaration")".\[[307]\](#cite_note-Miscamble_2007_201-310 "#cite_note-Miscamble_2007_201-310") During this conference, the United Kingdom [held its general election](/wiki/1945_United_Kingdom_general_election "1945 United Kingdom general election"), and [Clement Attlee](/wiki/Clement_Attlee "Clement Attlee") replaced Churchill as Prime Minister.\[[308]\](#cite_note-Miscamble_2007_203_204-311 "#cite_note-Miscamble_2007_203_204-311")

The call for unconditional surrender was rejected by the Japanese government, which believed it would be capable of negotiating for more favourable surrender terms.\[[309]\](#cite\*note-312 "#cite\*note-312") In early August, the United States [dropped atomic bombs](/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki "Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki") on the Japanese cities of [Hiroshima](/wiki/Hiroshima "Hiroshima") and [Nagasaki](/wiki/Nagasaki "Nagasaki"). Between the two bombings, the Soviets, pursuant to the Yalta agreement, [declared war on Japan](/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Japanese_War "Soviet–Japanese War"), [invaded Japanese-held Manchuria](/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Manchuria "Soviet invasion of Manchuria") and quickly defeated the [Kwantung Army](/wiki/Kwantung_Army "Kwantung Army"), which was the largest Japanese fighting force.\[[310]\](#cite_note-313 "#cite_note-313") These two events persuaded previously adamant Imperial Army leaders to accept surrender terms.\[[311]\](#cite_note-Pape_1993-314 "#cite_note-Pape_1993-314") The Red Army also captured the [southern part of Sakhalin Island](/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_South_Sakhalin "Soviet invasion of South Sakhalin") and the [Kuril Islands](/wiki/Invasion_of_the_Kuril_Islands "Invasion of the Kuril Islands"). On the night of 9–10 August 1945, Emperor Hirohito announced his decision to accept the terms demanded by the Allies in the [Potsdam Declaration](/wiki/Potsdam_Declaration "Potsdam Declaration").\[[312]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBix2000525–526-315 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBix2000525–526-315") On 15 August, the Emperor communicated this decision to the Japanese people through a speech broadcast on the radio ([\_Gyokuon-hōsō\*](/wiki/Hirohito*surrender_broadcast "Hirohito surrender broadcast"), literally "broadcast in the Emperor's voice").\[[313]\](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBix2000526–528-316 "#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBix2000526–528-316") On 15 August 1945, [Japan surrendered](/wiki/Surrender_of_Japan "Surrender of Japan"), with the [surrender documents](/wiki/Japanese_Instrument_of_Surrender "Japanese Instrument of Surrender") finally signed at [Tokyo Bay](/wiki/Tokyo_Bay "Tokyo Bay") on the deck of the American battleship [USS \_Missouri\*](</wiki/USS_Missouri*(BB-63)> "USS Missouri (BB-63)") on 2 September 1945, ending the war.\[[314]\](#cite_note-Beevor_2012_776-317 "#cite_note-Beevor_2012_776-317")

## Aftermath

Main articles: [Aftermath of World War II](/wiki/Aftermath_of_World_War_II "Aftermath of World War II") and [Consequences of Nazism](/wiki/Consequences_of_Nazism "Consequences of Nazism")
[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Nuremberg_Trials._Looking_down_on_defendants_dock%2C_circa_1945-1946._-_NARA_-_540127.jpg/250px-Nuremberg_Trials._Looking_down_on_defendants_dock%2C_circa_1945-1946._-_NARA_-_540127.jpg' alt='' title='' width='250' height='204' />](/wiki/File:Nuremberg_Trials._Looking_down_on_defendants_dock,_circa_1945-1946._-_NARA_-_540127.jpg "/wiki/File:Nuremberg_Trials._Looking_down_on_defendants_dock,_circa_1945-1946._-_NARA_-_540127.jpg")

Defendants at the [Nuremberg trials](/wiki/Nuremberg_trials "Nuremberg trials"), where the Allied forces prosecuted prominent members of the political, military, judicial, and economic leadership of [Nazi Germany](/wiki/Nazi_Germany "Nazi Germany") for [crimes against humanity](/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity "Crimes against humanity")

The Allies established occupation administrations in [Austria](/wiki/Allied-occupied_Austria "Allied-occupied Austria") and [Germany](/wiki/Allied-occupied_Germany "Allied-occupied Germany"), both initially divided between western and eastern occupation zones controlled by the Western Allies and the Soviet Union, respectively. However, their paths soon diverged. In Germany, the [western](/wiki/Trizone "Trizone") and [eastern occupation zones](/wiki/Soviet_occupation_zone_in_Germany "Soviet occupation zone in Germany") controlled by the Western Allies and the Soviet Union officially ended in 1949, with the respective zones becoming separate countries, [West Germany](/wiki/West_Germany "West Germany") and [East Germany](/wiki/East_Germany "East Germany").\[[315]\](#cite_note-Wettig_2008_96_100-318 "#cite_note-Wettig_2008_96_100-318") In Austria, however, occupation continued until 1955, when a joint settlement between the Western Allies and the Soviet Union permitted the reunification of Austria as a democratic state officially non-aligned with any political bloc (although in practice having better relations with the Western Allies). A [denazification](/wiki/Denazification "Denazification") program in Germany led to the prosecution of Nazi war criminals in the [Nuremberg trials](/wiki/Nuremberg_trials "Nuremberg trials") and the removal of ex-Nazis from power, although this policy moved towards amnesty and re-integration of ex-Nazis into West German society.\[[316]\](#cite_note-Frei_2002_41_66-319 "#cite_note-Frei_2002_41_66-319")

Germany lost a quarter of its pre-war (1937) territory. Among the eastern territories, [Silesia](/wiki/Silesia "Silesia"), [Neumark](/wiki/Neumark "Neumark") and most of [Pomerania](/wiki/Pomerania "Pomerania") were taken over by Poland,\[[317]\](#cite*note-Eberhardt-2015-320 "#cite_note-Eberhardt-2015-320") and [East Prussia](/wiki/East_Prussia "East Prussia") was divided between Poland and the Soviet Union, followed by the [expulsion to Germany](</wiki/Flight_and_expulsion_of_Germans*(1944%E2%80%931950)> "Flight and expulsion of Germans (1944–1950)") of the nine million Germans from these provinces,\[[318]\](#cite*note-Eberhardt-2006-321 "#cite_note-Eberhardt-2006-321")\[[319]\](#cite_note-Eberhardt-2011-322 "#cite_note-Eberhardt-2011-322") as well as three million Germans from the [Sudetenland](/wiki/Sudetenland "Sudetenland") in Czechoslovakia. By the 1950s, one-fifth of West Germans were refugees from the east. The Soviet Union also took over the Polish provinces east of the [Curzon Line](/wiki/Curzon_Line "Curzon Line"),\[[320]\](#cite_note-Eberhardt-2012-323 "#cite_note-Eberhardt-2012-323") from which [two million Poles were expelled](</wiki/Polish_population_transfers*(1944%E2%80%931946)> "Polish population transfers (1944–1946)").\[[319]\](#cite\*note-Eberhardt-2011-322 "#cite_note-Eberhardt-2011-322")\[[321]\](#cite_note-stalinswars43-324 "#cite_note-stalinswars43-324") North-east Romania,\[[322]\](#cite_note-stalinswars55-325 "#cite_note-stalinswars55-325")\[[323]\](#cite_note-shirer794-326 "#cite_note-shirer794-326") parts of eastern Finland,\[[324]\](#cite_note-ckpipe-327 "#cite_note-ckpipe-327") and the [Baltic states](/wiki/Baltic_states "Baltic states") were [annexed into the Soviet Union](</wiki/Soviet_re-occupation_of_the_Baltic_states*(1944)> "Soviet re-occupation of the Baltic states (1944)").\[[325]\](#cite_note-Wettig_2008_20_21-328 "#cite_note-Wettig_2008_20_21-328")\[[326]\](#cite_note-Senn_2007\_?-329 "#cite_note-Senn_2007\_?-329") Italy [lost its monarchy](/wiki/1946_Italian_institutional_referendum "1946 Italian institutional referendum"), [colonial empire](/wiki/Italian_Empire "Italian Empire"), and some [European territories](/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_between_Italy_and_the_Allied_Powers "Treaty of Paris between Italy and the Allied Powers").\[[327]\](#cite_note-330 "#cite_note-330")

In an effort to maintain [world peace](/wiki/World_peace "World peace"),\[[328]\](#cite_note-Yoder_1997_39-331 "#cite_note-Yoder_1997_39-331") the Allies formed the [United Nations](/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations"),\[[329]\](#cite_note-332 "#cite_note-332") which officially came into existence on 24 October 1945,\[[330]\](#cite_note-333 "#cite_note-333") and adopted the [Universal Declaration of Human Rights](/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights "Universal Declaration of Human Rights") in 1948 as a common standard for all [member nations](/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations "Member states of the United Nations").\[[331]\](#cite_note-Waltz_2002-334 "#cite_note-Waltz_2002-334") The [great powers](/wiki/Great_powers "Great powers") that were the victors of the war—France, China, the United Kingdom, the Soviet Union, and the United States—became the [permanent members](/wiki/Permanent_members_of_the_United_Nations_Security_Council "Permanent members of the United Nations Security Council") of the UN's [Security Council](/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council "United Nations Security Council").\[[332]\](#cite_note-The_UN_Security_Council-335 "#cite_note-The_UN_Security_Council-335") The five permanent members remain so to the present, although there have been two seat changes, [between](/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_2758 "United Nations General Assembly Resolution 2758") the [Republic of China](/wiki/Taiwan "Taiwan") and the [People's Republic of China](/wiki/China "China") in 1971, and between the Soviet Union and its [successor state](/wiki/Succession_of_states "Succession of states"), the [Russian Federation](/wiki/Russia "Russia"), following the [dissolution of the Soviet Union](/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union "Dissolution of the Soviet Union") in 1991. The alliance between the Western Allies and the Soviet Union had begun to deteriorate even before the war was over.\[[333]\](#cite_note-Kantowicz_2000_6-336 "#cite_note-Kantowicz_2000_6-336")

[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/EasternBloc_BorderChange38-48.svg/250px-EasternBloc_BorderChange38-48.svg.png' alt='' title='' width='250' height='425' />](/wiki/File:EasternBloc_BorderChange38-48.svg "/wiki/File:EasternBloc_BorderChange38-48.svg")

Post-war border changes in [Central Europe](/wiki/Central_Europe "Central Europe") and creation of the [Communist](/wiki/Communism "Communism") [Eastern Bloc](/wiki/Eastern_Bloc "Eastern Bloc")

Besides Germany, the rest of Europe was also divided into Western and Soviet [spheres of influence](/wiki/Spheres_of_influence "Spheres of influence").\[[334]\](#cite_note-Trachtenberg_1999_33-337 "#cite_note-Trachtenberg_1999_33-337") Most eastern and central European countries fell into the [Soviet sphere](/wiki/Eastern_Bloc "Eastern Bloc"), which led to establishment of Communist-led regimes, with full or partial support of the Soviet occupation authorities. As a result, [East Germany](/wiki/East_Germany "East Germany"),\[[335]\](#cite_note-Applebaum_2012-338 "#cite_note-Applebaum_2012-338") [Poland](/wiki/Polish_People%27s_Republic "Polish People's Republic"), [Hungary](/wiki/Hungarian_People%27s_Republic "Hungarian People's Republic"), [Romania](/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Romania "Socialist Republic of Romania"), [Bulgaria](/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Bulgaria "People's Republic of Bulgaria"), [Czechoslovakia](/wiki/Czechoslovak_Socialist_Republic "Czechoslovak Socialist Republic"), and [Albania](/wiki/People%27s_Socialist_Republic_of_Albania "People's Socialist Republic of Albania")\[[336]\](#cite_note-Naimark_2010-339 "#cite_note-Naimark_2010-339") became Soviet [satellite states](/wiki/Satellite_state#Soviet_satellite_states "Satellite state"). Communist [Yugoslavia](/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia "Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia") conducted a fully [independent policy](/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement "Non-Aligned Movement"), causing [tension with the Soviet Union](/wiki/Tito%E2%80%93Stalin_split "Tito–Stalin split").\[[337]\](#cite_note-Swain_1992-340 "#cite_note-Swain_1992-340") A [Communist uprising in Greece](/wiki/Greek_Civil_War "Greek Civil War") was put down with Anglo-American support and the country remained aligned with the West.\[[338]\](#cite_note-341 "#cite_note-341")

Post-war division of the world was formalised by two international military alliances, the United States-led [NATO](/wiki/NATO "NATO") and the Soviet-led [Warsaw Pact](/wiki/Warsaw_Pact "Warsaw Pact").\[[339]\](#cite_note-Borstelmann_2005_318-342 "#cite_note-Borstelmann_2005_318-342") The long period of political tensions and military competition between them—the [Cold War](/wiki/Cold_War "Cold War")—would be accompanied by an unprecedented [arms race](/wiki/Arms_race "Arms race") and number of [proxy wars](/wiki/Proxy_war "Proxy war") throughout the world.\[[340]\](#cite_note-343 "#cite_note-343")

In Asia, the United States led the [occupation of Japan](/wiki/Occupation_of_Japan "Occupation of Japan") and [administered Japan's former islands](/wiki/Trust_Territory_of_the_Pacific_Islands "Trust Territory of the Pacific Islands") in the Western Pacific, while the Soviets annexed [South Sakhalin](/wiki/South_Sakhalin "South Sakhalin") and the [Kuril Islands](/wiki/Kuril_Islands "Kuril Islands").\[[341]\](#cite_note-Weinberg_2005_911-344 "#cite_note-Weinberg_2005_911-344") [Korea](/wiki/Korea "Korea"), formerly [under Japanese colonial rule](/wiki/Korea_under_Japanese_rule "Korea under Japanese rule"), was [divided and occupied](/wiki/Division_of_Korea "Division of Korea") by the Soviet Union in the [North](/wiki/North_Korea "North Korea") and the United States in the [South](/wiki/South_Korea "South Korea") between 1945 and 1948. Separate republics emerged on both sides of the 38th parallel in 1948, each claiming to be the legitimate government for all of Korea, which led ultimately to the [Korean War](/wiki/Korean_War "Korean War").\[[342]\](#cite_note-345 "#cite_note-345")

In China, nationalist and communist forces resumed [the civil war](/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War "Chinese Civil War") in June 1946. Communist forces were victorious and established the People's Republic of China on the mainland, while nationalist forces retreated to [Taiwan](/wiki/Taiwan "Taiwan") in 1949.\[[343]\](#cite_note-Lynch_2010_12_13-346 "#cite_note-Lynch_2010_12_13-346") In the Middle East, the Arab rejection of the [United Nations Partition Plan for Palestine](/wiki/United_Nations_Partition_Plan_for_Palestine "United Nations Partition Plan for Palestine") and the [creation of Israel](/wiki/Creation_of_Israel "Creation of Israel") marked the escalation of the [Arab–Israeli conflict](/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_conflict "Arab–Israeli conflict"). While European powers attempted to retain some or all of their [colonial empires](/wiki/Colonial_empire "Colonial empire"), their losses of prestige and resources during the war rendered this unsuccessful, leading to [decolonisation](/wiki/Decolonization "Decolonization").\[[344]\](#cite_note-JMRoberts_1996_589-347 "#cite_note-JMRoberts_1996_589-347")\[[345]\](#cite_note-348 "#cite_note-348")

The global economy suffered heavily from the war, although participating nations were affected differently.
