The United States emerged much richer than any other nation, leading to a [baby boom](/wiki/Mid-20th_century_baby_boom "Mid-20th century baby boom"), and by 1950 its gross domestic product per person was much higher than that of any of the other powers, and it dominated the world economy.\[[346]\](#cite_note-349 "#cite_note-349") The Allied occupational authorities pursued a policy of [industrial disarmament in Western Germany](/wiki/Allied_plans_for_German_industry_after_World_War_II "Allied plans for German industry after World War II") from 1945 to 1948.\[[347]\](#cite_note-Balabkins_1964_207-350 "#cite_note-Balabkins_1964_207-350") Due to international trade interdependencies, this policy led to an economic stagnation in Europe and delayed European recovery from the war for several years.\[[348]\](#cite_note-351 "#cite_note-351")\[[349]\](#cite_note-Balabkins_1964_208,209-352 "#cite_note-Balabkins_1964_208,209-352")

At the [Bretton Woods Conference](/wiki/Bretton_Woods_Conference "Bretton Woods Conference") in July 1944, the Allied nations drew up an economic framework for the post-war world. The agreement created the [International Monetary Fund](/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund "International Monetary Fund") (IMF) and the [International Bank for Reconstruction and Development](/wiki/International_Bank_for_Reconstruction_and_Development "International Bank for Reconstruction and Development") (IBRD), which later became part of the [World Bank Group](/wiki/World_Bank_Group "World Bank Group"). The [Bretton Woods system](/wiki/Bretton_Woods_system "Bretton Woods system") lasted until 1973.\[[350]\](#cite_note-353 "#cite_note-353") Recovery began with the mid-1948 [currency reform in Western Germany](/wiki/Deutsche_Mark "Deutsche Mark"), and was sped up by the liberalisation of European economic policy that the US [Marshall Plan](/wiki/Marshall_Plan "Marshall Plan") economic aid (1948–1951) both directly and indirectly caused.\[[351]\](#cite_note-354 "#cite_note-354")\[[352]\](#cite_note-Balabkins_1964_212-355 "#cite_note-Balabkins_1964_212-355") The post-1948 West German recovery has been called the [German economic miracle](/wiki/Wirtschaftswunder#West_Germany "Wirtschaftswunder").\[[353]\](#cite_note-356 "#cite_note-356") Italy also experienced an [economic boom](/wiki/Italian_economic_miracle "Italian economic miracle")\[[354]\](#cite_note-357 "#cite_note-357") and the [French economy rebounded](/wiki/Trente_Glorieuses "Trente Glorieuses").\[[355]\](#cite_note-358 "#cite_note-358") By contrast, the United Kingdom was in a state of economic ruin,\[[356]\](#cite_note-359 "#cite_note-359") and although receiving a quarter of the total Marshall Plan assistance, more than any other European country,\[[357]\](#cite_note-360 "#cite_note-360") it continued in relative economic decline for decades.\[[358]\](#cite_note-361 "#cite_note-361") The Soviet Union, despite enormous human and material losses, also experienced rapid increase in production in the immediate post-war era,\[[359]\](#cite_note-Smith_1993_32-362 "#cite_note-Smith_1993_32-362") having seized and transferred most of Germany's industrial plants and exacted [war reparations](/wiki/World_War_II_reparations "World War II reparations") from its satellite states.\[[d]\](#cite_note-363 "#cite_note-363")\[[360]\](#cite_note-364 "#cite_note-364") Japan recovered much later.\[[361]\](#cite_note-365 "#cite_note-365") China returned to its pre-war industrial production by 1952.\[[362]\](#cite_note-366 "#cite_note-366")

## Impact

Main article: [Historiography of World War II](/wiki/Historiography_of_World_War_II "Historiography of World War II")

### Casualties and war crimes

Main article: [World War II casualties](/wiki/World_War_II_casualties "World War II casualties")
Further information: [War crimes in World War II](/wiki/War_crimes_in_World_War_II "War crimes in World War II")
[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/World_War_II_Casualties.svg/500px-World_War_II_Casualties.svg.png' alt='' title='' width='450' height='293' />](/wiki/File:World_War_II_Casualties.svg "/wiki/File:World_War_II_Casualties.svg")

World War II deaths

Estimates for the total number of casualties in the war vary, because many deaths went unrecorded.\[[363]\](#cite_note-367 "#cite_note-367") Most suggest 60 million people died, about [20 million military personnel](/wiki/Battle_casualties_of_World_War_II "Battle casualties of World War II") and 40 million civilians.\[[364]\](#cite_note-WWII:\_C&C-368 "#cite_note-WWII:\_C&C-368")\[[365]\](#cite_note-369 "#cite_note-369")

The Soviet Union alone lost around 27 million people during the war,\[[366]\](#cite_note-370 "#cite_note-370") including 8.7 million military and 19 million civilian deaths.\[[367]\](#cite_note-Ell&Mak_1994-371 "#cite_note-Ell&Mak_1994-371") A quarter of the total people in the Soviet Union were wounded or killed.\[[368]\](#cite_note-372 "#cite_note-372") Germany sustained 5.3 million military losses, mostly on the Eastern Front and during the final battles in Germany.\[[369]\](#cite_note-Herf_2003-373 "#cite_note-Herf_2003-373")

An estimated 11\[[370]\](#cite_note-374 "#cite_note-374") to 17 million\[[371]\](#cite_note-Niewyk45-375 "#cite_note-Niewyk45-375") civilians died as a direct or as an indirect result of Hitler's [racist policies](/wiki/Racial_policy_of_Nazi_Germany "Racial policy of Nazi Germany"), including [mass killing](/wiki/Mass_killing "Mass killing") of [around 6 million Jews](/wiki/The_Holocaust "The Holocaust"), along with [Roma](/wiki/Romani_Holocaust "Romani Holocaust"), [homosexuals](/wiki/Persecution_of_homosexuals_in_Nazi_Germany "Persecution of homosexuals in Nazi Germany"), at least 1.9 million ethnic [Poles](/wiki/World_War_II_casualties_of_Poland "World War II casualties of Poland")\[[372]\](#cite_note-376 "#cite_note-376")\[[373]\](#cite_note-377 "#cite_note-377") and [millions of other Slavs](/wiki/World_War_II_casualties_of_the_Soviet_Union "World War II casualties of the Soviet Union") (including Russians, Ukrainians and Belarusians), and [other ethnic and minority groups](/wiki/Holocaust_victims "Holocaust victims").\[[374]\](#cite_note-378 "#cite_note-378")\[[371]\](#cite_note-Niewyk45-375 "#cite_note-Niewyk45-375") Between 1941 and 1945, more than 200,000 ethnic [Serbs](/wiki/Serbs "Serbs"), along with Roma and Jews, were [persecuted and murdered](/wiki/Genocide_of_Serbs_in_the_Independent_State_of_Croatia "Genocide of Serbs in the Independent State of Croatia") by the Axis-aligned Croatian [Ustaše](/wiki/Usta%C5%A1e "Ustaše") in [Yugoslavia](/wiki/Yugoslavia "Yugoslavia").\[[375]\](#cite_note-379 "#cite_note-379") Concurrently, [Muslims](/wiki/Bosniaks "Bosniaks") and [Croats](/wiki/Croats "Croats") were [persecuted and killed](/wiki/Chetnik_war_crimes_in_World_War_II "Chetnik war crimes in World War II") by Serb nationalist [Chetniks](/wiki/Chetniks "Chetniks"),\[[376]\](#cite_note-380 "#cite_note-380") with an estimated 50,000–68,000 victims (of which 41,000 were civilians).\[[377]\](#cite_note-Geiger-381 "#cite_note-Geiger-381") Also, more than 100,000 Poles were massacred by the [Ukrainian Insurgent Army](/wiki/Ukrainian_Insurgent_Army "Ukrainian Insurgent Army") in the [Volhynia massacres](/wiki/Massacres_of_Poles_in_Volhynia_and_Eastern_Galicia "Massacres of Poles in Volhynia and Eastern Galicia"), between 1943 and 1945.\[[378]\](#cite_note-382 "#cite_note-382") At the same time, about 10,000–15,000 Ukrainians were killed by the Polish [Home Army](/wiki/Home_Army "Home Army") and other Polish units, in reprisal attacks.\[[379]\](#cite_note-383 "#cite_note-383")

[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Nanking_bodies_1937.jpg/250px-Nanking_bodies_1937.jpg' alt='' title='' width='250' height='175' />](/wiki/File:Nanking_bodies_1937.jpg "/wiki/File:Nanking_bodies_1937.jpg")

Bodies of Chinese civilians killed by the [Imperial Japanese Army](/wiki/Imperial_Japanese_Army "Imperial Japanese Army") during the [Nanjing Massacre](/wiki/Nanjing_Massacre "Nanjing Massacre") in December 1937

In Asia and the Pacific, the number of people killed by Japanese troops remains contested. According to R.J. Rummel, the Japanese killed between 3 million and more than 10 million people, with the most probable case of almost 6,000,000 people.\[[380]\](#cite_note-384 "#cite_note-384") According to the British historian [M. R. D. Foot](/wiki/M._R._D._Foot "M. R. D. Foot"), civilian deaths are between 10 million and 20 million, whereas Chinese military casualties (killed and wounded) are estimated to be over five million.\[[381]\](#cite_note-385 "#cite_note-385") Other estimates say that up to 30 million people, most of them civilians, were killed.\[[382]\](#cite_note-386 "#cite_note-386")\[[383]\](#cite_note-387 "#cite_note-387") The most infamous Japanese atrocity was the [Nanjing Massacre](/wiki/Nanjing_Massacre "Nanjing Massacre"), in which fifty to three hundred thousand Chinese civilians were raped and murdered.\[[384]\](#cite_note-388 "#cite_note-388") Mitsuyoshi Himeta reported that 2.7 million casualties occurred during the [Three Alls policy](/wiki/Three_Alls_policy "Three Alls policy"). General [Yasuji Okamura](/wiki/Yasuji_Okamura "Yasuji Okamura") implemented the policy in [Hebei](/wiki/Hebei "Hebei") and [Shandong](/wiki/Shandong "Shandong").\[[385]\](#cite_note-389 "#cite_note-389")

Axis forces employed [biological](/wiki/Biological_warfare "Biological warfare") and [chemical weapons](/wiki/Chemical_warfare "Chemical warfare"). The [Imperial Japanese Army](/wiki/Imperial_Japanese_Army "Imperial Japanese Army") used a variety of such weapons during its [invasion and occupation of China](/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War "Second Sino-Japanese War") (_see [Unit 731](/wiki/Unit_731 "Unit 731")_)\[[386]\](#cite_note-390 "#cite_note-390")\[[387]\](#cite_note-391 "#cite_note-391") and in [early conflicts against the Soviets](/wiki/Battles_of_Khalkhin_Gol "Battles of Khalkhin Gol").\[[388]\](#cite_note-392 "#cite_note-392") Both the Germans and the [Japanese tested](/wiki/Japanese_human_experimentation_on_the_Chinese "Japanese human experimentation on the Chinese") such weapons against civilians,\[[389]\](#cite_note-393 "#cite_note-393") and sometimes on [prisoners of war](/wiki/Prisoner_of_war "Prisoner of war").\[[390]\](#cite_note-394 "#cite_note-394")

The Soviet Union was responsible for the [Katyn massacre](/wiki/Katyn_massacre "Katyn massacre") of 22,000 Polish officers,\[[391]\](#cite_note-395 "#cite_note-395") and the imprisonment or execution of [hundreds of thousands of political prisoners](/wiki/NKVD_prisoner_massacres "NKVD prisoner massacres") by the [NKVD](/wiki/NKVD "NKVD") secret police, along with [mass civilian deportations to Siberia](/wiki/Population_transfer_in_the_Soviet_Union "Population transfer in the Soviet Union"), in the [Baltic states](/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Baltic_states "Occupation of the Baltic states") and [eastern Poland](/wiki/Territories_of_Poland_annexed_by_the_Soviet_Union "Territories of Poland annexed by the Soviet Union") annexed by the Red Army.\[[392]\](#cite_note-396 "#cite_note-396") Soviet soldiers committed mass rapes in occupied territories, especially [in Germany](/wiki/Soviet_occupation_zone_in_Germany "Soviet occupation zone in Germany").\[[393]\](#cite_note-397 "#cite_note-397")\[[394]\](#cite_note-Bird-398 "#cite_note-Bird-398") The exact number of German women and girls raped by Soviet troops during the war and occupation is uncertain, but historians estimate their numbers are likely in the hundreds of thousands, and possibly as many as two million,\[[395]\](#cite_note-:4-399 "#cite_note-:4-399") while figures for women raped by German soldiers in the Soviet Union go as far as ten million.\[[396]\](#cite_note-400 "#cite_note-400")\[[397]\](#cite_note-401 "#cite_note-401")

The mass bombing of cities in Europe and Asia has often been called a war crime, although no [positive](/wiki/Positive_law "Positive law") or specific [customary](/wiki/Customary_international_law "Customary international law") [international humanitarian law](/wiki/International_humanitarian_law "International humanitarian law") with respect to [aerial warfare](/wiki/Aerial_warfare "Aerial warfare") existed before or during World War II.\[[398]\](#cite_note-402 "#cite_note-402") The USAAF [bombed a total of 67 Japanese cities](/wiki/Air_raids_on_Japan "Air raids on Japan"), killing 393,000 civilians, including the [atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki](/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki "Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki"), and destroying 65% of built-up areas.\[[399]\](#cite_note-403 "#cite_note-403")

### Genocide, concentration camps, and slave labour

Main articles: [The Holocaust](/wiki/The_Holocaust "The Holocaust"), [Nazi concentration camps](/wiki/Nazi_concentration_camps "Nazi concentration camps"), [Extermination camp](/wiki/Extermination_camp "Extermination camp"), [Forced labour under German rule during World War II](/wiki/Forced_labour_under_German_rule_during_World_War_II "Forced labour under German rule during World War II"), [Kidnapping of children by Nazi Germany](/wiki/Kidnapping_of_children_by_Nazi_Germany "Kidnapping of children by Nazi Germany"), [Nazi human experimentation](/wiki/Nazi_human_experimentation "Nazi human experimentation"), [Soviet war crimes § World War II](/wiki/Soviet_war_crimes#World_War_II "Soviet war crimes"), and [Japanese war crimes](/wiki/Japanese_war_crimes "Japanese war crimes")
[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/The_Liberation_of_Bergen-belsen_Concentration_Camp%2C_April_1945_BU4031.jpg/250px-The_Liberation_of_Bergen-belsen_Concentration_Camp%2C_April_1945_BU4031.jpg' alt='' title='' width='250' height='247' />](/wiki/File:The_Liberation_of_Bergen-belsen_Concentration_Camp,_April_1945_BU4031.jpg "/wiki/File:The_Liberation_of_Bergen-belsen_Concentration_Camp,_April_1945_BU4031.jpg")

[Schutzstaffel](/wiki/Schutzstaffel "Schutzstaffel") (SS) female camp guards removing prisoners' bodies from lorries and carrying them to a mass grave, inside the German [Bergen-Belsen concentration camp](/wiki/Bergen-Belsen_concentration_camp "Bergen-Belsen concentration camp"), 1945

[Nazi Germany](/wiki/Nazi_Germany "Nazi Germany"), under the [dictatorship](/wiki/Dictatorship "Dictatorship") of Adolf Hitler, was responsible for murdering about 6 million Jews in what is now known as [the Holocaust](/wiki/The_Holocaust "The Holocaust"). They also murdered an additional 4 million others who were deemed "[unworthy of life](/wiki/Life_unworthy_of_life "Life unworthy of life")" (including the [disabled](/wiki/Disability "Disability") and [mentally ill](/wiki/Mental_disorder "Mental disorder"), [Soviet prisoners of war](/wiki/German_atrocities_committed_against_Soviet_prisoners_of_war "German atrocities committed against Soviet prisoners of war"), [Romani](/wiki/Romani_people "Romani people"), [homosexuals](/wiki/Homosexuals "Homosexuals"), [Freemasons](/wiki/Freemasons "Freemasons"), and [Jehovah's Witnesses](/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses "Jehovah's Witnesses")) as part of a program of deliberate extermination, in effect becoming a "[genocidal](/wiki/Genocide "Genocide") state".\[[400]\](#cite_note-404 "#cite_note-404") [Soviet POWs](/wiki/German_atrocities_committed_against_Soviet_prisoners_of_war "German atrocities committed against Soviet prisoners of war") were kept in especially unbearable conditions, and 3.6 million Soviet POWs out of 5.7 million died in Nazi camps during the war.\[[401]\](#cite_note-405 "#cite_note-405")\[[402]\](#cite_note-Overy_2004_568_569-406 "#cite_note-Overy_2004_568_569-406") In addition to [concentration camps](/wiki/Nazi_concentration_camps "Nazi concentration camps"), [death camps](/wiki/Extermination_camp "Extermination camp") were created in Nazi Germany to exterminate people on an industrial scale. Nazi Germany extensively used [forced labourers](/wiki/Forced_labour_under_German_rule_during_World_War_II "Forced labour under German rule during World War II"); about 12 million [Europeans](/wiki/Ostarbeiter "Ostarbeiter") from German-occupied countries were abducted and used as a slave work force in German industry, agriculture and war economy.\[[403]\](#cite_note-compensation-407 "#cite_note-compensation-407")

[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Czeslawa_Kwoka_-_Brasse.jpg/250px-Czeslawa_Kwoka_-_Brasse.jpg' alt='' title='' width='250' height='111' />](/wiki/File:Czeslawa_Kwoka_-_Brasse.jpg "/wiki/File:Czeslawa_Kwoka_-_Brasse.jpg")

[Prisoner identity photograph of a Polish girl](/wiki/Czes%C5%82awa_Kwoka "Czesława Kwoka") taken by the German [SS](/wiki/SS "SS") in [Auschwitz](/wiki/Auschwitz "Auschwitz").\[[404]\](#cite_note-408 "#cite_note-408") Approximately 230,000 children were held prisoner and used in forced labour and [Nazi medical experiments](/wiki/Nazi_human_experimentation "Nazi human experimentation")

The Soviet [Gulag](/wiki/Gulag "Gulag") became a _de facto_ system of deadly camps during 1942–1943, when wartime privation and hunger caused numerous deaths of inmates,\[[405]\](#cite_note-409 "#cite_note-409") including foreign citizens of Poland and [other countries](/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Baltic_states "Occupation of the Baltic states") occupied in 1939–1940 by the Soviet Union, as well as Axis [POWs](/wiki/German_prisoners_of_war_in_the_Soviet_Union "German prisoners of war in the Soviet Union").\[[406]\](#cite_note-410 "#cite_note-410") By the end of the war, most Soviet POWs liberated from Nazi camps and many repatriated civilians were detained in special filtration camps where they were subjected to [NKVD](/wiki/NKVD "NKVD") evaluation, and 226,127 were sent to the Gulag as real or perceived Nazi collaborators.\[[407]\](#cite_note-411 "#cite_note-411")

Japanese [prisoner-of-war camps](/wiki/Prisoner-of-war_camp "Prisoner-of-war camp"), many of which were used as labour camps, also had high death rates. The [International Military Tribunal for the Far East](/wiki/International_Military_Tribunal_for_the_Far_East "International Military Tribunal for the Far East") found the death rate of Western prisoners was 27 percent (for American POWs, 37 percent),\[[408]\](#cite_note-412 "#cite_note-412") seven times that of POWs under the Germans and Italians.\[[409]\](#cite_note-413 "#cite_note-413") While 37,583 prisoners from the UK, 28,500 from the Netherlands, and 14,473 from the United States were released after the [surrender of Japan](/wiki/Surrender_of_Japan "Surrender of Japan"), the number of Chinese released was only 56.\[[410]\](#cite_note-414 "#cite_note-414")

At least five million Chinese civilians from northern China and Manchukuo were enslaved between 1935 and 1941 by the [East Asia Development Board](/wiki/East_Asia_Development_Board "East Asia Development Board"), or _Kōain_, for work in mines and war industries. After 1942, the number reached 10 million.\[[411]\](#cite\*note-zhifen2002-415 "#cite_note-zhifen2002-415") In [Java](/wiki/Java "Java"), between 4 and 10 million \*[rōmusha](/wiki/R%C5%8Dmusha "Rōmusha")\_ (Japanese: "manual labourers"), were forced to work by the Japanese military. About 270,000 of these Javanese labourers were sent to other Japanese-held areas in Southeast Asia, and only 52,000 were repatriated to Java.\[[412]\](#cite_note-indonesiaww2-416 "#cite_note-indonesiaww2-416")

### Occupation

Main articles: [German-occupied Europe](/wiki/German-occupied_Europe "German-occupied Europe"), [Resistance during World War II](/wiki/Resistance_during_World_War_II "Resistance during World War II"), [Collaboration with Nazi Germany and Fascist Italy](/wiki/Collaboration_with_Nazi_Germany_and_Fascist_Italy "Collaboration with Nazi Germany and Fascist Italy"), [Collaboration with Imperial Japan](/wiki/Collaboration_with_Imperial_Japan "Collaboration with Imperial Japan"), and [Nazi plunder](/wiki/Nazi_plunder "Nazi plunder")
[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Palmiry_before_execution.jpg/250px-Palmiry_before_execution.jpg' alt='' title='' width='250' height='160' />](/wiki/File:Palmiry_before_execution.jpg "/wiki/File:Palmiry_before_execution.jpg")

Polish civilians wearing blindfolds photographed just before being massacred by German soldiers in [Palmiry forest](/wiki/Palmiry_massacre "Palmiry massacre"), 1940

In Europe, occupation came under two forms. In Western, Northern, and Central Europe (France, Norway, Denmark, the Low Countries, and the [annexed portions of Czechoslovakia](/wiki/Protectorate_of_Bohemia_and_Moravia "Protectorate of Bohemia and Moravia")) Germany established economic policies through which it collected roughly 69.5 billion reichsmarks (27.8 billion US dollars) by the end of the war; this figure does not include the [plunder](/wiki/Nazi_plunder "Nazi plunder") of industrial products, military equipment, raw materials and other goods.\[[413]\](#cite_note-417 "#cite_note-417") Thus, the income from occupied nations was over 40 percent of the income Germany collected from taxation, a figure which increased to nearly 40 percent of total German income as the war went on.\[[414]\](#cite_note-Milward_1979_138-418 "#cite_note-Milward_1979_138-418")

[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-031-2436-03A%2C_Russland%2C_Hinrichtung_von_Partisanen_retouched.jpg/250px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-031-2436-03A%2C_Russland%2C_Hinrichtung_von_Partisanen_retouched.jpg' alt='' title='' width='250' height='156' />](/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-031-2436-03A,_Russland,_Hinrichtung_von_Partisanen_retouched.jpg "/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-031-2436-03A,_Russland,_Hinrichtung_von_Partisanen_retouched.jpg")

[Soviet partisans](/wiki/Soviet_partisans "Soviet partisans") hanged by the German army. The [Russian Academy of Sciences](/wiki/Russian_Academy_of_Sciences "Russian Academy of Sciences") reported in 1995 that [civilian victims in the Soviet Union](/wiki/World_War_II_casualties_of_the_Soviet_Union "World War II casualties of the Soviet Union") at German hands totalled 13.7 million dead, twenty percent of the 68 million people in the occupied Soviet Union

In the East, the intended gains of _[Lebensraum](/wiki/Lebensraum "Lebensraum")_ were never attained as fluctuating front-lines and Soviet [scorched earth](/wiki/Scorched_earth "Scorched earth") policies denied resources to the German invaders.\[[415]\](#cite_note-Milward_1992_148-419 "#cite_note-Milward_1992_148-419") Unlike in the West, the [Nazi racial policy](/wiki/Racial_policy_of_Nazi_Germany "Racial policy of Nazi Germany") encouraged extreme brutality against what it considered to be the "[inferior people](/wiki/Untermensch "Untermensch")" of Slavic descent; most German advances were thus followed by [mass atrocities and war crimes](/wiki/Generalplan_Ost "Generalplan Ost").\[[416]\](#cite_note-420 "#cite_note-420") The Nazis [killed an estimated 2.8 million ethnic Poles](/wiki/Nazi_crimes_against_the_Polish_nation "Nazi crimes against the Polish nation") in addition to Polish-Jewish victims of the Holocaust.\[[417]\](#cite_note-421 "#cite_note-421") Although [resistance groups](/wiki/Resistance_during_World_War_II "Resistance during World War II") formed in most occupied territories, they did not significantly hamper German operations in either the East\[[418]\](#cite_note-422 "#cite_note-422") or the West\[[419]\](#cite_note-423 "#cite_note-423") until late 1943.

In Asia, Japan termed nations under its occupation as being part of the [Greater East Asia Co-Prosperity Sphere](/wiki/Greater_East_Asia_Co-Prosperity_Sphere "Greater East Asia Co-Prosperity Sphere"), essentially a Japanese [hegemony](/wiki/Hegemony "Hegemony") which it claimed was for purposes of liberating colonised peoples.\[[420]\](#cite_note-424 "#cite_note-424") Although Japanese forces were sometimes welcomed as liberators from European domination, [Japanese war crimes](/wiki/Japanese_war_crimes "Japanese war crimes") frequently turned local public opinion against them.\[[421]\](#cite_note-GSWW6_266-425 "#cite_note-GSWW6_266-425") During Japan's initial conquest, it captured 4,000,000 barrels (640,000 m3) of oil (~550,000 tonnes) left behind by retreating Allied forces; and by 1943, was able to get production in the Dutch East Indies up to 50 million barrels (7,900,000 m3) of oil (~6.8 million tonnes), 76 percent of its 1940 output rate.\[[421]\](#cite_note-GSWW6_266-425 "#cite_note-GSWW6_266-425")

### Home fronts and production

Main articles: [Military production during World War II](/wiki/Military_production_during_World_War_II "Military production during World War II") and [Home front during World War II](/wiki/Home_front_during_World_War_II "Home front during World War II")
[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/World_War_II_Allies_to_Axis_GDP_Ratio.svg/500px-World_War_II_Allies_to_Axis_GDP_Ratio.svg.png' alt='' title='' width='400' height='229' />](/wiki/File:World_War_II_Allies_to_Axis_GDP_Ratio.svg "/wiki/File:World_War_II_Allies_to_Axis_GDP_Ratio.svg")

Allies to Axis GDP ratio throughout the war

In the 1930s Britain and the United States together controlled almost 75% of world mineral output—essential for projecting military power.\[[422]\](#cite_note-426 "#cite_note-426")

In Europe, before the outbreak of the war, the Allies had significant advantages in both population and economics. In 1938, the Western Allies (United Kingdom, France, Poland and the British Dominions) had a 30 percent larger population and a 30 percent higher gross domestic product than the European Axis powers (Germany and Italy); including colonies, the Allies had more than a 5:1 advantage in population and a nearly 2:1 advantage in GDP.\[[423]\](#cite_note-6Econ3-427 "#cite_note-6Econ3-427") In Asia at the same time, China had roughly six times the population of Japan but only an 89 percent higher GDP; this reduces to three times the population and only a 38 percent higher GDP if Japanese colonies are included.\[[423]\](#cite_note-6Econ3-427 "#cite_note-6Econ3-427")

The United States produced about two-thirds of all munitions used by the Allies in World War II, including warships, transports, warplanes, artillery, tanks, trucks, and ammunition.\[[424]\](#cite_note-428 "#cite_note-428") Although the Allies' economic and population advantages were largely mitigated during the initial rapid blitzkrieg attacks of Germany and Japan, they became the decisive factor by 1942, after the United States and Soviet Union joined the Allies and the war evolved into one of [attrition](/wiki/Attrition_warfare "Attrition warfare").\[[425]\](#cite_note-6Econ2-429 "#cite_note-6Econ2-429") While the Allies' ability to out-produce the Axis was partly due to more access to natural resources, other factors, such as Germany and Japan's reluctance to employ women in the [labour force](/wiki/Workforce "Workforce"),\[[426]\](#cite_note-430 "#cite_note-430") Allied [strategic bombing](/wiki/Strategic_bombing_during_World_War_II "Strategic bombing during World War II"),\[[427]\](#cite_note-431 "#cite_note-431") and Germany's late shift to a [war economy](/wiki/War_economy "War economy")\[[428]\](#cite_note-432 "#cite_note-432") contributed significantly. Additionally, neither Germany nor Japan planned to fight a protracted war, and had not equipped themselves to do so.\[[429]\](#cite_note-433 "#cite_note-433") To improve their production, Germany and Japan used millions of [slave labourers](/wiki/Slavery "Slavery");\[[430]\](#cite_note-434 "#cite_note-434") [Germany enslaved](/wiki/Forced_labour_under_German_rule_during_World_War_II "Forced labour under German rule during World War II") about 12 million people, mostly from Eastern Europe,\[[403]\](#cite_note-compensation-407 "#cite_note-compensation-407") while [Japan used](/wiki/Slavery_in_Japan "Slavery in Japan") more than 18 million people in Far East Asia.\[[411]\](#cite_note-zhifen2002-415 "#cite_note-zhifen2002-415")\[[412]\](#cite_note-indonesiaww2-416 "#cite_note-indonesiaww2-416")

### Advances in technology and its application

Main article: [Technology during World War II](/wiki/Technology_during_World_War_II "Technology during World War II")
[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1978-Anh.026-01%2C_Peenem%C3%BCnde%2C_V2_beim_Start.jpg/250px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1978-Anh.026-01%2C_Peenem%C3%BCnde%2C_V2_beim_Start.jpg' alt='' title='' width='250' height='173' />](/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1978-Anh.026-01,_Peenem%C3%BCnde,_V2_beim_Start.jpg "/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1978-Anh.026-01,_Peenem%C3%BCnde,_V2_beim_Start.jpg")

A [V-2 rocket](/wiki/V-2_rocket "V-2 rocket") launched from a fixed site in [Peenemünde](/wiki/Peenem%C3%BCnde "Peenemünde"), 21 June 1943

Aircraft were used for [reconnaissance](/wiki/Reconnaissance_aircraft "Reconnaissance aircraft"), as [fighters](/wiki/Fighter_aircraft "Fighter aircraft"), [bombers](/wiki/Bomber "Bomber"), and [ground-support](/wiki/Close_air_support "Close air support"), and each role developed considerably. Innovations included [airlift](/wiki/Airlift "Airlift") (the capability to quickly move limited high-priority supplies, equipment, and personnel);\[[431]\](#cite_note-EncWWII_76-435 "#cite_note-EncWWII_76-435") and [strategic bombing](/wiki/Strategic_bombing "Strategic bombing") (the bombing of enemy industrial and population centres to destroy the enemy's ability to wage war).\[[432]\](#cite_note-436 "#cite_note-436") [Anti-aircraft weaponry](/wiki/Anti-aircraft_warfare "Anti-aircraft warfare") also advanced, including defences such as [radar](/wiki/Radar "Radar") and surface-to-air artillery, in particular the introduction of the [proximity fuze](/wiki/Proximity_fuze "Proximity fuze"). The use of the [jet aircraft](/wiki/Jet_aircraft "Jet aircraft") was pioneered and led to jets becoming standard in air forces worldwide.\[[433]\](#cite_note-437 "#cite_note-437")

Advances were made in nearly every aspect of [naval warfare](/wiki/Naval_warfare "Naval warfare"), most notably with [aircraft carriers](/wiki/Aircraft_carrier "Aircraft carrier") and [submarines](/wiki/Submarine "Submarine"). Although [aeronautical](/wiki/Aeronautics "Aeronautics") warfare had relatively little success at the start of the war, [actions at Taranto](/wiki/Battle_of_Taranto "Battle of Taranto"), [Pearl Harbor](/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor "Attack on Pearl Harbor"), and the [Coral Sea](/wiki/Battle_of_the_Coral_Sea "Battle of the Coral Sea") established the carrier as the dominant capital ship (in place of the battleship).\[[434]\](#cite\*note-EncWWII\*163-438 "#cite_note-EncWWII_163-438")\[[435]\](#cite_note-439 "#cite_note-439")\[[436]\](#cite_note-440 "#cite_note-440") In the Atlantic, [escort carriers](/wiki/Escort_carrier "Escort carrier") became a vital part of Allied convoys, increasing the effective protection radius and helping to close the [Mid-Atlantic gap](/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_gap "Mid-Atlantic gap").\[[437]\](#cite_note-441 "#cite_note-441") Carriers were also more economical than [battleships](/wiki/Battleship "Battleship") due to the relatively low cost of aircraft\[[438]\](#cite_note-442 "#cite_note-442") and because they are not required to be as heavily armoured.\[[439]\](#cite_note-443 "#cite_note-443") Submarines, which had proved to be an effective weapon during the [First World War](/wiki/World_War_I "World War I"),\[[440]\](#cite_note-Bur&Ryd_1995_15-444 "#cite_note-Bur&Ryd_1995_15-444") were expected by all combatants to be important in the second. The British focused development on [anti-submarine](/wiki/Anti-submarine_warfare "Anti-submarine warfare") [weaponry](/wiki/Anti-submarine_weapon "Anti-submarine weapon") and tactics, such as [sonar](/wiki/Sonar "Sonar") and convoys, while Germany focused on improving its offensive capability, with designs such as the [Type VII submarine](/wiki/Type_VII_submarine "Type VII submarine") and [wolfpack](</wiki/Wolfpack*(naval*tactic)> "Wolfpack (naval tactic)") tactics.\[[441]\](#cite_note-Bur&Ryd_1995_16-445 "#cite_note-Bur&Ryd_1995_16-445") Gradually, improving Allied technologies such as the [Leigh Light](/wiki/Leigh_Light "Leigh Light"), [Hedgehog](</wiki/Hedgehog*(weapon)> "Hedgehog (weapon)"), [Squid](</wiki/Squid*(weapon)> "Squid (weapon)"), and [homing torpedoes](/wiki/Mark_24_mine "Mark 24 mine") proved effective against German submarines.\[[442]\](#cite_note-446 "#cite_note-446")

[<img src='//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Trinity_device_readied.jpg/250px-Trinity_device_readied.jpg' alt='' title='' width='250' height='198' />](/wiki/File:Trinity_device_readied.jpg "/wiki/File:Trinity_device_readied.jpg")

Nuclear _Gadget_ being raised to the top of the detonation "shot tower", at [Alamogordo Bombing Range](/wiki/Alamogordo_Bombing_and_Gunnery_Range "Alamogordo Bombing and Gunnery Range"); [Trinity nuclear test](</wiki/Trinity_(nuclear_test)> "Trinity (nuclear test)"), [New Mexico](/wiki/New_Mexico "New Mexico"), July 1945

[Land warfare](/wiki/Land_warfare "Land warfare") changed from the static frontlines of [trench warfare](/wiki/Trench_warfare "Trench warfare") of World War I, which had relied on improved [artillery](/wiki/Artillery "Artillery") that outmatched the speed of both [infantry](/wiki/Infantry "Infantry") and [cavalry](/wiki/Cavalry "Cavalry"), to increased mobility and [combined arms](/wiki/Combined_arms "Combined arms"). The [tank](/wiki/Tank "Tank"), which had been used predominantly for infantry support in the First World War, had evolved into the primary weapon.\[[443]\](#cite_note-EncWWII_125-447 "#cite_note-EncWWII_125-447") In the late 1930s, tank design was considerably more advanced than it had been during World War I,\[[444]\](#cite_note-448 "#cite_note-448") and [advances continued throughout the war](/wiki/Tanks_in_World_War_II "Tanks in World War II") with increases in speed, armour and firepower.\[[445]\](#cite_note-449 "#cite_note-449")\[[446]\](#cite_note-450 "#cite_note-450") At the start of the war, most commanders thought enemy tanks should be met by tanks with superior specifications.\[[447]\](#cite_note-EncWWII_108-451 "#cite_note-EncWWII_108-451") This idea was challenged by the poor performance of the relatively light early tank guns against armour, and German doctrine of avoiding tank-versus-tank combat. This, along with Germany's use of combined arms, were among the key elements of their highly successful blitzkrieg tactics across Poland and France.\[[443]\](#cite_note-EncWWII_125-447 "#cite_note-EncWWII_125-447") Many means of [destroying tanks](/wiki/Anti-tank_warfare "Anti-tank warfare"), including [indirect artillery](/wiki/Indirect_fire "Indirect fire"), [anti-tank guns](/wiki/Anti-tank_gun "Anti-tank gun") (both towed and [self-propelled](/wiki/Self-propelled_artillery "Self-propelled artillery")), [mines](/wiki/Anti-tank_mine "Anti-tank mine"), short-ranged infantry antitank weapons, and other tanks were used.\[[447]\](#cite_note-EncWWII_108-451 "#cite_note-EncWWII_108-451") Even with large-scale mechanisation, infantry remained the backbone of all forces,\[[448]\](#cite_note-EncWWII_734-452 "#cite_note-EncWWII_734-452") and throughout the war, most infantry were equipped similarly to World War I.\[[449]\](#cite_note-Comp_221-453 "#cite_note-Comp_221-453") The portable machine gun spread, a notable example being the German [MG 34](/wiki/MG_34 "MG 34"), and various [submachine guns](/wiki/Submachine_gun "Submachine gun") which were suited to [close combat](/wiki/Close_combat "Close combat") in urban and jungle settings.\[[449]\](#cite_note-Comp_221-453 "#cite_note-Comp_221-453") The [assault rifle](/wiki/Assault_rifle "Assault rifle"), a late war development incorporating many features of the rifle and submachine gun, became the standard post-war infantry weapon for most armed forces.\[[450]\](#cite_note-454 "#cite_note-454")

Most major belligerents attempted to solve the problems of complexity and security involved in using large [codebooks](/wiki/Codebook "Codebook") for [cryptography](/wiki/Cryptography "Cryptography") by designing [ciphering](/wiki/Cipher "Cipher") machines, the most well-known being the German [Enigma machine](/wiki/Enigma_machine "Enigma machine").\[[451]\](#cite\*note-455 "#cite\*note-455") Development of [SIGINT](/wiki/SIGINT "SIGINT") (*sig*nals *int*elligence) and [cryptanalysis](/wiki/Cryptanalysis "Cryptanalysis") enabled the countering process of decryption. Notable examples were the Allied decryption of [Japanese naval codes](/wiki/Japanese_naval_codes "Japanese naval codes")\[[452]\](#cite_note-Schoenherr-456 "#cite_note-Schoenherr-456") and British [Ultra](</wiki/Ultra*(cryptography)> "Ultra (cryptography)"), a [pioneering method](/wiki/Bombe#The_British_Bombe "Bombe") for decoding Enigma that benefited from information given to the United Kingdom by the [Polish Cipher Bureau](</wiki/Cipher_Bureau*(Poland)#Gift_to_allies> "Cipher Bureau (Poland)"), which had been decoding early versions of Enigma before the war.\[[453]\](#cite_note-457 "#cite_note-457") Another component of [military intelligence](/wiki/Military_intelligence "Military intelligence") was [deception](/wiki/Deception "Deception"), which the Allies used to great effect in operations such as [Mincemeat](/wiki/Operation_Mincemeat "Operation Mincemeat") and [Bodyguard](/wiki/Operation_Bodyguard "Operation Bodyguard").\[[452]\](#cite_note-Schoenherr-456 "#cite_note-Schoenherr-456")\[[454]\](#cite_note-458 "#cite_note-458")

Other technological and engineering feats achieved during, or as a result of, the war include the world's first programmable computers ([Z3](</wiki/Z3_(computer)> "Z3 (computer)"), [Colossus](/wiki/Colossus_computer "Colossus computer"), and [ENIAC](/wiki/ENIAC "ENIAC")), [guided missiles](/wiki/V-1_flying_bomb "V-1 flying bomb") and [modern rockets](/wiki/V-2_rocket "V-2 rocket"), the [Manhattan Project](/wiki/Manhattan_Project "Manhattan Project")'s development of [nuclear weapons](/wiki/Nuclear_weapon "Nuclear weapon"), [operations research](/wiki/Operations_research "Operations research"), the development of [artificial harbours](/wiki/Mulberry_harbour "Mulberry harbour"), and [oil pipelines under the English Channel](/wiki/Operation_Pluto "Operation Pluto").\[[455]\](#cite_note-459 "#cite_note-459") [Penicillin](/wiki/Penicillin "Penicillin") was first [developed, mass-produced, and used](/wiki/History_of_penicillin "History of penicillin") during the war.\[[456]\](#cite_note-460 "#cite_note-460")

## See also

- [Opposition to World War II](/wiki/Opposition_to_World_War_II "Opposition to World War II")
- [World War III](/wiki/World_War_III "World War III")

## Notes

1. **[^](#cite_ref-1 "#cite_ref-1")** While [various other dates](#Start_and_end_dates "#Start_and_end_dates") have been proposed as the date on which World War II began or ended, this is the period most frequently cited.
1. **[^](#cite_ref-2 "#cite_ref-2")** Often abbreviated as **WWII** or **WW2**
1. **[^](#cite_ref-71 "#cite_ref-71")** [The UK declared war on Germany](</wiki/United_Kingdom_declaration_of_war_on_Germany_(1939)> "United Kingdom declaration of war on Germany (1939)") at 11 am. [France followed 6 hours later](</wiki/French_declaration_of_war_on_Germany_(1939)> "French declaration of war on Germany (1939)") at 5 pm.
1. **[^](#cite_ref-363 "#cite_ref-363")** Reparations were exacted from [East Germany](/wiki/East_Germany "East Germany"), [Hungary](/wiki/Hungarian_People%27s_Republic "Hungarian People's Republic"), [Romania](/wiki/Romanian_People%27s_Republic "Romanian People's Republic"), and [Bulgaria](/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Bulgaria "People's Republic of Bulgaria") using Soviet-dominated joint enterprises. The Soviet Union also instituted trading arrangements deliberately designed to favour the country. Moscow controlled the Communist parties that ruled the satellite states, and they followed orders from the Kremlin. Historian Mark Kramer concludes: "The net outflow of resources from eastern Europe to the Soviet Union was approximately $15 billion to $20 billion in the first decade after World War II, an amount roughly equal to the total aid provided by the United States to western Europe under the [Marshall Plan](/wiki/Marshall_Plan "Marshall Plan")."

   [Cienciala 2010](#CITEREFCienciala2010 "#CITEREFCienciala2010"), p. 128, observes that, while it is true that Poland was far away, making it difficult for the French and British to provide support, "[f]ew Western historians of World War II ... know that the British had committed to bomb Germany if it attacked Poland, but did not do so except for one raid on the base of Wilhelmshaven. The French, who committed to attacking Germany in the west, had no intention of doing so."

1. **[^](#cite_ref-186 "#cite_ref-186")** [Dower 1986](#CITEREFDower1986 "#CITEREFDower1986"), p. 5, calls attention to the fact that "the Allied struggle against Japan exposed the racist underpinnings of the European and American colonial structure. Japan did not invade independent countries in southern Asia. It invaded colonial outposts which the Westerners had dominated for generations, taking absolutely for granted their racial and cultural superiority over their Asian subjects." Dower goes on to note that, before the horrors of Japanese occupation made themselves felt, many Asians responded favourably to the victories of the Imperial Japanese forces.

1. **[^](#cite_ref-Chubarov_2001_122_266-0 "#cite_ref-Chubarov_2001_122_266-0")** [Chubarov 2001](#CITEREFChubarov2001 "#CITEREFChubarov2001"), p. 122.
1. **[^](#cite_ref-267 "#cite_ref-267")** [Holland 2008](#CITEREFHolland2008 "#CITEREFHolland2008"), pp. 169–184; [Beevor 2012](#CITEREFBeevor2012 "#CITEREFBeevor2012"), pp. 568–573.
   The weeks after the fall of Rome saw a dramatic upswing in German atrocities in Italy ([Mazower 2008](#CITEREFMazower2008 "#CITEREFMazower2008"), pp. 500–502). The period featured massacres with victims in the hundreds at [Civitella](/wiki/Civitella_in_Val_di_Chiana "Civitella in Val di Chiana") ([de Grazia & Paggi 1991](#CITEREFde_GraziaPaggi1991 "#CITEREFde_GraziaPaggi1991"); [Belco 2010](#CITEREFBelco2010 "#CITEREFBelco2010")), [Fosse Ardeatine](/wiki/Ardeatine_massacre "Ardeatine massacre") ([Portelli 2003](#CITEREFPortelli2003 "#CITEREFPortelli2003")), and [Sant'Anna di Stazzema](/wiki/Sant%27Anna_di_Stazzema_massacre "Sant'Anna di Stazzema massacre") ([Gordon 2012](#CITEREFGordon2012 "#CITEREFGordon2012"), pp. 10–11), and is capped with the [Marzabotto massacre](/wiki/Marzabotto_massacre "Marzabotto massacre").

1. **[^](#cite_ref-countrystudies.us_281-0 "#cite_ref-countrystudies.us_281-0")** ["Armistice Negotiations and Soviet Occupation"](https://countrystudies.us/romania/23.htm "https://countrystudies.us/romania/23.htm"). US Library of Congress. [Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20110430001849/https://countrystudies.us/romania/23.htm "https://web.archive.org/web/20110430001849/https://countrystudies.us/romania/23.htm") from the original on 30 April 2011. Retrieved 14 November 2009. The coup speeded the Red Army's advance, and the Soviet Union later awarded Michael the Order of Victory for his courage in overthrowing Antonescu and putting an end to Romania's war against the Allies. Western historians uniformly point out that the Communists played only a supporting role in the coup; postwar Romanian historians, however, ascribe to the Communists the decisive role in Antonescu's overthrow

1. **[^](#cite_ref-Pape_1993_314-0 "#cite_ref-Pape_1993_314-0")** [Pape 1993](#CITEREFPape1993 "#CITEREFPape1993") " The principal cause of Japan's surrender was the ability of the United States to increase the military vulnerability of Japan's home islands, persuading Japanese leaders that defense of the homeland was highly unlikely to succeed. The key military factor causing this effect was the sea blockade, which crippled Japan's ability to produce and equip the forces necessary to execute its strategy. The most important factor accounting for the timing of surrender was the Soviet attack against Manchuria, largely because it persuaded previously adamant Army leaders that the homeland could not be defended.".
